Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
15 min
Allocating Destroyed Camels in Zakat: The Three Hanafi Positions
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on allocating losses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam Abu Hanifa's method of allocating destroyed camels to 'afw and nisab sequentially, and compare it with the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Destroyed animals are allocated first to 'afw (subordinate), then to nisab, preserving the nisab threshold.

When some camels in a zakat herd are destroyed after the year ends, how do we determine the remaining zakat obligation? The Hanafi school has three views, all rooted in the concept of 'afw (the surplus between nisabs). This lesson unpacks the rational proof (qiyas with mudarabah) and the differing conclusions of the three leading imams.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of 'afw
Identify that 'afw is the surplus between two nisab amounts (e.g., camels 6-9) on which no zakat is due. It is subordinate to the nisab.
The hadith about zakat on 5 and 10 camels establishes this.
2
Grasp the qiyas with mudarabah
In mudarabah, losses are first applied to profit (subordinate) not capital (original). Similarly, destroyed camels are first allocated to 'afw (subordinate) rather than the nisab itself.
This is the 'illa: property consists of original (nisab) and subordinate ('afw).
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's sequential method
Apply destruction first to 'afw, then to the last nisab, then to the adjacent nisab. Example: 40 camels, 20 destroyed → allocate 4 to 'afw (37-40), then 11 to the last nisab (26-36? Actually up to 25), then remaining to adjacent nisab until 20 remain → zakat = 4 goats.
Result: 20 camels remain, zakat = 4 goats (for 20-24 camels).
4
Examine Imam Abu Yusuf's proportional method
After allocating 4 to 'afw, the remaining 16 are spread proportionally over the 36-camel nisab. Thus 16/36 of the bint labun is waived.
Result: 20/36 of a bint labun is due.
5
Examine Imam Muhammad's half-and-half method
Zakat relates to both nisab and 'afw, so half the herd destroyed = half the zakat waived. Result: half a bint labun.
This view treats 'afw as having some zakat relevance.

Book of Zakat. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Three. From this hadith it is clearly apparent that on five camels and ten camels which are the nisab, zakat is obligatory. And on the four camels between five and ten, which are called 'afw, zakat is not obligatory. Similarly, in every nisab, obligation is negated for the 'afw. From this it is understood that zakat is related to the nisab, not to the 'afw. Subordinate to [the nisab]. The rational proof is that 'afw, since it is established only after the existence of the nisab, therefore 'afw will be subordinate to the nisab. And where wealth consists of an original and an increase, and then some of it is destroyed, the destroyed wealth is turned toward the subordinate, not toward the original. That is, it will be said that what was destroyed was the wealth that is subordinate, not the wealth that is original. Just as in mudarabah wealth, profit is ... (continues with the example). For this reason Imam Abu Hanifa said that whatever amount was destroyed, after the 'afw, it will be turned toward the last nisab. That is, if the destroyed amount does not suffice for the 'afw, then it will be placed on the last nisab. If that also does not suffice, then on the nisab adjacent to it, because the original is the first nisab and whatever is in addition is all subordinate. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, first it is turned toward the 'afw. If that does not suffice, then it is turned toward the entire nisab on a proportional basis. An example: a person has 40 camels. After a year, 20 camels are destroyed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, on the remaining 20 camels, four goats are obligatory. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, twenty parts out of thirty-six parts of a bint labun are obligatory. According to Imam Muhammad, half the value of a bint labun is obligatory. The reason for Imam Muhammad's view is that zakat is related to both the nisab and the 'afw. When half the wealth, i.e., 20 out of 40 camels, were destroyed, then half the zakat is waived. The reason for Imam Abu Yusuf's view is that after 36, four are 'afw, i.e., out of the destroyed 20 camels, four are allocated to 'afw. So it will be said that four camels of 'afw were destroyed, which have no connection with zakat. Therefore, due to the destruction of these four, no portion of zakat is waived. The remaining sixteen are placed on the entire nisab. That is, it will be said that on 36 camels, one bint labun is obligatory. But when sixteen camels were destroyed, sixteen out of thirty-six parts of the bint labun are waived, and twenty parts remain. For example, if the value of a bint labun is 36 silver rupees, then 1600 rupees are waived and 2000 rupees remain. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, out of the destroyed 20 camels, four are allocated to 'afw, i.e., it will be said that four camels of 'afw (37-40) were destroyed. Then the destroyed animals are turned toward the last nisab. That is, it will be said that up to 25, eleven camels were destroyed. But since the destroyed animals are not complete, they are turned toward the nisab adjacent to the last nisab, i.e., it will be said that from after 20 to 25 were destroyed. Now the destroyed camels are complete. Now 20 camels remain, so on them four goats are obligatory, because on 20 camels four goats are obligatory.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning how to allocate the destruction of some camels after the zakat year has passed, when the total herd was 40 camels and 20 are destroyed. The key concept is 'afw (surplus between nisabs) and its subsidiary status. The author first establishes from hadith that zakat is only on the nisab numbers (5, 10, etc.) and not on the intervening 'afw. Then a rational proof is given: 'afw is subordinate to nisab because it exists only after the nisab is complete. By analogy with mudarabah losses being first applied to profit (the subordinate), the destruction is applied to the subordinate portion first. Imam Abu Hanifa applies the destruction first to the 'afw (camels 37-40), then to the last nisab (25), then to the adjacent nisab (20-25), resulting in 20 camels remaining, on which zakat is 4 goats (for 20-24 camels, zakat is 4 goats per the zakat schedule). Imam Abu Yusuf first allocates destruction to the 'afw (4 camels), then proportionally to the entire 36 camel nisab, so 16/36 of a bint labun is waived, leaving 20/36. Imam Muhammad holds that zakat relates to both nisab and 'afw, so half the herd destroyed means half the zakat is waived (i.e., half a bint labun). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is not stated here, but later Hanafi works typically adopt Imam Abu Hanifa's view as the basis.

Key Terms
عفو ('afw): The surplus number of camels between two nisab amounts on which zakat is not obligatory (e.g., camels 6-9 between nisabs of 5 and 10).
نصاب (nisab): The minimum quantity of wealth that triggers zakat obligation (e.g., 5 camels, 40 goats, 200 dirhams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 20 goats
C) 1 bint labun
D) Half a bint labun

Key Takeaway
When some camels are destroyed, allocate losses first to 'afw (the exempt surplus), then sequentially to the nisab layers, following Imam Abu Hanifa's relied-upon method.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Ruling on Zakat and Kharaj Taken by Khawarij
States ruling and reasons when Khawarij forcibly take zakat and kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when Khawarij forcibly take zakat and kharaj, and explain the reasoning based on the principle of protection and recipient eligibility.

Core Idea
Zakat taken by Khawarij must be re-given to the poor; kharaj need not, because Khawarij are fighters who are valid recipients of kharaj.

When rebels (Khawarij) forcibly collect zakat and land tax (kharaj) from Muslims, the obligation of the owner is not automatically discharged. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on whether the owner must pay again, focusing on the nature of each levy and the eligibility of the Khawarij as recipients. The key principle is that collection is based on protection, and the recipient classes differ for zakat and kharaj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of payments
Distinguish between zakat on grazing animals and kharaj (land tax). Zakat is a compulsory charity for the poor; kharaj is a state tax for public expenditure, including fighters.
Kharaj recipients include those who fight for the state, which the Khawarij are doing (though illegitimately).
2
Apply the principle 'al-jibayah bi al-himayah'
Understand that the just imam cannot collect taxes from the people again because he failed to protect them from the Khawarij. Taxation is premised on protection.
This is a legal maxim: collection is by protection.
3
Determine recipient eligibility
Analyze that Khawarij are fighters (muqatilah), so they are legitimate recipients of kharaj. However, zakat must be given to the poor, and the Khawarij will not spend it on the poor, so the owner must re-give zakat to the eligible poor.
The owner re-gives zakat as an act between himself and Allah, not to the imam.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi alternative
Consider the second opinion: if the owner intended the payment to the Khawarij as sadaqah (charity), then the zakat obligation is discharged. This applies to any oppressive taker, as they are considered poor due to their sins.
The first view (re-give) is more precautionary (ahwat) and is the mufta bihi.

Source Text

وَإِذَا اَخَذَ الْخَوَارِجُ الْخَرَاجَ وَصَدَقَةَ السَّوَائِم لاَ يُؤْخَذُ عَلَيْهِمْ لأَنَّ الاِمَامَ لَمْ يَحْمِهِمْ وَالْجِبَايَةُ بِالْحِمَايَةِ وَافْتُوا بِأَنَّهُمْ يُعِيدُوهَا دُونَ الْخَرَاجَ فِيْمَا بَيْنَهُمْ وَ بَيْنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِأَنَّهُمْ مَصَارِفَ الْخَرَاجِ لِكُوْنِهِم مُقَاتِلَةً وَالزَّكوةُ مَصْرَفُهَا الْفُقَرَاءُ فَلا يَصْرِفُونَهَا إِلَيْهِمْ وَقِيلَ إِذَا نَوَى بِالدَّفْعِ التَّصَدَّقْ عَلَيْهِم سَقَطَ عَنْهُ وَكَذَا مَا دَفَعَ إِلَى كُلِّ جَائِرٍ لأَنَّهُمْ بِمَا عَلَيْهِمْ مِنَ التَّبِعَاتِ فُقَرَاءُ وَالأَوَّلُ أَحْوَطُ
ترجمہ اور اگر خارجیوں نے خراج کو اور سائمہ جانوروں کی زکوۃ کو وصول کر لیا تو لوگوں سے دوبارہ نہ لی جائے گی کیونکہ امام نے لوگوں کی حفاظت نہیں کی ہے اور محصول تو حمایت پر ہے۔ اور لوگوں کو فتویٰ دیا جائے گا کہ وہ زکوۃ دوبارہ (فقیروں کو ) دیدیں۔ خراج دوبارہ نہ دیں۔ ( یہ دوبارہ زکوۃ دینا ) ان کے اور اللہ کے درمیان ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خوارج خراج کا مصرف ہیں ۔ کیونکہ خوارج بھی لڑنے والوں میں ہیں اور زکوۃ کا مصرف فقراء ہیں اور خوارج اس کو فقیروں میں خرچ نہ کریں گے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ جب مالک مال نے خارجیوں کو دیتے وقت ان کو صدقہ دینے کی نیت کی تو مالک سے زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور ایسے ہی ہر اس مال کے دینے میں جو کسی ظالم کو دینا پڑے کیونکہ یہ لوگ ان مظالم کی وجہ سے جو ان کے پیچھے لگے ہوئے ہیں فقیر ہیں۔ اور قول اول میں زیادہ احتیاط ہے۔
And when the Khawarij take the kharaj and the zakat of grazing animals, it will not be taken again from the people because the imam did not protect them, and collection is by protection. And they are given a fatwa that they should repay it (the zakat) without the kharaj, between themselves and Allah the Exalted, because the Khawarij are the recipients of kharaj due to their being fighters, and the recipient of zakat is the poor, so they (the Khawarij) will not spend it on the poor. And it was said: when (the owner) intended by payment to give charity to them, it is waived from him. And similarly, whatever is paid to any oppressor, because they, due to the obligations upon them, are poor. And the first is more precautionary.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the situation where Khawarij (rebel Muslims who reject the just imam) forcefully collect kharaj (land tax) and zakat on grazing animals from the people. The ruling is that the people will not be required to pay these amounts again to the just imam who later gains control, because the previous imam failed to protect them—and taxation is based on protection. However, they are given a fatwa to re-give the zakat to the poor in secret, as an act between them and Allah, because the Khawarij are not valid recipients of zakat (zakat is only for the poor). In contrast, they do not re-give the kharaj because the Khawarij are fighters, and fighters are legitimate recipients of kharaj (as it is a tax for military purposes). There is a second opinion: if the owner intended the payment to the Khawarij as sadaqah (charity), then the zakat obligation is discharged, and the same applies to payments made to any oppressor, because the oppressors themselves are poor due to their sins. The first opinion (that zakat must be re-given) is considered more precautionary (ahwat). The passage also provides a background on the Khawarij sect, but that is not part of the ruling itself.

Key Terms
خوارج (Khawarij): A group of Muslims who rebel against the just imam, declaring him and his followers as disbelievers due to major sins, and who consider it lawful to kill them and take their property.
خراج (kharaj): A land tax levied on non-Muslims (or sometimes generally) for the use of land, collected by the imam; its recipients include fighters (mujahidin).
صدقہ (sadaqah): Voluntary charity; in this context, if the owner intended the payment to the Khawarij as sadaqah, it may suffice for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first (ahwat) ruling in the passage, if Khawarij forcibly take zakat on grazing animals, what must the owner do?
A) The owner must re-give the zakat to the poor.
B) The owner does not need to do anything; the zakat is discharged.
C) The owner must re-give both zakat and kharaj.
D) The owner must give the kharaj again but not the zakat.

Key Takeaway
Zakat forcibly taken by Khawarij must be re-given to the poor because the Khawarij are ineligible recipients; kharaj is not re-given because they are fighters and valid recipients.

Ruling When Khawarij Forcibly Collect Kharaj and Zakat
Ruling on forcibly collected taxes from Khawarij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when Khawarij forcibly collect kharaj and zakat, distinguish between the two taxes, and explain the intra-madhhab difference regarding intention.

Core Idea
Zakat taken by force from Khawarij must be re-given to the poor; kharaj is not re-collected.

What happens when a group of rebels (Khawarij) takes over a region and forcibly collects the land tax (kharaj) from non-Muslims and the zakat on livestock from Muslims? Does the legitimate imam collect again? This passage from al-Hidayah addresses the scenario, distinguishing between the two taxes based on the principle that taxation is based on protection (jibayah bi'l-himayah). It also presents an important intra-Hanafi difference on whether a Muslim's zakat obligation is discharged if he intended to give charity to the Khawarij.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the opening: 'When the Khawarij take the kharaj and the zakat of grazing livestock.' This is a situation where an illegitimate group rebels against the imam and forcibly collects these taxes.
The Khawarij are considered rebellious Muslims (baghi), not non-Muslims.
2
Understand the ruling for re-collection by the imam
The text says 'they will not be approached (again) because the imam did not protect them.' The imam cannot re-collect from the people because he failed to protect them from the Khawarij. The legal maxim 'taxation is based on protection' (al-jibayah bi'l-himayah) is invoked.
This applies equally to kharaj and zakat as far as state re-collection is concerned.
3
Differentiate between zakat and kharaj for religious re-giving
The people are advised (given a fatwa) to repeat the zakat between themselves and Allah, but not the kharaj. Why? Because the Khawarij are eligible recipients of kharaj (they are fighters, and kharaj funds military efforts), but zakat must reach the poor, and the Khawarij will not spend it on the poor.
The ruling for kharaj is that it is considered discharged, while zakat is not.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
A second opinion (from Faqih Abu Ja'far) states that if the owner intended to give charity to the Khawarij when paying, the obligation is fulfilled. The reasoning: oppressors are 'poor' due to the burdens (debts) they incur from their oppression. However, the majority and the author of al-Hidayah prefer the first opinion as more cautious (ahwat).
This shows the school's commitment to ensuring zakat reaches the truly deserving.
5
State the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The preferred fatwa is the first opinion: a Muslim must re-give the zakat to the poor, even after having paid the Khawarij by force. The kharaj is not re-given. Intention does not change the ruling in the preferred view.
This is based on the principle of caution (ihtiyat) in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اَخَذَ الْخَوَارِجُ الْخَرَاجَ وَصَدَقَةَ السَّوَائِم لَا يُتَى عَلَيْهِمُ لأنَّ الاِمَامَ لَمْ يَحْمِهِمُ وَالْجِبَايَةُ بِالْحِمَايَةِ وَافْتُوابانُ يُعِيدُوهَا دُونَ الْخَرَاجَ فِيْمَا بَيْنَهُمْ وَ بَيْنَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى لِأَنَّهُمْ مَصَارِفَ الْخَرَاجَ لِكُوْنِهِم مُقَاتِلَةً وَالزَّكوةُ مَصْرَفُهَا الْفُقَرَاءُ فَلا يَصْرِفُونَهَا إِلَيْهِمُ وَقِيلَ إِذَا نَوَى بِالدَّفْعِ التَّصَدَّقْ عَلَيْهِم سَقَطَ عَنْهُ وَكَذَا مَا دَفَعَ إِلَى كُلِّ جَائِرٍ لأَنَّهُمْ بِمَا عَلَيْهِمْ مِنَ التَّبِعَاتِ فُقَرَاءُ وَالأَوَّلُ أَحْوَطُ
And when the Khawarij take the kharaj and the zakat of grazing livestock, they (the people) will not be approached (again) because the imam did not protect them, and taxation is based on protection. And they are given the fatwa to repeat it (the zakat) without the kharaj, between themselves and Allah the Exalted, because they (the Khawarij) are recipients of the kharaj for being fighters, and the zakat's recipients are the poor, so they do not spend it to them. And it is said: if he intended by paying to give charity to them, it falls from him, and likewise what he pays to every oppressor because they, due to the obligations upon them, are poor. And the first is more cautious.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah discusses the situation where Kharijite rebels forcibly collect the kharaj (land tax) from non-Muslims and the zakat on grazing livestock from Muslims. The ruling: the imam cannot re-collect these taxes from the people because he failed to protect them, and tax is contingent on protection (jibayah bi'l-himayah). However, the people are advised religiously (between themselves and Allah) to re-give the zakat to the poor, but not the kharaj. The reason: the Khawarij are eligible recipients of kharaj because they participate in fighting (as Muslims, albeit rebels), so that tax is considered discharged. But zakat must reach the poor, and the Khawarij will not spend it on the poor (since they consider killing opponents permissible). The second opinion from Faqih Abu Ja'far says if the owner intended zakat when paying the Khawarij, it suffices, because the oppressors are effectively poor due to the debts they owe from oppression. The author prefers the first (more cautious) view, as it ensures certainty that zakat reaches the deserving.

Key Terms
خوارج (Khawarij): Rebellious Muslim group that revolted against the legitimate imam and consider opponents as disbelievers.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax levied on non-Muslims (or conquered land) in exchange for protection.
صدقة السوائم (sadaqat al-sawa'im): Zakat obligatory on grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep/goats) that are free-range.
جِبَايَة بالحِمَايَة (jibayah bi'l-himayah): The legal principle that taxation (collection) is contingent on protection. If the imam fails to protect the people from an oppressor, he cannot re-collect taxes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what must a Muslim do if Khawarij forcibly take zakat on his livestock but do not distribute it to the poor?
A) Nothing, because the collection by any authority discharges the obligation.
B) Re-give the zakat to the poor himself, as a matter of religious duty.
C) Re-give both the zakat and the kharaj to the imam.
D) Only re-give the kharaj to the poor.

Key Takeaway
When zakat is forcibly taken by an oppressor who will not give it to the poor, the payer must re-give the zakat to the poor; kharaj is not re-given.

Zakat on Livestock of Banu Taghlib's Children and Women
Clarifies zakat liability for Banu Taghlib minors and women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat liability for Banu Taghlib minors and women, and explain the basis in the treaty.

Core Idea
A minor of Banu Taghlib pays no zakat on livestock; a woman pays double the Muslim rate.

This lesson explains the special zakat rules for the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib, based on their historic peace treaty. You will learn why minors are exempt and women are liable, mirroring Muslim rules but at double the rate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject groups
The passage names two groups: the minor (الصبي) and the woman (المرأة) of Banu Taghlib. Recognize that 'minor' means a child not yet legally responsible (mukallaf).
2
State the ruling for each
For the minor: 'nothing upon him' (لا شيء عليه). For the woman: same as the man (على المرأة ما على الرجل), meaning she is liable.
3
Identify the basis: the treaty
The ruling is derived from the peace treaty (الصُلح) which set the obligation at double the Muslim rate (ضعف ما يؤخذ من المسلمين).
4
Understand the analogy to Muslims
The treaty follows Muslim practice: zakat is taken from Muslim women (if they own the nisab) but not from their children. Hence Banu Taghlib minors are exempt, women are liable.
5
Note the rate: double
Banu Taghlib women pay twice the zakat that a Muslim woman would pay on the same livestock. This is due to the treaty condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الصَّبِي مِنْ بَنِي تَغْلِبَ فِي سَائِمَتِهِ شَيْءٌ ، وَعَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ مَا عَلَى الرَّجُلِ مِنْهُمْ ، لِأَنَّ الصُّلْحَ قَدْ جَرَى عَلَى ضِعْفِ مَا يُوجَدُ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ ، وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْ نِسَاءِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ دُونَ صِبْيَانِهِمْ.
And there is nothing upon the minor of Banu Taghlib concerning his grazing livestock, and upon the woman is what is upon the man among them, because the peace treaty proceeded upon double of what is taken from the Muslims, and it is taken from the women of the Muslims instead of their children.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on zakat for the Christian tribe Banu Taghlib, who had a special peace treaty with the caliph Umar to pay double the jizya that Muslims pay as zakat. The rule: a minor child (even if he owns grazing livestock) is not required to pay anything, because among Muslims, minors are exempt from zakat. Women, however, are liable just like the men of Banu Taghlib, because Muslim women are also liable for zakat on livestock (if they own the nisab). The amount for Banu Taghlib is double the Muslim rate. So the women pay double the zakat that Muslim women would pay. The treaty is based on the Muslim rule, so liability parallels Muslim liability except for the doubling.

Key Terms
بني تغلب (Banu Taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe from northern Arabia that made a peace treaty with Caliph Umar to pay double the jizya instead of zakat.
سائمته (sa'imatahu): His grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep/goats) that are free-range and subject to zakat.
ضعف (di'f): Double the amount; i.e., twice the zakat rate that Muslims pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the child's livestock is considered part of the father's wealth.
D) Because Banu Taghlib only pay on women's property.

Key Takeaway
Banu Taghlib minors are exempt from zakat on livestock; women are liable at double the Muslim rate, mirroring Muslim rules.

Zakat and Kharaj Under Khawarij Rule
Explains when zakat and kharaj are due under Khawarij rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat and kharaj when Khawarij seize control and explain the reason for the difference between the two obligations.

Core Idea
Kharaj drops when protection fails; zakat requires correct recipient – intention may or may not suffice.

This lesson examines a complex scenario where Khawarij (Muslim rebels) have taken over a region. The question arises: are the residents still obliged to pay kharaj (land tax) and zakat to the Khawarij, and if so, are these payments valid? The Hanafi jurists provide a nuanced answer rooted in the purposes of each obligation: kharaj is a payment for protection, while zakat must reach the poor. The passage also presents an internal Hanafi dispute on whether intention can salvage an otherwise invalid zakat payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two obligations and their purposes
First, recall that kharaj is a land tax taken in exchange for military protection by the Muslim state. Zakat is a mandatory charity for the poor. The passage contrasts their purposes.
Kharaj's purpose is defensive; zakat's is redistributive.
2
Apply the principle for kharaj
If the just imam cannot protect the people from Khawarij, then kharaj is no longer obligatory. This is supported by a decree from Umar (RA).
The ruling is conditional: no protection → no tax.
3
Analyze the zakat ruling
Zakat paid to Khawarij is not discharged because the Khawarij will not spend it on the rightful poor (they consider killing Ahl al-Adl permissible). Hence, the payer must repeat the zakat.
The recipient's eligibility is critical.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Faqih Abu Ja'far argues that if the payer intended zakat when giving to the Khawarij (or any oppressor), the obligation is discharged. He analogizes that oppressors are effectively poor due to their debts.
The author of Hidayah cautions that the first opinion (repeating) is safer, while the second offers ease.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The cautious position (repeat zakat) is preferred for certainty, though the ruling acknowledges the validity of the dissenting view.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of preferring certainty in ibadat.

Source Text

دار الاسلام پر چڑھائی کر دیں تو خوارج بھی اہل عدل مسلمانو کے شانہ بشانہ کفار کو دار الاسلام سے دفع کرنے کے لئے قتال کرتے ہیں۔ پس جب خوارج بھی کفار کے مقابلہ میں قتال کرتے ہیں تو وہ بھی خراج کا مصرف ہوئے ۔ کیونکہ خراج کا مصرف وہی لوگ ہوتے ہیں جو ملک کو کفار کے حملہ سے محفوظ رھیں ۔ اور حملہ کرنے والوں سے لڑیں پس جب خوارج کا مصرف خراج ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو خراج دوبارہ ادا کرنے کا فتویٰ نہیں دیا جائے ہے اس سے ان ظالموں کو بھی زکوۃ دینے سے زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی۔ بشرطیکہ دیتے وقت زکوۃ کی نیت کی ہو ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ احتیاط قول اول میں ہے کیونکہ دوبارہ بذات خود فقراء کوز کو ۃ دینے سے زکوۃ بالیقین ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ لیکن آسانی قول ثانی میں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
ZA Book of Zakat Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Three. And the tax (kharaj) is obligatory because of protection. So when the just imam cannot protect from the Khawarij, then the tax is not obligatory upon them. That is, when the disbelievers agreed to submit, they are under our covenant and protection; protecting their life and property is a duty upon us for our own life and property. Then kharaj is taken from them for this reason: that from this kharaj the expenses of the army will be paid, which will protect their life and property from others. So when the just imam cannot save them from the domination of the Khawarij, then how can he be entitled to the kharaj? The decree of Sayyiduna Umar also supports this. The decree is that once Sayyiduna Umar wrote to one of his officials: 'If you cannot protect them, then do not take tax from them' meaning if you cannot protect them, then do not take tax from them. But the people there will be given the fatwa that they, as a matter of conscience between themselves and Allah, should give zakat again by themselves to the needy, and should not give kharaj again. The reason for the difference is that the Khawarij are recipients of kharaj. In this manner: that the Khawarij are not disbelievers but Muslims, however they are rebels. Now if the disbelievers attack Dar al-Islam, then the Khawarij also fight alongside the just Muslims to repel the disbelievers from Dar al-Islam. So when the Khawarij also fight against the disbelievers, they too become recipients of kharaj. Because the recipients of kharaj are those people who protect the country from the attack of disbelievers and fight against the attackers. So when the Khawarij's being recipients of kharaj is established, then a fatwa of paying kharaj again will not be given. As for the matter of zakat, the recipients of zakat are Muslim poor. And the Khawarij will not spend it on the poor because according to the Khawarij, killing the just (Ahl al-Adl) is permissible (mubah). So when according to them killing the just Muslims is permissible, how can these people spend the zakat wealth on the Muslim poor? The conclusion is that the zakat of the just Muslims was not spent in the correct recipient. And when it was not spent in the correct recipient, then a fatwa will be given to pay it again as a matter of conscience. Faqih Abu Ja'far said: If the owner, at the time of giving to the Khawarij, had the intention of paying zakat, then zakat will be discharged from him. Similarly, when giving to any oppressive powerful person, if he intends that he is giving zakat to this poor person, then zakat will be discharged from his liability. There is no need to pay zakat again. The proof of this statement is that due to the oppressors' oppression, so many obligatory rights of people are upon them that if these oppressors start paying off people's rights from their accumulated wealth, nothing would remain in their possession and they would become purely poor. Therefore, giving zakat to oppressors is like giving to the poor, and giving zakat to the poor discharges zakat. So from this, giving zakat to these oppressors will also discharge zakat, provided that at the time of giving, the intention of zakat was made. The author of Hidayah said: Caution is in the first opinion because by giving zakat again by oneself to the poor, zakat is definitely discharged. But ease is in the second opinion. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex scenario where Khawarij (rebels) have seized control of a region. The question is whether the Muslim residents must pay kharaj (land tax) and zakat to the Khawarij, and if their payments are valid. The ruling clarifies that kharaj is a tax in exchange for protection by the Muslim state. Since the just imam cannot provide protection due to Khawarij domination, kharaj is no longer obligatory. This is supported by a letter from Umar (RA). However, the residents are advised to pay zakat again directly to the poor because the Khawarij, though Muslim, will not spend zakat on the poor (as they consider killing Ahl al-Adl permissible). Hence the zakat paid to them was not discharged. The passage then presents an opinion by Faqih Abu Ja'far that if the payer intended zakat when giving to the Khawarij, the zakat is discharged. He analogizes that oppressors are practically poor because they owe so many debts. The author of Hidayah prefers caution (repeat zakat) over ease (accept intention). Learners should note the Hanafi principle that zakat must reach the rightful recipients; if it goes to those who will not distribute it properly, the obligation remains. The fatwa here is a practical guide for people under Khawarij control.

Key Terms
خوارج (Khawarij): A group of rebels who broke away from the Muslim community, considered Muslims but transgressors.
محصول (mahsul): Tax, here referring to both kharaj (land tax) and jizya (poll tax).
مصرف (masrif): The rightful recipients or category of expenditure for a particular fund.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kharaj not required to be paid again if it was taken by Khawarij?
A) Because Khawarij are disbelievers and cannot take kharaj.
B) Because Khawarij are legitimate recipients of kharaj as they fight against disbelievers.
C) Because the just imam never demanded it.
D) Because kharaj is only due when the imam asks.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is contingent on protection and is not repeated; zakat must reach the poor, so payment to Khawarij requires repetition unless intention is accepted per a minority Hanafi view.

Zakat on Grazing Animals of Banu Taghlib's Children and Women
Ruling on zakat for Banu Taghlib's children and women based on treaty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for minors and women of Banu Taghlib and explain how the treaty with Umar (RA) determines this ruling.

Core Idea
The treaty with Banu Taghlib mirrors Muslim zakat rules: minors exempt, women liable at double rate.

This lesson examines a unique historical treaty between Caliph Umar (RA) and the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib. Instead of jizya, they agreed to pay double the Muslim zakat rate. The ruling on zakat for their children and women is derived from this treaty by analogy to Muslim zakat obligations. We will explore the reasoning behind the exemption of minors and the liability of women, as well as a dissenting opinion within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the treaty
Banu Taghlib (Christian Arabs) made a treaty with Umar (RA) to pay double the zakat of Muslims instead of jizya. This treaty is the basis for all rulings on this community.
The treaty was approved by the Companions and upheld by Uthman (RA), making it binding.
2
Identify the base ruling for Muslims
Muslim minors are not subject to zakat on grazing animals (saimah); Muslim women are subject if they own nisab. This is the standard Hanafi ruling.
Zakat on saimah is wajib for adult Muslims who own nisab and have free-grazing livestock.
3
Apply the treaty analogy
The treaty states 'double of what is taken from Muslims.' Therefore, the categories of persons liable follow the Muslim pattern: minors exempt, women liable.
The treaty does not create a new rule; it mirrors the Muslim obligation with a doubling of the rate.
4
Derive the ruling for Banu Taghlib
Minors: nothing on their saimah. Women: same as men — double the Muslim zakat rate (5% instead of 2.5%). Note the dissent: Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates from Abu Hanifa that women are exempt.
The dissenting view treats the payment as jizya, which is not on women.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference and the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that women are liable, based on the explicit treaty wording and the practice of the Caliphs. The dissenting view is a weak (marjuh) narration.
The mufta bihi is consistent with the analogy to Muslim zakat.

پس اس پر صلح ہوگئی کہ ان سے مسلمانوں کی زکوۃ کا دو گنا لیا جائے گا۔ یعنی مسلمانوں سے ڈھائی فیصد لیا جاتا ہے تو ان سے پانچ فیصد لیا جائے گا۔ حضرت عمر کے بعد پھر حضرت عثمان نے بھی اس صلح سے کوئی تعرض نہیں کیا۔ اس لئے یہ صلح پوری امت کے لئے لازم ہو گئی ۔ اب مسئلہ یہ ہوا کہ بنو تغلب کے نابالغ بچوں کے سائمہ جانوروں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے ۔ البتہ ان کی عورتوں پر وہ واجب ہے جو ان کے مردوں پر واجب ہے کیونکہ بنو تغلب سے اس بات پر صلح ہوئی ہے کہ مسلمانوں سے جو لیا جاتا ہے تو تغلب سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا پس چونکہ مسلمان بچوں سے کچھ نہیں لیا جاتا۔ اس لئے ان کے بچوں سے بھی نہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ مسلمان عورتوں سے لیا جاتا ہے لہذا ان کی عورتوں سے بھی لیا جائے گا۔ لیکن ان کی عورتوں سے وہ لیا جائے گا جو ان کے مردوں سے لیا جاتا ہے۔ یعنی مسلمانوں پر جو واجب ہے اس کا دو چند اور حسن بن زیاد نے حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ بنو تغلب کی عورتوں سے بھی نہ لیا جائے گا۔ یہی امام شافعی اور امام زفر کا قول ہے کیونکہ یہ حقیقتا جزیہ ہے اور عورتوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہوتا۔
Ruling on zakat of the grazing animals of the child of Banu Taghlib, and ruling on zakat of the man and woman of Banu Taghlib. And there is nothing upon the child of Banu Taghlib regarding his grazing animals, and upon the woman is the same as upon the man from them, because the treaty was established on double of what is taken from the Muslims, and it is taken from the Muslim women but not from their children. Translation: And upon the minor child of Banu Taghlib there is nothing in his grazing animals. And upon the Taghlibi woman is that which is upon their men. Because the treaty (with them) was concluded on the basis that double of what is taken from the Muslims will be taken. And it is taken from Muslim women, not from their children. Explanation: Banu Taghlib is a Christian Arab tribe that lived near Rome. When Sayyiduna Umar (RA) intended to impose jizya on them, they refused and said: 'We too are Arabs; we are ashamed of jizya. If you impose jizya on us, we will flee to your enemies in Rome. If you take from us what is taken from Muslims, i.e., zakat, and double it, we are agreeable.' After consulting the Companions, Sayyiduna Umar made a treaty and said: 'This is jizya; name it whatever you wish.' So the treaty was established that double the zakat of Muslims would be taken from them. That is, 2.5% is taken from Muslims, so 5% will be taken from them. After Umar, Uthman (RA) did not interfere with this treaty, so it became binding on the entire ummah. Now the ruling is that zakat is not obligatory on the grazing animals of Banu Taghlib's minor children. However, upon their women, that is obligatory which is obligatory upon their men, because the treaty with Banu Taghlib is that from what is taken from Muslims, double is taken from Taghlib. Since nothing is taken from Muslim children, nothing will be taken from their children. And since it is taken from Muslim women, it will be taken from their women. But from their women, that amount will be taken which is taken from their men, i.e., double of what is obligatory on Muslims. And Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifah that nothing will be taken from the women of Banu Taghlib. This is also the saying of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, because it is essentially jizya, and jizya is not imposed on women.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage deals with the unique case of Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe that made a treaty with Caliph Umar (RA). Instead of jizya, they agreed to pay double the zakat rate of Muslims. The passage clarifies that the treaty follows the pattern of Muslim zakat obligations: since Muslim minors are not subject to zakat on grazing animals (saima), the children of Banu Taghlib are also exempt. Muslim women, however, are subject to zakat on grazing animals if they own nisab, so Banu Taghlib women are also subject. The treaty treats this payment as a land tax (jizya) in essence, but the ruling follows the analogy to Muslim zakat. There is a difference of opinion: Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates from Abu Hanifa that Banu Taghlib women are not subject, similar to the view of Shafi'i and Zufar, who argue it is essentially jizya (which is not on women). The Hanafi position stated in the Hidayah is the first one: women are subject, based on the treaty's analogy to Muslim women. Students should note that this is a specific historical treaty, not a general rule.

Key Terms
سائمہ (sā'imah): Grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep/goats) that are allowed to graze freely for most of the year.
صلح (sulh): A peace treaty or compromise agreement, here referring to the treaty between Umar and Banu Taghlib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the treaty only applies to adults.

The treaty with Banu Taghlib determines zakat obligations by analogy to Muslim zakat: minors exempt, women liable at double rate.

Destruction of Wealth After Zakat Obligation
Presents Hanafi ruling that zakat drops if wealth perishes, rebutting Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat when nisab wealth is destroyed, explain the Hanafi proof using the analogy of the criminal slave, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Zakat is a part of the nisab, not a debt in the dhimma — if the wealth perishes, so does the obligation.

This lesson examines a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does zakat remain due if the nisab wealth is destroyed after the obligation becomes established but before payment? The Hanafi school, relying on the principle 'juz' min al-nisab' (a portion of the wealth), holds that the obligation drops. Imam al-Shafi'i, viewing zakat as a liability in the dhimma, maintains that the obligation remains if the owner had the ability to pay. Understanding this dispute illuminates the foundational Hanafi concept of zakat's attachment to specific wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly: zakat drops if the nisab wealth is destroyed after the obligation becomes due, as long as the destruction is not due to the owner's fault.
The ruling is based on the principle that zakat is attached to the specific wealth.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that zakat becomes a liability in the dhimma once the owner is able to pay, so destruction does not drop the obligation.
The Shafi'i proof analogizes zakat to sadaqat al-fitr, which is a liability per person.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof: zakat is a part (juz') of the nisab, not a debt. This is supported by the analogy to a criminal slave handed over as compensation: if the slave dies, the liability lapses.
The slave analogy demonstrates that obligations attached to specific items expire when the item is destroyed.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
Shafi'i argues based on ability to pay and demand; Hanafis respond that the obligation is not in the dhimma and that the owner is not liable unless he deliberately destroys the wealth (istihlak).
After the collector's demand, some Hanafis entertain liability, but the relied-upon view is no liability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if wealth is destroyed by fire, Hanafis say no zakat due; Shafi'is say it is still owed if the owner had means to pay before destruction.
This difference affects whether the owner must compensate from other wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ هَلَكَ الْمَالُ بَعْدَ وُجُوبِ الزَّكَاةِ سَقَطَتِ الزَّكَاةُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَضْمَنُ إِذَا هَلَكَ بَعْدَ التَّمَكُّنِ مِنَ الْأَدَاءِ لِأَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ فِي الذِّمَّةِ فَصَارَ كَصَدَقَةِ الْفِطْرِ وَلِأَنَّهُ مَنَعَهُ بَعْدَ الطَّلَبِ فَصَارَ كَالْاسْتِهْلَاكِ وَلَنَا الْوَاجِبُ جُزْءٌ مِنَ النِّصَابِ تَحْقِيقًا لِلتَّيْسِيرِ فَيَسْقُطُ بِهَلَاكِ مَحَلِّهِ كَدَفْعِ الْعَبْدِ الْجَانِي بِالْجِنَايَةِ يَسْقُطُ بِهَلَاكِهِ وَالْمُسْتَحِقُ فَقِيرٌ يُعَيِّنُهُ الْمَالِكُ وَلَمْ يَتَحَقَّقْ مِنْهُ الطَّلَبُ وَبَعْدَ طَلَبِ السَّاعِي قِيلَ يَضْمَنُ وَقِيلَ لَا يَضْمَنُ لِانْعِدَامِ التَّقْوِيتِ وَفِي الِاسْتِهْلَاكِ وُجِدَ التَّعَدِّي وَفِي هَلَاكِ الْبَعْضِ يَسْقُطُ بِقَدْرِهِ اعْتِبَارًا بِالْكُلِّ
And if the wealth is destroyed after the obligation of zakat, the zakat is dropped. And al-Shafi'i said: He will be liable (daman) if it is destroyed after being able to pay, because the obligation is in the dhimmah (liability), so it becomes like sadaqat al-fitr; and because he prevented it after the demand, so it becomes like destruction (istihlak). And our proof is that the obligatory is a part of the nisab, for the purpose of facilitation, so it falls due to the destruction of its locus (mahall), like the handing over of the slave who commits a crime (al-jani) for the crime: it falls with his destruction. And the entitled person is a poor person whom the owner specifies, and the demand (talab) from him is not actualized. And after the demand of the collector (sa'i), it is said he will be liable, and it is said he will not be liable due to the absence of delay (taqwit). And in the case of destruction (istihlak), transgression (ta'addi) is found, and in the destruction of some (of the wealth), it falls proportionately, by analogy with the whole.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding what happens when the wealth on which zakat is obligatory is destroyed after zakat became due but before payment. The Hanafi position: zakat is dropped because it is a specific portion (juz') of the nisab itself. Since the property is destroyed, there is nothing from which to take the portion. This is like a slave who commits a crime: if the slave is handed over as compensation and then dies, the compensation lapses because the specific item is gone. Zakat is not a pure debt (dain) in the dhimmah; it is attached to the wealth. Al-Shafi'i argues that zakat becomes a liability (fil dhimma) once the owner is able to pay, so it is like sadaqat al-fitr (which is a liability that cannot drop due to destruction). He also says that if the owner prevented payment after a demand, it is like deliberate destruction (istihlak). The Hanafis respond that the purpose of zakat is facilitation (taysir), so it is attached to the specific wealth. The text then notes a difference of opinion after the collector's demand: some say liability, some say no. The destruction of part of the wealth: zakat falls proportionally. This ruling is important because it protects the owner from liability for circumstances beyond their control, unlike a debt. The Hanafi principle here is 'zakat is a portion of the property (juz' min al-mal)', not a debt in the dhimmah.

Key Terms
جزء من النصاب (juz' min al-nisab): Zakat is considered an inseparable part of the nisab wealth, not a separate debt.
التَّمَكُّن من الأداء (al-tamakkun min al-ada'): The ability to pay; having both the wealth and the ability to hand it over to the recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, if a person's zakatable wealth is completely destroyed by a natural disaster after zakat became due, what happens to the zakat obligation?
A) The zakat is still owed because it is a debt in the dhimma.
B) The zakat is dropped because it is a part of the nisab that no longer exists.
C) The zakat is only dropped if the owner was unable to pay at the time of destruction.
D) The zakat must be paid from other wealth.

Key Takeaway
Zakat is not a debt in the dhimma; it is a portion from the specific nisab, so if the nisab is destroyed without fault, the zakat obligation drops.

Banu Taghlib Treaty: Zakat or Jizya?
Historical treaty and derived fiqh rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the doubled payment for Banu Taghlib women and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding their obligation.

Core Idea
A treaty can create a binding obligation distinct from standard zakat.

This lesson explores a unique historical case: the peace treaty between Umar (RA) and the Christian Arab tribe of Banu Taghlib. The treaty imposed a doubled payment in place of jizya, leading to rulings on liability for minors and women, and an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether women must pay.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Recognize why Banu Taghlib refused jizya and how the treaty was made, with Umar's consultation and Uthman's affirmation.
The treaty is an example of sulh (peace agreement) that later became binding through Caliphal consensus.
2
Identify the general ruling from the treaty
From the analogy to Muslim zakat: minors are exempt (as nothing is taken from Muslim minors), women pay (as Muslim women pay zakat).
Key: the doubled payment is treated like zakat for liability categories, even though its nature is jizya.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the narration from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad: women are exempt because the payment is jizya in reality.
This narration is from the Nawadir (rare transmissions), not Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The treaty position (women pay) is mufta bihi because it was acted upon by Umar and Uthman, representing ijma’ of the Companions.
Tarjih authority: the practice of the Caliphs outweighs the qiyas (jizya analogy) from the opposing view.

تشریح بن تغلب عرب کے نصاری کی ایک قوم ہے جو روم کے قریب آباد تھی ۔ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ نے جب ان پر جزیہ مقرر کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو انہوں نے انکار کیا۔ اور کہنے لگے کہ ہم بھی عرب ہیں ہم کو ادار جزیہ سے شرم آتی ہے۔ اگر آپ ہم پر جزیہ مقرر کریں گے تو ہم بھاگ کر آپ کے دشمنوں کے پاس روم چلے جائیں گے۔ اگر آپ ہم سے وہ لیں جو مسلمانوں سے لیا جاتا ہے یعنی زکوۃ اور آپ اس کو ہم پر دو گنا کر دیں تب بھی ہم راضی ہیں۔ حضرت عمر نے صحابہ سے مشورہ کرنے کے بعد اس پر صلح کرلی اور فرمایا۔ هَذِهِ حِزْيَةٌ وَسَمُّوهَا ما شتم یعنی یہ جزیہ ہے تم اس کا جو چاہے نام رکھو! پس اس پر صلح ہوگئی کہ ان سے مسلمانوں کی زکوۃ کا دو گنا یا جائے گا۔ یعنی مسلمانوں سے ڈھائی فیصد لیا جاتا ہے تو ان سے پانچ فیصد لیا جائے گا۔ حضرت عمر کے بعد پھر حضرت عثمان نے بھی اس صلح سے کوئی تعرض نہیں کیا۔ اس لئے یہ صلح پوری امت کے لئے لازم ہو گئی ۔
اب مسئلہ یہ ہوا کہ بنو تغلب کے نابالغ بچوں کے سائمہ جانوروں میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے ۔ البتہ ان کی عورتوں پر وہ واجب ہے جو ان کے مردوں پر واجب ہے کیونکہ بنو تغلب سے اس بات پر صلح ہوئی ہے کہ مسلمانوں سے جولیا جاتا ہے ہو تغلب سے اس کا دو چند لیا جائے گا پس چونکہ مسلمان بچوں سے کچھ نہیں لیا جاتا۔ اس لئے ان کے بچوں سے بھی نہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ مسلمان عورتوں سے لیا جاتا ہے لہذا ان کی عورتوں سے بھی لیا جائے گا۔ لیکن ان کی عورتوں سے وہ لیا جائے گا۔ جو ان کے مردوں سے لیا جاتا ہے۔ یعنی مسلمانوں پر جو واجب ہےاس کا دو چنڈ اور حسن بن زیاد نے حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ بنو تغلب کی عورتوں سے بھی نہ لیا جائے گا۔ یہی امام شافعی اور امام زفر کا قول ہے کیونکہ یہ حقیقتا جزیہ ہے اور عورتوں پر جزیہ نہیں ہوتا۔
Commentary on Banu Taghlib: Banu Taghlib is a Christian Arab tribe living near Rome. When Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) intended to impose jizya on them, they refused and said: 'We too are Arabs; we are ashamed of jizya. If you impose jizya, we will flee to your enemies in Rome. But if you take from us what is taken from Muslims, i.e., zakat, and double it, we are willing.' Umar consulted the Companions and made a treaty, saying: 'This is jizya; name it whatever you wish.' So the treaty was made that they would pay double the zakat of Muslims (i.e., 5% instead of 2.5%). After Umar, Uthman also did not interfere, so this treaty became binding on the entire ummah. The ruling: For the minor children of Banu Taghlib, zakat on their grazing livestock is not obligatory. However, for their women, what is obligatory on their men is also obligatory on them, because the treaty stipulates that what is taken from Muslims is taken double from Banu Taghlib. Since nothing is taken from Muslim children, nothing is taken from their children; and since it is taken from Muslim women, it is taken from their women. But from their women is taken what is taken from their men, i.e., double what is obligatory on Muslims. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that nothing will be taken from Banu Taghlib's women either. This is also the view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, because it is actually jizya, and jizya is not imposed on women.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses the historical treaty between the Muslims and the Christian tribe of Banu Taghlib, which was made by Umar (RA). The treaty established a payment that is like zakat in form but is actually jizya in nature. The key rulings derived from this treaty are:
- Minor children of Banu Taghlib do not pay anything on their grazing livestock.
- Women of Banu Taghlib must pay the same doubled amount as their men, because in Islam, women also pay zakat on their property.
- There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: a narration from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) holds that women do not pay because the payment is jizya, and jizya is not upon women. This is also the view of Shafi'i and Zufar.
- The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the treaty stipulation: women do pay, as the treaty was binding and followed by Umar and Uthman.

The passage shows how historical precedents (sulh) and ijma’ of the Companions establish rulings.

Key Terms
جزیہ (jizyah): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state.
سائمہ (sā'imah): Grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep, goats) that are left to graze freely.
نابالغ (nābāligh): Minor (child not yet reached puberty). In the context, minors are not liable for zakat or treaty payments.
صلح (sulh): A peace treaty or settlement that creates binding obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are Banu Taghlib minors exempt from the doubled payment according to the treaty ruling?
A) Because the treaty explicitly exempts them.
B) Because Muslim minors do not pay zakat, and the treaty follows the same categories.
C) Because they are too young to own livestock.
D) Because they will convert to Islam later.

Key Takeaway
A binding sulh can create tax obligations that differ from default fiqh rulings, and the practice of the Caliphs is a valid source of tarjih.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
When Zakat Lapses: Hanafi Ruling on Wealth Destruction
Ruling with proof on zakat lapsing with wealth destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat when wealth perishes after obligation, explain the primary and secondary proofs, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Zakat is part of the nisab itself, so it falls with the wealth's destruction without transgression.

This passage addresses a critical distinction: is zakat a separate liability or an integral part of the wealth? The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith 'Fi kulli arba'ina shatin shatun', treats zakat as a part of the nisab itself. Consequently, if the wealth perishes without fault, the zakat obligation falls. This lesson unpacks the proof and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its basis
State that according to the Hanafi school, if zakatable wealth perishes after the obligation arises, without the owner's transgression (ta'addi), the zakat obligation lapses. This is the core ruling of this passage.
Note the condition: no ta'addi.
2
Examine the primary dalil (hadith)
The hadith 'Fi kulli arba'ina shatin shatun' (in every forty sheep, one sheep) is cited. The preposition 'fi' indicates that the zakat is part of the nisab itself, not a separate liability. This is the foundational textual evidence.
The wajh al-dalalah is the word 'fi'.
3
Understand the secondary analogy (qiyas)
The author draws an analogy with the offending slave ('abd janin): if a slave who committed a crime is to be handed over, but the slave dies before delivery, the obligation falls. Similarly, when the subject of zakat (the wealth) perishes, the obligation falls.
This strengthens the Hanafi position.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i evidence and reasoning
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that zakat is a liability in the dhimma (debt), like sadaqat al-fitr and other obligations, so it persists even if wealth perishes. He also analogizes refusal after demand to destruction. The Hanafi response refutes this by distinguishing the nature of zakat and the absence of a demand from the mustahiq.
The key difference: what is the nature of zakat?
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the sa'i's demand
After the official tax collector (sa'i) demands zakat and the owner refuses, then the wealth perishes, there is a difference: Abu al-Hasan al-Karghi says the owner is liable; the Mashayikh of Ma wara al-Nahr say he is not. This shows refinement within the school.
The mufta bihi position is that no liability exists even after demand, as per the text's inclination.

بعيناء
And if the wealth perishes after the obligation of zakat, the zakat lapses. Al-Shafi'i said: He is liable if it perishes after capability of payment, because the obligation is in the dhimma, so it becomes like sadaqat al-fitr, and because he prevented it after demand, so it becomes like destruction. Our proof: The obligatory is a part of the nisab, actually for facilitation, so it falls with the destruction of its locus, like the delivery of the offending slave for the crime falls with his destruction. The mustahiq is a poor person designated by the owner, and no demand has materialized from him. After the demand of the sa'i (tax collector), it is said he is liable, and it is said he is not liable, due to the absence of [something]. In destruction with transgression, it is found; and in destruction of part, it falls proportionally, analogizing to the whole.
Explanation: According to us, after zakat becomes obligatory, if the wealth is destroyed without transgression, the zakat is also waived. This is also the view of Ahmad. Al-Shafi'i said: If it is destroyed after ability to pay, zakat is not waived but he is liable for the amount of zakat. Ability to pay means the owner, after the completion of the year, was able to find a mustahiq, whether after a demand or not. Shafi'i's proof: Zakat is obligatory in the dhimma, and whoever has an obligation in the dhimma is not absolved due to inability to pay, like sadaqat al-fitr, Hajj, and debts. If a person owes sadaqat al-fitr, or Hajj becomes obligatory, or he is a debtor, then if all his wealth is destroyed, those obligations do not fall from his dhimma. Similarly, zakat. Second proof: Zakat is a right of Allah, and after being able to pay, Allah has demanded it through address (metaphorical demand), but he did not pay. So the destruction is like withholding after the right-holder's demand, which imposes liability. Our proof: Zakat is not obligatory in the dhimma but in the specific wealth, i.e., zakat is a part of the nisab, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'In every forty sheep is one sheep.' The word 'in' (fi) indicates inclusion/part, meaning one sheep from among the forty. This is not that the zakat is a separate sheep outside them, but a part. So zakat is a part of the nisab, and when the whole is destroyed, the part cannot be extracted, so it falls. This is like if a slave commits accidental homicide, the owner must surrender the slave or pay ransom; if the slave dies before surrender, the obligation falls. So zakat is not like sadaqat al-fitr etc. The phrase 'al-mustahiq fageer yu'ayyih al-malik' is the answer to Shafi'i's second proof. The mustahiq is not every poor person but the one the owner designates, and the owner has not yet designated anyone, so no demand from him. As for the sa'i (tax collector) demanding and the owner not giving until the wealth is destroyed: Abu al-Hasan al-Karghi said he is liable, but the Mashayikh of Ma wara al-Nahr said he is not. Abu al-Hasan's proof: The sa'i is designated to collect, so his demand is like the demand of the mustahiq...
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on zakat when the wealth is destroyed after obligation. The text begins with the ruling (zakat lapses) and then contrasts it with Shafi'i's view (liability if able to pay). The Hanafi proof is based on the hadith 'Fi kulli arba'ina shatin shatun' which shows zakat is part of the nisab, not a debt in the dhimma. The analogy of the offending slave illustrates that if the subject matter is destroyed, the obligation falls. The text also addresses two other points: (1) The mustahiq (entitled recipient) is specified by the owner, so there is no demand from the state unless the sa'i (tax collector) demands; (2) there is an intra-Hanafi difference after the sa'i's demand: Abu al-Hasan al-Karghi holds that refusal after such demand creates liability, while the Mashayikh of Ma wara al-Nahr hold it does not. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that zakat falls with destruction without ta'addi (transgression). The passage is a model of usul al-fiqh: using a hadith to establish hukm, qiyas, and refuting opposing analogy.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or responsibility to pay compensation. Here, whether the owner is liable for zakat after destruction.
تعدی (ta'addī): Transgression or wrongful act. If the owner causes destruction, he is liable; if natural, not.
ساعی (sā'ī): The official tax collector sent by the state to collect zakat from the wealthy.
جزء (juz'): Part. Here, zakat is a literal part of the nisab, not a separate debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the nature of zakat on livestock as deduced from the hadith 'Fi kulli arba'ina shatin shatun'?
A) A debt in the dhimma
B) A part of the nisab
C) A sunnah
D) A state tax

Key Takeaway
Zakat is part of the nisab itself, so its obligation lapses with the destruction of the wealth without transgression.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat Waived if Nisab Destroyed: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Arguments on zakat validity when nisab destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat waiver when nisab is destroyed and evaluate the Shafi'i proof based on liability.

Core Idea
Zakat is part of the nisab, not a personal debt; destruction waives the obligation.

In Hanafi fiqh, zakat is considered a part of the nisab itself, not a separate liability on the person. This leads to a fundamental difference with the Shafi'i school regarding what happens if the nisab is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory. This lesson examines the proofs from both sides, focusing on the hadith 'fi kulli arba'ina shatin shah' and the analogy to qisas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Explain that according to Hanafi (and Imam Ahmad), zakat is waived if the nisab is destroyed without transgression.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that zakat is a liability in the dhimma and is not waived by destruction if the owner was able to pay.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues by analogy to sadaqat al-fitr, Hajj, and debts: one does not become free of these obligations due to inability to pay.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi rebuts that zakat is not a liability but a part of wealth; the hadith uses 'fi' to indicate partiality; also analogized to a slave dying before delivery in qisas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if wealth destroyed, Hanafi says no zakat due; Shafi'i says zakat remains as a debt.

النہر نے کہا ہے کہ ضامن نہ ہوگا ۔ شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سامی چونکہ زکوۃ وصول کرنے کے لئے متعین ہے۔ اس کے مانگنے کے باوجود اس نے منع کر دیا۔ پس اس کا منع کرنا تفویت اور استہلاک ہو گا۔ ہے کہ اس کار رکنا کسی دوسری جگہ دینے کے ارادے سے ہو پس جب زکوۃ دینے سے رکنا تقویت نہیں ہے تو وہ ضامن بھی نہ ہو گا۔ وفی الاستهلاك ..... الخ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے، جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ استبلاک کی صورت میں چونکہ مالک کی طرف سے تعدی پائی گئی۔ اس لئے زجر ا اس پر ضمان واجب کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کچھ مال ہلاک ہو گیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تو ہلاک شدہ کی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی اور باقی ماندہ میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی کیونکہ بعض کو کل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا پس جب کل ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں پوری زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے تو بعض مال ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں اسی کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔
Explanation: The issue is that in our view, if wealth is destroyed without transgression after zakat becomes obligatory, then its zakat is also waived. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i said: If it was destroyed after being able to pay zakat, then zakat is not waived; rather, he is liable for the amount of zakat. Being able to pay means that after the completion of the year, the owner succeeded in finding a deserving recipient, whether after seeking or without seeking. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that zakat is obligatory in the liability (dhimma), and one who has an obligation in his liability is not absolved from it due to inability to pay, like sadaqat al-fitr, Hajj, and debts of people. That is, if sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory on someone, or Hajj becomes obligatory, or he is in debt, then all his wealth is destroyed, those obligations are not waived. Similarly, if after zakat becomes obligatory all wealth is destroyed, zakat is not waived. The second evidence: Zakat is the right of Allah, and after being able to pay, Allah demanded it through address (addressing intention), but he did not pay. So the destruction of wealth is like withholding after the right-holder's demand, and withholding after demand necessitates liability, just as destroying with transgression necessitates liability. Our evidence: Zakat is not obligatory in the liability but in the specific wealth; i.e., zakat is a part of the nisab, because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'For every forty sheep, one sheep.' The word 'fi' indicates partiality. This does not mean that the zakat of forty sheep is one sheep given separately; rather, it means that from those forty, one sheep which is a part of the forty is given. Designating a part of the nisab as zakat is for ease, because extracting a part of the nisab is within human capability. So it is established that zakat is a part of the nisab, and this part exists within the wealth. When the entire wealth is lost, this part is also lost because the person is unable to extract it. When he is unable to extract it, it is not obligatory; rather, it is waived. This is exactly like a slave who kills someone by mistake: the ruling is that the killer slave is given to the guardian of the victim, or his ransom is paid, and the owner agreed. Then before handing over, the slave dies. Now the delivery is waived, and nothing is obligatory on the owner. Since it is established that zakat is not obligatory in the liability but in the specific wealth, and sadaqat al-fitr etc. are obligatory in the liability, analogizing zakat to sadaqat al-fitr is incorrect. 'And the deserving recipient is a poor person designated by the owner' is the response to Imam al-Shafi'i's second evidence. The gist: the deserving recipient is not every poor person but the one whom the owner designates; the owner has not yet designated anyone, so demand from that side is not actualized, and thus withholding after demand is not found. If the sā'ī (collector) demanded zakat and the owner did not give until all wealth was destroyed, then Shaikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said he becomes liable for zakat, and when he obtains wealth, he must pay the penalty. The scholars of Transoxiana said he is not liable. Al-Karkhi's evidence: since the sā'ī is appointed to collect zakat, his refusal despite demand is causing loss and destruction; in case of loss/destruction, liability for zakat arises, so he must pay the penalty. The scholars of Transoxiana's evidence: refusing to give zakat is not causing loss because he may have intended to give elsewhere; since refusal is not causing loss, he is not liable. 'And in the case of destruction...' is the response to al-Shafi'i's analogy. The gist: in the case of destruction, since there is transgression from the owner, liability is imposed as a deterrent. The author of Hidayah says: If some wealth is destroyed and some remains, the zakat of the destroyed part is waived, and zakat is obligatory on the remaining part, because the part is analogized to the whole. So when zakat is waived in case of total destruction, it is waived proportionally in case of partial destruction.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on whether zakat is waived if the nisab is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory. The Hanafi position (followed by Imam Ahmad) is that zakat ceases to be obligatory because it is a part of the nisab itself. Imam Shafi'i holds that zakat is a liability on the person and is not waived by destruction if he was able to pay. The Hanafi respond with a hadith using 'fi' to indicate partiality, and analogize to the case of a slave dying before being handed over for qisas. The passage also addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the official collector (sā'ī) demands zakat and the owner refuses, then the wealth is destroyed—Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi says the owner becomes liable, while the scholars of Transoxiana say not, since refusal is not necessarily destruction. Finally, the author applies the same principle to partial destruction: zakat is waived proportionally.

Key Terms
زكوۃ (zakāh): The obligatory charity on specified wealth, considered a part of the nisab in Hanafi law.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.
ساعی (sāʿī): The official collector appointed by the state to collect zakat.
تفویت (tafwīt): Causing loss or destruction of the wealth by preventing the recipient from getting it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person's entire nisab is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory but before payment, what is the ruling?
A) He must still pay zakat from other wealth.
B) The zakat obligation is waived.
C) He must make up the zakat when he can.
D) He is sinful for not paying earlier.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, zakat is a part of the nisab, so its destruction extinguishes the obligation, unlike a personal debt.

Intra-Hanafi Debate: Effect of Sā'ī Demand and Partial Destruction on Zakat
Intra-Hanafi arguments on sā'ī demand and partial destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and the Transoxiana scholars regarding liability when the sā'ī demands zakat, and apply the ruling on partial destruction.

Core Idea
Refusing the sā'ī does not necessarily constitute tafwīt; the owner's intention matters.

After establishing the Hanafi view that zakat is part of the nisab, a secondary debate arises: what if the official collector (sā'ī) demands zakat and the owner refuses, then the wealth is destroyed? Some Hanafi scholars hold the owner liable, while others do not. Additionally, the principle is applied to partial destruction of the nisab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The sā'ī demands zakat, the owner refuses, then all wealth is destroyed. Is the owner liable?
2
State Al-Karkhi's view
Shaikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said the owner becomes liable because his refusal is tafwīt (causing loss).
3
State the Transoxiana scholars' view
They said he is not liable because refusal may be due to intention to give elsewhere; it is not necessarily tafwīt.
4
Analyse the proofs
Al-Karkhi analogizes to destruction with transgression; Transoxiana scholars focus on the owner's possible good intention.
5
Apply to partial destruction
The author of Hidayah rules that if part of the nisab is destroyed, zakat is waived proportionally, following the same principle.
