بعد اگر پورا مال ہلاک ہو گیا۔ تو اس کے ذمہ سے زکوۃ ساقط نہ ہوگی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کہ زکوۃ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے اور ادا پر قادر ہونے کے بعد خطاب کے ذریعہ اللہ تعالی نے اس کو طلب بھی کیا ہے (خطاب باری سے تقدیری خطاب مراد ہے) لیکن اس نے ادا نہیں کیا۔ تو یہ مال کا ہلاک ہونا ایسا ہو گا جیسے کہ صاحب حق کے طلب کرنے کے بعد اس کو روکنا ۔ اور صاحب حق کے طلب کرنے کے بعد روکنا ضمان واجب کرتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ تعدی کے ساتھ ہلاک کرنا ضمان واجب کرتا ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ ذمہ میں واجب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ معین مال میں واجب ہوتی ہے یعنی زکوۃ نصاب کا ایک جز ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ فِى كُلِّ اَرْبَعِيْنَ شاةٍ شاۃ ، اس قول میں کلمہ فی “ ہے اور کلمہ فی جزئیت پر دلالت کرتا ہے یعنی چالیس ۴۰ بکریوں میں ایک بکری ہے ۔اس کا یہ مطلب ہرگز نہیں ہے کہ چالیس ۴۰ بکریوں کی زکوۃ یہ ہے ایک بکری ان کے علاوہ دے بلکہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ انہیں چالیس ۴۰ میں سے ایک بکری جوان چالیس ۴۰ کا جز ہے وہ دے، اور نصاب کے ایک جز وکوز کو ۃ مقرر کرنا آسانی کے پیش نظر ہے کیونکہ نصاب کے ایک جز کو نکالنا انسان کی قدرت میں ہے بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ زکو مال نصاب ہی کا ایک جز ہے اور یہ جز خود مال میں موجود ہے تو یہ جزا پنا کل تلف ہونے سے ساقط ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ جب پور امال ہلاک ہو گیا تو یہ شخص اس جز کونکالنے پر قادر نہ رہا۔ اور جب نکالنے پر قادر نہ رہا تو اس پر واجب بھی نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسے کسی کے غلام نے کسی کو خطا قتل کر دیا تو حکم یہ ہے که قاتل غلام، ولی مقتول کو دیدیا جائے ۔ یا اس کا فدیہ دیدیا جائے اور مالک نے اس کو منظور بھی کر لیا۔ پھر سپر د کر دینے سے پہلے وہ قاتل غلام مرگیا۔ تو اب یہ دینا ساقط ہو گیا۔ یعنی مالک پر کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی پس جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ زکوۃ ذمہ میں واجب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ عین مال میں واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اور صدقہ الفطر وغیرہ ذمہ میں واجب ہوتے ہیں تو زکوۃ کو صدقۃ الفطر وغیرہ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ وَالْمُسْتَحقَ فَقِير يُعَيِّهُ المَالِكُ سے امام شافعی کی دوسری دلیل کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ کا مستحق ہر فقیر نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ فقیر ہے جس کو مالک متعین کرے اور مالک نے ابھی تک کسی کو متعین نہیں کیا لہذا اس کی طرف سے طلب بھی متحقق نہ ہوئی اور جب طلب نہیں پائی گئی تو طلب کے بعد منع کرنا بھی نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور جب منع کرنا نہیں پایا گیا تو مال ہونے کی صورت میں منمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ اگر ساعی یعنی زکوۃ وصول کرنے والے نے زکوۃ مانگی ۔ اور مالک نے نہ دی یہاں تک کہ پورا مال ہلاک ہو گیا۔ تو شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی نے کہا کہ شیخص زکوۃ کا ضامن ہو گا حتی کہ جب اس کو مال میسر آئے تو یہ تاوان ادا کرے۔ اور مشائخ ماوراء النہر نے کہا ہے کہ ضامن نہ ہوگا ۔ شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سامی چونکہ زکوۃ وصول کرنے کے لئے متعین ہے۔ اس کے مانگنے کے باوجود اس نے منع کر دیا۔ پس اس کا منع کرنا تفویت اور استہلاک ہو گا۔ تفویت اور استبلاک کی صورت میں چونکہ زکوۃ کا ضمان آتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں اس پر زکوۃ کا تاوان واجب ہوگا۔ مشائخ ماوراء النہر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ دینے سے رکنا تفویت (فوت کر دیتا ) نہیں ہے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ اس کار رکنا کسی دوسری جگہ دینے کے ارادے سے ہو پس جب زکوۃ دینے سے رکنا تقویت نہیں ہے تو وہ ضامن بھی نہ ہو گا۔ وفی الاستهلاك ..... الخ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے، جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ استبلاک کی صورت میں چونکہ مالک کی طرف سے تعدی پائی گئی۔ اس لئے زجر ا اس پر ضمان واجب کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کچھ مال ہلاک ہو گیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تو ہلاک شدہ کی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی اور باقی ماندہ میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی کیونکہ بعض کو کل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا پس جب کل ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں پوری زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے تو بعض مال ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں اسی کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔
Explanation: The issue is that in our view, if wealth is destroyed without transgression after zakat becomes obligatory, then its zakat is also waived. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i said: If it was destroyed after being able to pay zakat, then zakat is not waived; rather, he is liable for the amount of zakat. Being able to pay means that after the completion of the year, the owner succeeded in finding a deserving recipient, whether after seeking or without seeking. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that zakat is obligatory in the liability (dhimma), and one who has an obligation in his liability is not absolved from it due to inability to pay, like sadaqat al-fitr, Hajj, and debts of people. That is, if sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory on someone, or Hajj becomes obligatory, or he is in debt, then all his wealth is destroyed, those obligations are not waived. Similarly, if after zakat becomes obligatory all wealth is destroyed, zakat is not waived. The second evidence: Zakat is the right of Allah, and after being able to pay, Allah demanded it through address (addressing intention), but he did not pay. So the destruction of wealth is like withholding after the right-holder's demand, and withholding after demand necessitates liability, just as destroying with transgression necessitates liability. Our evidence: Zakat is not obligatory in the liability but in the specific wealth; i.e., zakat is a part of the nisab, because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'For every forty sheep, one sheep.' The word 'fi' indicates partiality. This does not mean that the zakat of forty sheep is one sheep given separately; rather, it means that from those forty, one sheep which is a part of the forty is given. Designating a part of the nisab as zakat is for ease, because extracting a part of the nisab is within human capability. So it is established that zakat is a part of the nisab, and this part exists within the wealth. When the entire wealth is lost, this part is also lost because the person is unable to extract it. When he is unable to extract it, it is not obligatory; rather, it is waived. This is exactly like a slave who kills someone by mistake: the ruling is that the killer slave is given to the guardian of the victim, or his ransom is paid, and the owner agreed. Then before handing over, the slave dies. Now the delivery is waived, and nothing is obligatory on the owner. Since it is established that zakat is not obligatory in the liability but in the specific wealth, and sadaqat al-fitr etc. are obligatory in the liability, analogizing zakat to sadaqat al-fitr is incorrect. 'And the deserving recipient is a poor person designated by the owner' is the response to Imam al-Shafi'i's second evidence. The gist: the deserving recipient is not every poor person but the one whom the owner designates; the owner has not yet designated anyone, so demand from that side is not actualized, and thus withholding after demand is not found. If the sā'ī (collector) demanded zakat and the owner did not give until all wealth was destroyed, then Shaikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said he becomes liable for zakat, and when he obtains wealth, he must pay the penalty. The scholars of Transoxiana said he is not liable. Al-Karkhi's evidence: since the sā'ī is appointed to collect zakat, his refusal despite demand is causing loss and destruction; in case of loss/destruction, liability for zakat arises, so he must pay the penalty. The scholars of Transoxiana's evidence: refusing to give zakat is not causing loss because he may have intended to give elsewhere; since refusal is not causing loss, he is not liable. 'And in the case of destruction...' is the response to al-Shafi'i's analogy. The gist: in the case of destruction, since there is transgression from the owner, liability is imposed as a deterrent. The author of Hidayah says: If some wealth is destroyed and some remains, the zakat of the destroyed part is waived, and zakat is obligatory on the remaining part, because the part is analogized to the whole. So when zakat is waived in case of total destruction, it is waived proportionally in case of partial destruction.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on whether zakat is waived if the nisab is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory. The Hanafi position (followed by Imam Ahmad) is that zakat ceases to be obligatory because it is a part of the nisab itself. Imam Shafi'i holds that zakat is a liability on the person and is not waived by destruction if he was able to pay. The Hanafi respond with a hadith using 'fi' to indicate partiality, and analogize to the case of a slave dying before being handed over for qisas. The passage also addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the official collector (sā'ī) demands zakat and the owner refuses, then the wealth is destroyed—Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi says the owner becomes liable, while the scholars of Transoxiana say not, since refusal is not necessarily destruction. Finally, the author applies the same principle to partial destruction: zakat is waived proportionally.

Key Terms
زكوۃ (zakāh): The obligatory charity on specified wealth, considered a part of the nisab in Hanafi law.
ساعی (sāʿī): The official collector appointed by the state to collect zakat.
تفویت (tafwīt): Causing loss or destruction of the wealth by preventing the recipient from getting it.
استہلاک (istihlāk): Destruction of wealth, often with transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the scholars of Transoxiana, if the sā'ī demands zakat and the owner refuses, then the wealth is destroyed, the owner is:
A) Liable for the full zakat.
B) Not liable because refusal is not necessarily tafwīt.
C) Liable only for half.
D) Sinful but not liable.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute on whether refusal to pay the sā'ī constitutes tafwīt, but the majority of later scholars (Transoxiana) hold it does not, preserving the principle that zakat is part of the nisab.

Liability for Zakat When Property Is Destroyed or Refused
Ruling on zakat liability with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat liability when the owner prevents collection or destroys property, and distinguish the positions of Hidayah and the Mashayikh of Transoxiana.

Core Idea
Preventing zakat collection amounts to destruction, making the owner liable—unless intention to give elsewhere is proven.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical question: if the owner of zakatable property prevents the collector from taking the zakat or destroys the property, is he liable to compensate the missing zakat? The text presents the main ruling, an intra-Hanafi difference from the Mashayikh of Transoxiana, and a response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. We will unpack the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its basis
The text states that if the owner prevents the collector, his action is considered tafwit (destruction) and istihlak (consumption), making compensation wajib. Note the reasoning: prevention is equated to actual destruction.
This is the position of the author of Hidayah, representing the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the Mashayikh's objection
The Mashayikh of Ma wara' al-nahr argue that mere refusal is not tafwit because the owner might intend to give the zakat elsewhere. Their qiyas: if the action is not tafwit, no liability arises.
This intra-Hanafi difference turns on the characterization of 'prevention'.
3
Analyze the response regarding istihlak
The text then addresses istihlak (consumption/destruction) as a response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The key is ta'addi (transgression) by the owner, which justifies liability as a deterrent.
Istihlak clearly involves destruction, so liability is imposed even according to the Mashayikh?
4
Apply the partial loss analogy
The author of Hidayah extends the principle: if only part of the wealth is destroyed, the zakat on that part is dropped, analogizing part to whole. Thus zakat is only wajib on the remaining portion.
This shows the scope of the rule: proportional to loss.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the Mashayikh, merely preventing without destruction does not create liability; according to Hidayah, prevention itself creates liability unless the owner can prove a valid intent to give elsewhere.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly given; both views are presented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
Al اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم كتاب الزكوة اس نے منع کر دیا۔ پس اس کا منع کرنا تفویت اور استہلاک ہو گا۔ تفویت اور استبلاک کی صورت میں چونکہ زکوۃ کا ضمان آتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں اس پر زکوۃ کا تاوان واجب ہوگا۔ مشائخ ماوراء النہر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ دینے سے رکنا تفویت (فوت کر دیتا ) نہیں ہے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ اس کار کنا کسی دوسری جگہ دینے کے ارادے سے ہو پس جب زکوۃ دینے سے رکنا تقویت نہیں ہے تو وہ ضامن بھی نہ ہو گا۔
وفی الاستهلاك ..... الخ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے، جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ استبلاک کی صورت میں چونکہ مالک کی طرف سے تعدی پائی گئی۔ اس لئے زجر ا اس پر ضمان واجب کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کچھ مال ہلاک ہو گیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تو ہلاک شدہ کی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی اور باقی ماندہ میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی کیونکہ بعض کو کل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا پس جب کل ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں پوری زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے تو بعض مال ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں اسی کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔
Al Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Three Book of Zakat: He prevented (the zakat collector). So his prevention becomes tafwit (destruction) and istihlak (consumption). In the case of tafwit and istihlak, since compensation for zakat is due, therefore in this case compensation for zakat is wajib upon him. The proof of the Mashayikh of Ma wara' al-nahr is that refraining from giving zakat is not tafwit (causing to be lost) because it is possible that his preventing was with the intention of giving it at another place. So when refraining from giving zakat is not tafwit, then he will also not be liable. "And concerning istihlak..." etc. is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The summary of the answer is that in the case of istihlak, since transgression (ta'addi) occurred on the part of the owner, therefore as a deterrent liability is made wajib upon him. The author of Hidayah says: If some of the wealth is destroyed and some remains, then the zakat on the destroyed part is dropped, and zakat is wajib on the remaining, because the part is analogized to the whole. Thus when in the case of total loss the entire zakat is dropped, then in the case of partial loss, that portion is dropped proportionally.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on liability for zakat when the owner prevents the collector from taking the zakat or destroys the zakatable property. The text first states the ruling: if the owner prevents the collector, his action is considered tafwit (destruction) and istihlak (consumption), making him liable for the zakat amount. Then it presents the view of the Mashayikh of Ma wara' al-nahr, who argue that mere refusal is not tafwit because the owner might intend to give the zakat elsewhere, so liability does not arise. The text then notes that the discussion on istihlak is a response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy; the response is that in istihlak, the owner has committed transgression (ta'addi), so liability is imposed as a deterrent. Finally, the author of Hidayah introduces the case of partial loss: if only part of the wealth is destroyed, the zakat on that part is dropped, and zakat on the remainder is wajib, drawing an analogy from the case of total loss. This is a clear ruling with an intra-Hanafi difference (Mashayikh vs. Hidayah) and an inter-madhhab response to Shafi'i.

Key Terms
تفویت (tafwit): Causing the loss or destruction of the zakatable property, making the owner liable for compensation.
استہلاک (istihlak): Consumption or destruction of the property by the owner, clearly establishing liability due to transgression (ta'addi).
ضمان (daman): Compensation owed for the zakat value when the property is destroyed or lost due to the owner's action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when only part of the zakatable wealth is destroyed, what happens to the zakat on the destroyed portion?
A) The zakat on the destroyed portion is still wajib because the year completed.
B) The zakat on the destroyed portion is dropped, and zakat is wajib only on the remaining portion.
C) The zakat on the destroyed portion must be paid from other wealth immediately.
D) The entire zakat is dropped because the wealth is incomplete.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, preventing zakat collection can create liability, but there is disagreement on whether mere refusal (without destruction) suffices for compensation.

Prepaying Zakat Before the Year's Completion
Ruling on permissibility of advanced zakat payment before haul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prepaying zakat before the haul and explain the proof from hadith and analogy.

Core Idea
Zakat can be prepaid once the nisab exists; the haul is only a condition for obligation, not for validity.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but its timing is often misunderstood. Can you pay your zakat before a full lunar year passes? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced distinction between the cause (nisab) and the condition (haul). This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proofs, and the scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Prepaying zakat before completion of the haul). What is the hukm according to the Hanafi school? (Ja'iz/permissible).
The ruling is that prepayment is valid and discharges the obligation once the year completes.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the text provide? (Hadith of the Prophet accepting two years' zakat from Abbas, and analogy to expiation after wounding).
The hadith is mursal but accepted by Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof establish permissibility? (The cause of obligation—nisab—is present; the Prophet's action shows validity of prepayment).
The haul is a condition for obligation, not for the act of giving.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which schools disagree? (Imam Malik opposes prepayment; Imam Zufar opposes prepayment for multiple nisabs). What are their proofs? (Malik: haul is a condition like nisab; Zufar: each nisab is an independent cause).
Malik argues that advancing the conditioned before the condition is invalid.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? (The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, supported by the hadith and the principle that the subordinate follows the origin).
The text favours the majority Hanafi view.

پیشگی زکوۃ ادا کر نے کا حکم
وَاِنْ قَدَّمَ الزَّكوةَ عَلَى الْحَوْلِ وَهُوَ مَالِكُ لِلبَصَابِ جَازَ الأَنَّهُ أَدَّى بَعْدَ سَببِ الْوُجُوبِ فَيَجُوزُ كَمَا إِذَا كَفَّرَ بَعْدَ الجرح وَفِيهِ خَلَافٌ مَالِكَ وَيَجُوزُ التَّعْجِيل لأكثر مِنْ نَسَةٍ لِوُجُودِ السَّبَبِ وَ يَجُوزُ لِنُصُبِ إِذَا كَانَ فِي مِلْكِهِ نِصَابُ وَاحِدٌ خِلَافًا لِزُفِّر لأنَّ النِّصَابَ الأَوَّلَ هُوَ الْأَصْلُ فِى السَّبَيَّةِ وَالزَّائِدُ عَلَيْهِ تَابِعَ لَهُ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے سال پورا ہونے سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کر دی اور وہ مالک نصاب بھی ہے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اس نے سبب وجوب کے بعد ادا کیا ہے تو جائز ہے جیسے زخمی کرنے کے بعد کفارہ دید یا ہو ۔ اور اس میں امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے اور ایک سال سے زیادہ کے لئے بھی زکوۃ مقدم کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ سبب موجود ہے اور کئی نصابوں کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدینا بھی جائز ہے جبکہ اس کی ملک میں ایک ہی نصاب
ہو اس میں امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ سب ہونے میں نصاب اول ہی اصل ہے اور جو اس پر زائد ہو وہ اس کے تابع ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک مالک نصاب کو حوالان حول سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کرنا جائز ہے یہی امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا قول ہے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حولان حول شرط ہے جیسے نصاب شرط ہے اور مشروط کا شرط پر مقدم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے حولان حول سے پہلے زکوۃ کا مقدم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے سبب وجوب (نصاب ) کے بعد زکوۃ ادا کی ہے اور سبب وجوب کے بعد ادا کرنا جائز ہے جیسے کسی شخص نے کسی مسلمان کو خطا سے گولی ماری اور اس کو ایسا مجروح کر دیا کہ زندگی کی امید نہیں رہی ۔ پس قتل خطاء میں ایک غلام آزاد کرنا چاہئے۔ وہ مجروح کی موت سے پہلے آزاد کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ سب قتل پایا گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اول وقت میں نماز ادا کی تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ نماز کسب یعنی وہ یکے بعد دائیگی پائی گئی ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حولان حول وجوب ادا کی شرط ہے نہ کہ جو از ادا کی یعنی حولان حول کے بعد زکوۃ ادا کرنا واجب ہو جاتا ہے اور اس سے پہلے واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ حولان حول کے بعد زکوۃ ادا کرنا جائز ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہوتا ۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ایک سال سے زیادہ پر بھی زکوۃ مقدم کرنا جائز ہے یعنی اگر کوئی شخص چند سال کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ سب یعنی نصاب کامل موجود ہے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعودؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت عباس سے دو سال کی زکوۃ چیگی قبول کر لی تھی اس حدیث سے بھی ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ چند سال کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی کی ملک میں ایک ہی نصاب ہو۔ لیکن اس نے کئی نصابوں کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدی تو جائز ہے۔ اس میں امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے۔ مثلا ایک آدمی کے پاس پانچ اونٹ ہیں۔ لیکن اس نے جولان حول سے پہلے چار بکریاں زکوۃ میں دید ہیں۔ پھر سال پورا ہوتے ہوتے اس کی ملک میں ہیں اونٹ ہو گئے ۔ تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ چار بکریاں کل یعنی میں اونٹ کی طرف سے ادا ہو گئیں اور امام زفر کے نزدیک صرف پانچ اونوں کی زکوۃ ادا ہوئی۔ باقی پندرہ کی زکوۃ دوبارہ ادا کرنا ضروری ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہر نصاب زکوۃ کے حق میں اصل بذاتہ ہے پس نصاب ثانی پر زکوۃ مقدم کرنا ایسا ہے جیسے نصاب اول پر مقدم کرنا ۔ اور زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت چونکہ نصاب ثانی موجود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر زکوۃ مقدم کرنا در حقیقت حکم کو سب پر مقدم کرنا ہے۔ اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ جو نصاب موجود ہے۔ اس کی زکوۃ مقدم کرنا تو جائز ہے لیکن جو موجود نہیں ہے اس کی زکوۃ کا مقدم کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ سبب ہونے میں نصاب اول ہی اصل ہے۔ اور جو اس پر زائد ہے وہ اس کے تابع ہے۔ اور اصل کے موجود ہونے سے اس کا تابع بھی موجود شمار کیا جاتا ہے اس کہا جائے گا کہ زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت جب نصاب اول موجود ہے تو دوسرے نصاب جو اس کے تابع ہیں وہ بھی موجود ہیں ۔ اور جب دوسرے نصاب ادائیگی زکوۃ کے وقت موجود ہیں تو تقدیم حکم علی السبب بھی لازم نہ آئے گا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے ایک آدمی کے پاس سال کے شروع میں ایک نصاب ہے۔ پھر سال کے آخر میں اور نصاب حاصل ہو گئے ۔ پھر نصاب اول پر سال پورا ہو گیا اور باقی نصابوں پر پورا نہیں ہوا تو یہی کہا جاتا ہے کہ گویا تمام نصابوں پر سال پورا ہو گیا اور مجموعہ سے زکوۃ کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو گیا۔ پس اسی طرح نصاب ثانی کو تقدیم زکوۃ کے حق میں اول سال میں موجود شمار کیا جائے گا۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم جمیل احمد صفی اللہ
Ruling on Prepaying Zakat: "And if he gives zakat before the year (completes), while he is owner of a nisab, it is permissible, because he gave after the cause of obligation, so it is permissible, just as if he expiates after wounding. And there is a difference with Malik. And prepayment for more than a year is permissible due to existence of the cause. And prepayment for multiple nisabs is permissible when he owns one nisab, contrary to Zufar, because the first nisab is the origin in causation, and what is in excess of it is subordinate to it. And Allah knows best." Translation: And if someone gives zakat before the year completes and he is the owner of a nisab, it is permissible, because he gave after the cause of obligation, so it is permissible, like giving expiation after causing a wound. And there is a difference with Imam Malik. And prepayment for more than one year is also permissible because the cause exists. And giving zakat for multiple nisabs in advance is also permissible while he owns only one nisab; there is a difference with Imam Zufar, because in the existence (of the nisab) the first nisab is the origin and what is in excess of it is subordinate to it. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The issue is that according to us, it is permissible for the owner of nisab to give zakat before the completion of the year. This is the saying of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. And according to Imam Malik, it is not permissible. Imam Malik's proof is that completion of the year is a condition just as the nisab is a condition, and advancing the conditioned before the condition is not permissible. Therefore, advancing zakat before the completion of the year is not permissible. Our proof is that this person gave zakat after the cause of obligation (nisab), and giving after the cause is permissible, like a person who accidentally shoots a Muslim and wounds him so that there is no hope of life; in accidental killing, he should free a slave; if he frees him before the wounded person dies, it is permissible, because the cause (the killing) is established. Similarly, if one prays at the beginning of the time, it is permissible, because prayer is a deed (i.e., it becomes due sequentially). The answer to Imam Shafi'i's proof is that completion of the year is a condition for the obligation of payment (wujub al-ada'), not for the permissibility of payment (jawaz al-ada'); meaning, after the year, it becomes wajib to give zakat, and before it is not wajib. It does not mean that after the year giving zakat is permissible and before it is not permissible. The author of Hidayah says: Prepaying for more than a year is also permissible, i.e., if a person gives zakat for several years in advance, there is no harm, because the cause (i.e., complete nisab) exists. Hadhrat Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) said that the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) accepted two years' zakat in advance from Hadhrat Abbas. This hadith also shows that there is no harm in giving several years' zakat in advance. And if a person owns only one nisab, but he gives zakat for multiple nisabs in advance, it is permissible. There is a difference with Imam Zufar. For example, a man has five camels; he gives four goats as zakat before the completion of the year; then by the end of the year, his ownership increases to twenty camels. According to us, these four goats are paid on behalf of all twenty camels, and according to Imam Zufar, only the zakat for the five camels is paid; the zakat for the remaining fifteen must be paid again. Imam Zufar's proof is that every nisab is an origin in itself with respect to zakat, so advancing zakat on the second nisab is like advancing it on the first nisab. And at the time of giving zakat, since the second nisab is not present, advancing zakat on it is in reality advancing the ruling before the cause, and that is not permissible. Therefore, we said that advancing zakat on the nisab that exists is permissible, but advancing it on what does not exist is not permissible. Our proof is that in causation, the first nisab is the origin, and that which exceeds it is subordinate to it. And due to the existence of the origin, its subordinate is also considered existent. So it will be said that at the time of giving zakat, when the first nisab exists, the other nisabs that are subordinate to it are also existent. And when the other nisabs are existent at the time of giving zakat, then advancing the ruling before the cause will not occur. And it is like a person who owns one nisab at the beginning of the year, then at the end of the year he acquires additional nisabs; then the year completes for the first nisab but not for the others; in that case it is said that it is as if the year completed for all nisabs, and paying zakat from the total becomes wajib. So similarly, the second nisab will be considered as present from the beginning of the year for the purpose of advancing zakat. And Allah the Exalted knows best. Jamil Ahmad Safi Allah.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on prepaying zakat before the completion of the haul (year). It begins by stating the Hanafi position: it is permissible to give zakat before the year ends as long as one possesses a nisab, because the cause of obligation (nisab) is present. This is analogized to expiation after wounding or performing prayer at the beginning of its time. Imam Malik opposes this, arguing that completion of the year is a condition like nisab, so advancing it is invalid. The Hanafi response clarifies that completion is a condition for the obligation of payment (wujub al-ada'), not for the permissibility; one may pay before it becomes wajib. The text then discusses prepayment for more than one year, citing the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (PBUH) accepted two years' zakat from Abbas. This establishes permissibility of multi-year advance payment. Finally, the passage addresses the case where one owns only one nisab but prepays zakat for multiple nisabs. Imam Zufar holds this invalid because each nisab is an independent cause; prepaying for a nonexistent nisab is advancing the ruling before the cause. The Hanafi response argues that in causation, the first nisab is the origin and subsequent nisabs are subordinate; with the origin present, subordinates are considered present as well. Thus, the prepayment covers the excess nisabs that are expected to be acquired later. An example is given: five camels initially, four goats given as zakat, then later fifteen more camels acquired; the prepaid goats cover all twenty. The lesson concludes with the preference for the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
تعجیل (ta'jil): Prepayment or advancing a payment before its due time, here referring to giving zakat before the end of the lunar year.
سبب وجوب (sabab al-wujub): The cause that triggers the obligation, here the possession of a complete nisab.
حولان حول (hawlan hawl): The completion of one full lunar year after possession of nisab, which is a condition for obligation of zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on prepaying zakat for multiple nisabs when currently only one nisab is owned?
A) It is not permissible because the other nisabs do not exist yet.
B) It is permissible because the first nisab is the origin and the excess is subordinate, considered present.
C) It is permissible only for the first nisab, not for the excess.
D) It is not permissible because Imam Zufar forbade it.

Key Takeaway
Prepaying zakat before the haul is permissible in the Hanafi school due to the existence of the nisab as the cause, and the haul is only a condition for the obligation to pay, not for the validity of the payment.

Defining Maal and the Order of Zakat Discussion
Chapter opening defining scope and ordering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'maal' as used in this chapter and state the two reasons why silver zakat is discussed before gold zakat.

Core Idea
Maal here excludes grazing animals; silver is mentioned first because it was the common currency.

This lesson opens the chapter on zakat of wealth (maal) after the chapter on zakat of grazing animals (saa'imah). The author clarifies that 'maal' in this context refers to non-livestock property, primarily gold, silver, and trade goods. He also explains why silver is given priority over gold in the discussion—a reflection of its practical importance in daily transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scope of 'Maal'
Understand that in this chapter, 'maal' means wealth other than grazing animals (saa'imah). It includes gold, silver, and trade goods (urud).
The chapter on saa'imah has already been covered.
2
Learn the General Definition of Maal
According to Imam Ahmad, maal is anything that people can own, such as dirhams, dinars, grains, animals, cloth, etc. But here the scope is limited.
This broad definition comes from another source, not directly from the Hidayah.
3
Understand the Exclusion of Saa'imah
Grazing animals were already discussed; this chapter covers all other zakatable wealth.
4
Recall the Two Reasons for Silver Preceding Gold
First, the Prophet's command (hadith) mentions zakat on silver before gold. Second, silver was more commonly used in transactions among the Arabs.
The author gives both a textual and a practical reason.
5
Connect to the Structure of the Hidayah
Note how the author arranges topics according to importance and textual order, a feature of Hanafi fiqh works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكوةِ الْمَالِ
ترجمہ یہ باب زکو و مال کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح عرب کے نزدیک سائمہ جانور چونکہ قیمتی مال شمار کیا جاتا تھا اس لئے اس کو مقدم کیا گیا۔ اب اس کے بیان سے فراغت کے بعد دوسرے اموال زکوۃ کا ذکر ہے ۔ امام احمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ مال ہر وہ چیز ہے جس کے لوگ مالک بن سکتے ہوں ۔ مثلاً در اہم دنا نیر گندم جو جانور کپڑ او غیر ولیکن اس جگہ مال سے مراد سوائم کے علاوہ ہے۔ چاندی کی زکوۃ پہلے بیان کی گئی ہے اور سونے کی بعد میں کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان میں چاندی کی زکوۃ کا ذکر پہلے ہے اور سونے کی زکوۃ کا بعد میں۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ چاندی چونکہ بکثرت متداول ہے اس لئے اس کو مقدم کیا گیا۔
Chapter on Zakat of Wealth. Translation: This chapter is about the discourse on zakat and wealth. Explanation: According to the Arabs, grazing animals were considered valuable wealth, therefore they were given precedence. Now, after finishing its discussion, the mention of other zakatable wealth is given. Imam Ahmad said: Al-maal (wealth) is everything that people can own, such as dirhams, dinars, wheat, barley, animals, cloth, etc. But here, by wealth is meant other than grazing animals. The zakat of silver was mentioned first and that of gold later, because in the order of the Prophet's (PBUH) command, the zakat of silver is mentioned first and the zakat of gold later. The second reason is that silver is commonly circulated, so it was given precedence.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This is the opening of a new chapter: 'Chapter on Zakat of Wealth (Maal)'. The author explains why, after discussing zakat on grazing animals (saa'imah), he now turns to other types of wealth. The term 'maal' is defined broadly by Imam Ahmad as anything that can be owned, including currency, grains, animals, and textiles. However, in this chapter, 'maal' refers specifically to non-livestock property (i.e., gold, silver, and trade goods). The text then explains why silver is discussed before gold: first, because the Prophet's (PBUH) hadith mentions silver zakat first; second, because silver was more commonly used in transactions among the Arabs. This ordering reflects the practical importance of silver as a medium of exchange. The lesson serves as a transitional and definitional introduction, setting the scope for the subsequent rulings on zakat on gold, silver, and trade goods.

Key Terms
مال (maal): Wealth; anything that people can own and possess. In this chapter, it specifically excludes grazing animals (saa'imah) and refers to gold, silver, and trade goods.
سائمہ (saa'imah): Grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep, goats) that feed on open pasture; their zakat rules were previously discussed.
زکوة (zakat): Obligatory charity on wealth, one of the Five Pillars of Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is silver zakat mentioned before gold zakat?
A) Because gold is more valuable.
B) Because silver is more commonly used in transactions.
C) Because the Prophet (PBUH) said silver is better.
D) Because gold zakat is not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The chapter on Zakat of Wealth defines 'maal' as non-livestock property and prioritizes silver over gold due to its textual order and practical prevalence.

Prepaying Zakat for Multiple Years: The Hanafi Position and Imam Zufar's Dispute
Ruling on advancing zakat for several years with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on prepaying zakat for multiple years and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar regarding the legal reasoning using the asl-tabi' principle.

Core Idea
Prepaying zakat is permissible because the first nisab is the principal and additional nisabs are subordinate.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on advancing zakat payments before the completion of the lunar year. The Hanafi school, based on a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and legal reasoning, allows prepayment for multiple years. However, Imam Zufar within the school dissents, arguing that each nisab is an independent cause, making prepayment for future nisabs invalid. We will walk through the evidence and analyze the reasoning that resolves this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
Identify the ruling from the Hidayah: prepaying zakat for more than one year is permissible. Note the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud as a primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
2
Identify Imam Zufar's objection and its proof
Imam Zufar argues that each nisab is an independent cause (sabab) for zakat. Prepaying for a non-existent nisab is applying the ruling (hukm) before the cause, which is invalid.
This is a methodological disagreement about the nature of the cause.
3
Analyze the Hanafi counter-argument using asl and tabi'
The Hanafi response: the first nisab is the principal (asl), and additional nisabs are subordinate (tabi'). Since the principal exists, the subordinates are considered existent by extension, so no advancement of hukm over sabab occurs.
This is an application of Hanafi usul: the subordinate follows the principal in legal existence.
4
Work through the illustrative example
Apply the reasoning to the example: a person with 5 camels gives 4 goats as zakat in advance, then acquires 15 more. According to the Hanafi school, the prepayment covers all 20; according to Imam Zufar, it covers only the first 5.
This example highlights the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position is the Hanafi permissibility. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that no additional zakat is required for the additional nisabs if prepayment was made.
Always check if the nisab exists at the time of payment.

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ایک سال سے زیادہ پر بھی زکوۃ مقدم کرنا جائز ہے یعنی اگر کوئی شخص چند سال کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ سب یعنی نصاب کامل موجود ہے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعودؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت عباس سے دو سال کی زکوۃ چیگی قبول کر لی تھی اس حدیث سے بھی ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ چند سال کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی کی ملک میں ایک ہی نصاب ہو۔ لیکن اس نے کئی نصابوں کی زکوۃ پیشگی دیدی تو جائز ہے۔ اس میں امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے۔ مثلا ایک آدمی کے پاس پانچ اونٹ ہیں۔ لیکن اس نے جولان حول سے پہلے چار بکریاں زکوۃ میں دید ہیں۔ پھر سال پورا ہوتے ہوتے اس کی ملک میں ہیں اونٹ ہو گئے ۔ تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ چار بکریاں کل یعنی میں اونٹ کی طرف سے ادا ہو گئیں اور امام زفر کے نزدیک صرف پانچ اونوں کی زکوۃ ادا ہوئی۔ باقی پندرہ کی زکوۃ دوبارہ ادا کرنا ضروری ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہر نصاب زکوۃ کے حق میں اصل بذاتہ ہے پس نصاب ثانی پر زکوۃ مقدم کرنا ایسا ہے جیسے نصاب اول پر مقدم کرنا ۔ اور زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت چونکہ نصاب ثانی موجود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر زکوۃ مقدم کرنا در حقیقت حکم کو سب پر مقدم کرنا ہے۔ اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ جو نصاب موجود ہے۔ اس کی زکوۃ مقدم کرنا تو جائز ہے لیکن جو موجود نہیں ہے اس کی زکوۃ کا مقدم کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ سبب ہونے میں نصاب اول ہی اصل ہے۔ اور جو اس پر زائد ہے وہ اس کے تابع ہے۔ اور اصل کے موجود ہونے سے اس کا تابع بھی موجود شمار کیا جاتا ہے اس کہا جائے گا کہ زکوۃ ادا کرتے وقت جب نصاب اول موجود ہے تو دوسرے نصاب جو اس کے تابع ہیں وہ بھی موجود ہیں ۔ اور جب دوسرے نصاب ادائیگی زکوۃ کے وقت موجود ہیں تو تقدیم حکم علی السبب بھی لازم نہ آئے گا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے ایک آدمی کے پاس سال کے شروع میں ایک نصاب ہے۔ پھر سال کے آخر میں اور نصاب حاصل ہو گئے ۔ پھر نصاب اول پر سال پورا ہو گیا اور باقی نصابوں پر پورا نہیں ہوا تو یہی کہا جاتا ہے کہ گویا تمام نصابوں پر سال پورا ہو گیا اور مجموعہ سے زکوۃ کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو گیا۔ پس اسی طرح نصاب ثانی کو تقدیم زکوۃ کے حق میں اول سال میں موجود شمار کیا جائے گا۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم جمیل احمد صفی اللہ
The author of Hidayah says: Prepaying zakat for more than one year is permissible. That is, if a person gives zakat in advance for several years, there is no harm. Because the complete nisab exists. Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA) said that the Prophet (SAW) accepted two years' zakat from Abbas (RA) in advance. This hadith shows that there is no harm in giving several years' zakat in advance. If a person owns only one nisab but gives zakat for several nisabs in advance, it is permissible. There is a difference of opinion with Imam Zufar. For example, a person has five camels and gives four goats as zakat before the year completes. Then by the end of the year, he owns twenty camels. According to us, these four goats suffice for all twenty camels. According to Imam Zufar, only the zakat for five camels is paid; zakat for the remaining fifteen must be paid again. Imam Zufar's proof: each nisab is a principal (asl) in itself regarding zakat; thus prepaying zakat for a second nisab is like prepaying for the first nisab. At the time of payment, the second nisab is not present; prepaying it is like applying the ruling before its cause, which is impermissible. Our proof: the first nisab is the principal (asl) in being the cause, and additional nisabs are subordinate (tabi'). Since the principal exists, the subordinate is considered existent. At the time of payment, when the first nisab exists, the other nisabs subordinate to it are also considered existent, so no advancement of ruling over cause occurs. This is similar to a person who has one nisab at the beginning of the year and acquires additional nisabs at the end; the year completes for the first nisab but not for the others. It is ruled that the year is considered complete for all, and zakat becomes wajib on the total. Similarly, for prepayment, the second nisab is considered as existing from the first year. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad Safiullah.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether zakat can be paid in advance for multiple years. The ruling from the base text (Hidayah) is that it is permissible to prepay zakat for several years, provided the complete nisab exists at the time of payment. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (SAW) accepted two years' zakat in advance from Abbas (RA). The author then presents an example to illustrate the principle and contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam Zufar. Imam Zufar argues that each nisab is an independent cause for zakat, so prepaying for a nisab not yet owned is applying the ruling before its cause, which is invalid. The Hanafi response is that when multiple nisabs exist, the first is the principal (asl) and the others are subordinate (tabi'), so they are considered existent by extension. Therefore, prepaying is not advancing the ruling before the cause because the cause (the nisab) is considered present. The same principle applies when multiple nisabs are acquired during the year: the year is considered complete for all, and zakat is due on the total. This reasoning supports the permissibility of prepaying zakat for multiple years.

Key Terms
تقدیم زکوۃ (taqdim al-zakat): Giving zakat before its due time, i.e., before completion of the lunar year (hawl).
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat.
تابع (tabi'): Something subordinate to the principal (asl); in this context, additional nisabs beyond the first are considered tabi'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, if a person has five camels and gives four goats as zakat in advance, then acquires fifteen more camels before the year completes, what is the ruling?
A) The zakat is valid only for the first five camels; additional zakat must be paid for the fifteen.
B) The zakat is valid for all twenty camels because the first nisab is principal and the rest are subordinate.
C) The prepayment is invalid because the year has not completed for any of the camels.
D) The prepayment is only valid if the person intends it for the first nisab only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits prepaying zakat for multiple years because the first nisab is principal and additional nisabs are subordinate.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Nisab of Silver and Dispute on Zakat for Excess
Ruling on zakat of silver with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on zakat of silver exceeding the nisab and apply them to calculate zakat on a given amount.

Core Idea
Zakat on silver is 2.5% of 200 dirhams, but how to calculate on excess differs: Abu Hanifa exempts fractions, while the Sahibayn apply proportional zakat.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn establishes the nisab of silver at 200 dirhams and the zakat rate of 5 dirhams. It then presents a critical intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on how to calculate zakat for amounts exceeding 200 dirhams. Understanding this dispute is essential for accurate zakat computation in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic ruling
Identify the nisab (200 dirhams) and the zakat rate (5 dirhams per 200) based on the hadith of Mu'adh and Mu'awiya. Note the definition of uqiya as 40 dirhams.
2
Identify the dispute scope
Recognize that the dispute concerns amounts exceeding 200 dirhams. Both sides agree on the basic ruling but differ on the excess.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on the excess until it reaches 40 dirhams. Then one dirham is due for each 40 dirhams, and fractions below 40 are exempt.
This is based on the hadith 'Do not take from fractions' and 'No sadaqah on less than forty'.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (and al-Shafi'i) hold that zakat is due proportionally on all excess at the rate of 2.5% (e.g., for every additional dirham, 2.5% zakat).
This is based on the hadith 'Whatever exceeds two hundred, it is according to its calculation'.
5
Evaluate the proofs and thamarah
Compare the hadith evidence and reasoning. Note the practical difference: e.g., on 250 dirhams, Abu Hanifa would give 6 dirhams (200 gives 5, excess 50 gives 1 for the first 40), while the Sahibayn would give 6.25 dirhams.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice is often the Sahibayn's proportional method.

تشریح عرب کے نزدیک سائمہ جانور چونکہ قیمتی مال شمار کیا جاتا تھا اس لئے اس کو مقدم کیا گیا۔ اب اس کے بیان سے فراغت کے بعد دوسرے اموال زکوۃ کا ذکر ہے ۔ امام احمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ مال ہر وہ چیز ہے جس کے لوگ مالک بن سکتے ہوں ۔ مثلاً در اہم دنا نیر گندم جو جانور کپڑ او غیر ولیکن اس جگہ مال سے مراد سوائم کے علاوہ ہے۔ چاندی کی زکوۃ پہلے بیان کی گئی ہے اور سونے کی بعد میں کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان میں چاندی کی زکوۃ کا ذکر پہلے ہے اور سونے کی زکوۃ کا بعد میں۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ چاندی چونکہ بکثرت متداول ہے اس لئے اس کو مقدم کیا گیا۔

دوسو درہم سے زائد میں زکوۃ کا حکم
قَالَ وَلَاشَى فِي الرِّيَادَةِ حَتَّى تُبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ فَيَكُونُ فِيهَا دِرْهُمْ ثُمَّ فِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَّا دِرُهُمْ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي
حَبِيْقَةً وَقَالَا مَازَادَ عَلَى الْمَانُتَيْنِ فَرَكَاتُهُ بِحِسَابِهَا وَهُوَ قُوْلُ الشَّافِعِي لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي حَدِيثِ وَمَازَادَ عَلَى الْمِائَتَيْنِ فَبِحِسَابِهِ وَلِأَنَّ الزَّكَوةَ وَحَبَيْتُ شُكْرًا لِنِعْمَةِ الْمَالِ وَاشْتِرَاطُ النِّصَابِ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ لِتَحْفَقِ الْغِنَاءِ وَبَعْدَ النِّصَابَ فِى السَّوَائِمِ تَحَرُّزًا عَنِ التَّشْقِيْصِ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ قَوْلَهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي حَدِيثٍ مُعَاذٍ لَا تَأْخُذُ مِنَ الْكُسُورِ شَنْيَا وَقَوْلُهُ فِي حَدِيثِ عَمْرِ وَبُنِ حَزْمٍ وَ لَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ الْأَرْبَعِينَ صَدَقَةً وَلانَّ الْحَرَجَ مَدْفُوعٌ وَ فِى إِيجَابِ الْكُسُورِ ذَلِكَ لِتَعَدّرِ الْوُقُوفِ وَالْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الدَّرَاهِم وَزْنُ سَبْعَةٍ وَهُوَ أَن تَكُونَ الْعَشْرَةَ مِنْهَا وَزْنُ سَبْعَةٍ مَتَاقِيلَ بِذلِكَ جَرَى التَّقْدَيرُ فِى دِبْرانِ عُمَرَ وَاسْتَقَرَّ الأمرُ عَلَيْهِ

ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ زیادتی میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ چالیس تک پہنچے تو اس میں ایک درہم ہوگا ۔ پھر ہر چالیس در ہم میں ایک درہم ہوگا۔ اور یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ دوسو پر جو کچھ بڑھے اس کی زکو 5 اس کے حساب سے ہے اور یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول حدیث علی میں ہے وَمَا زَادَ عَلَى الْمَائَتَيْنِ فَبِحِسَابِهِ اوران وَمَازَادَ
Chapter of Zakat of Wealth. Translation: This chapter is about zakat of wealth. Commentary: According to Arabs, grazing animals were considered valuable wealth, so they were given priority. After completing that discussion, other zakatable wealth is mentioned. Imam Ahmad said: Wealth is everything that people can own, e.g., dirhams, dinars, wheat, barley, animals, cloth, etc. But here, wealth means other than grazing animals. Zakat of silver is mentioned first, then gold, because in the Prophet's command, zakat of silver is mentioned first, then zakat of gold. Another reason is that silver is more widely circulated, so it was given priority.

Section on Silver. Translation: This section is about silver: its nisab and zakat amount. There is no zakat on less than two hundred dirhams because the Prophet (SAW) said: There is no zakat on less than five awaq. One uqiya is forty dirhams. So when it reaches two hundred and the year passes, five dirhams are due, because the Prophet (SAW) wrote to Mu'adh: Take from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams, and from every twenty mithqals of gold, half a mithqal.

Translation: There is no zakat on less than two hundred dirhams; when it reaches two hundred and a year passes, five dirhams are wajib. The proof is that the Prophet (SAW) wrote to Mu'awiya: Take five dirhams from every two hundred dirhams, and from every twenty mithqals of gold, half a mithqal.

Commentary: Uqiya is derived from waqaya meaning protection. Uqiya protects its owner from poverty and need. Plural is awaq. One uqiya is forty dirhams. The author said: The nisab of silver is two hundred dirhams. So on less than two hundred, no zakat is wajib. If silver reaches two hundred dirhams and a year passes, silver equivalent to five dirhams is wajib. The proof is that the Prophet (SAW) wrote to Mu'awiya: Take five dirhams from every two hundred dirhams, and half a mithqal from every twenty mithqals.

Ruling on silver exceeding two hundred dirhams: He (al-Quduri) said: There is nothing in the excess until it reaches forty, then one dirham is due, then for every forty dirhams one dirham. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Whatever exceeds two hundred, its zakat is calculated proportionally, and this is the statement of al-Shafi'i, due to the Prophet's statement in a hadith: And whatever exceeds two hundred, it is according to its calculation. And because zakat is gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and the condition of nisab at the beginning is to ensure sufficiency, and after nisab in grazing animals to avoid division. For Abu Hanifa is his statement in the hadith of Mu'adh: Do not take anything from fractions (kusur), and his statement in the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: There is no sadaqah on less than forty. And because hardship is avoided, and requiring zakat on fractions would entail impossibility. And the standard for dirhams is the weight of seven, meaning that ten of them should weigh seven mithqals. The estimation in the Diwan of Umar proceeded on this basis, and the matter became established.

Translation: Al-Quduri said: There is nothing wajib in the excess until it reaches forty, then one dirham is due, then for every forty dirhams one dirham. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said: Whatever exceeds two hundred, its zakat is according to its proportion, and this is the statement of al-Shafi'i, because the Prophet said: And whatever exceeds two hundred, it is according to its calculation, and...
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered discussion on zakat of silver, combining a chapter introduction, a definition of wealth, the basic ruling on silver nisab, and a significant intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on the calculation of zakat for amounts exceeding the nisab. The base text establishes that zakat on silver begins at 200 dirhams at a rate of 2.5% (5 dirhams). It explains the derivation of the nisab from the uqiya (40 dirhams) and cites the famous hadith of Mu'adh and Mu'awiya. The dispute arises on how to handle amounts beyond 200 dirhams. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that there is no zakat on the excess until it reaches an additional 40 dirhams, then one dirham is due, and then for every additional 40 dirhams, one dirham. This means increments below 40 are exempt. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Shafi'i hold that any amount above 200 is zakatable proportionally at 2.5%. The text provides proofs: Abu Hanifa cites the hadith of Mu'adh (do not take from fractions) and Amr ibn Hazm (no sadaqah on less than forty), while the Sahibayn cite the general hadith 'whatever exceeds two hundred is according to its calculation' and the principle that zakat is gratitude for wealth. The text also discusses the standard dirham weight: ten dirhams should weigh seven mithqals, established in Umar's Diwan.

Key Terms
اوقیہ (uqiya): A unit of weight equal to 40 dirhams, used to determine the nisab of silver.
كسور (kusur): Fractions or small amounts of property that do not reach a complete nisab increment (e.g., less than 40 dirhams).
وزن سبعة (wazn sab'ah): The standard weight of a dirham: 10 dirhams should weigh 7 mithqals (approx. 2.975 g).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how is zakat calculated on 230 dirhams of silver?
A) 5.75 dirhams (proportional 2.5% of 230)
B) 5 dirhams (only on 200, because excess 30 is less than 40)
C) 6 dirhams (5 on 200 + 1 on the next 40, but 30 is less than 40 so no)
D) 5.5 dirhams (half of 5 plus something)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on zakat of excess silver: incremental per 40 dirhams (Abu Hanifa) and proportional (Sahibayn); the mufta bihi is proportional.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Nisab of Silver and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Excess Zakat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of silver excess with dalil naqli and rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on zakat of silver excess and explain the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
No zakat on excess silver until it forms a full nisab of 40 dirhams — Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.

You already know that zakat is wajib on 200 dirhams of silver. But what happens when you have 220 dirhams? Do you pay zakat on just the first 200, or on the entire 220? This seemingly small question generated a deep intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two great students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Both sides bring strong proofs. Let's work through the arguments and see why the school ultimately follows Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed-upon base ruling
Identify the nisab of silver (200 dirhams) and the zakat amount (5 dirhams per 200) from the matn. Note that this is not disputed.
This is from the hadith of Mu'adh and the five awaq tradition.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Locate where al-Quduri states Abu Hanifa's view: no zakat on excess until 40 dirhams. Contrast with 'Qala' (they said) referring to the Sahibayn: proportional zakat on any excess.
The dispute is about amounts between 200 and 240 dirhams.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Read their dalil: the hadith of 'Ali ('whatever exceeds, proportion') and the rational argument that zakat is gratitude for wealth, and any increase is wealth.
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Examine his proofs: the hadith of Mu'adh ('do not take from fractions'), the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm ('no sadaqah on less than forty'), and the principle that hardship is repelled.
He also interprets the hadith of 'Ali as referring to a full nisab increment.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Calculate the practical difference: 220 dirhams → 5 dirhams (Abu Hanifa) vs. 5.5 dirhams (Sahibayn). Note that the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view due to stronger dalil and ease.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ مِانَتِى دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامِ لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةٌ وَالأُوقِيَةُ أَرْبَعُونَ درْهُما فَإِذَا كَانَتْ مِائَتَيْنِ وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَوْلُ فَفَيهَا خَمْسَةٌ دَرَاهِمَ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَتَبَ إِلَى مُعَادٍ أَنْ خُذْ مِنْ كُلّ مِانَتَى دِرْهَم خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَمِنْ كُلِّ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا مِنْ ذَهَبٍ نَصْفَ مِثْقَالِ

گئے تو ان چار اونٹوں کی زکوۃ ایک بکری کے پانچ
There is no sadaqah on less than two hundred dirhams, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq,' and the uqiyya is forty dirhams. So when they reach two hundred and a year has passed over them, then five dirhams are due, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) wrote to Mu'adh: 'Take from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams, and from every twenty mithqals of gold half a mithqal.' He (al-Quduri) said: 'And there is nothing in the excess until it reaches forty, then one dirham is due, and then one dirham for every forty dirhams. This is according to Abu Hanifa. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Whatever exceeds the two hundred, its zakat is according to its proportion, and that is the saying of al-Shafi'i, due to his saying (peace be upon him) in the hadith: 'And whatever exceeds two hundred, then its zakat is according to its proportion,' and because zakat became obligatory as gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and the condition of nisab in the beginning is to achieve the criterion of being wealthy, and after the nisab, the nisab is considered only in grazing animals to avoid fragmentation. And according to Abu Hanifa is his saying (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take anything from the fractions,' and his saying in the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'And there is no sadaqah on less than forty,' and because difficulty is repelled, and in making fractions obligatory that (difficulty) would occur due to the difficulty of assessing them. And the weight considered in dirhams is the weight of seven, meaning that ten of them should weigh seven mithqals. By that the assessment was made in the register of 'Umar, and the matter became settled.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the zakat on silver exceeding the nisab of 200 dirhams, with the matn from al-Quduri and the sharh from the author. The passage begins by establishing the basic ruling: zakat is not due on less than 200 dirhams of silver, based on the hadith that there is no sadaqah on less than five awaq (each uqiyya = 40 dirhams). When one possesses 200 dirhams for a full lunar year, 5 dirhams (2.5%) are due. This is supported by the Prophet's letter to Mu'adh instructing him to take 5 dirhams from every 200 dirhams. The text then transitions to the ruling on amounts exceeding 200 dirhams. Al-Quduri states: 'There is nothing in the excess until it reaches forty, then one dirham is due, and then for every forty dirhams one dirham.' This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: no zakat is due on the excess between 200 and 240 dirhams; the excess does not trigger zakat until it itself reaches a full nisab of 40 dirhams. After that, each additional 40 dirhams require 1 dirham. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They hold that any excess beyond 200 dirhams, however small, incurs zakat proportionally. So if one has 201 dirhams, one pays 5 dirhams plus the proportional share of 1/40 of a dirham (0.025 dirham). They cite the hadith: 'And whatever exceeds two hundred, then its zakat is according to its proportion' (from the hadith of 'Ali). They also argue that zakat is gratitude for the blessing of wealth, and any increase is wealth; requiring a full nisab increment is arbitrary. The Sahibayn's argument is further defended against an objection: if zakat is for gratitude, why require a nisab at all? The answer is that zakat is only on the wealthy, and the nisab is the threshold for being considered wealthy (ghina). The Sahibayn then clarify that the nisab condition is only at the beginning; once one is wealthy, any additional wealth is also subject to zakat. However, this reasoning seems to contradict the ruling for grazing animals (sawa'im), where excess beyond the nisab does not incur zakat until it reaches another nisab. The Sahibayn explain that this is to avoid fragmentation (tashqis) in assessing zakat on animals. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof includes the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take anything from the fractions (kusur),' and the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty.' He also argues that making fractions obligatory would lead to hardship (haraj) in accurately assessing small amounts. The passage concludes by stating that the standard weight for dirhams is 'wazn sab'ah' (weight of seven), meaning ten dirhams should weigh seven mithqals, as established in the register of 'Umar. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, that no zakat is due on amounts between 200 and 240 dirhams. This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat liability; for silver, 200 dirhams.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin; the standard dirham used in zakat is one weighing 2.97 grams (approx), with 10 dirhams equaling 7 mithqals (weight of seven).
اوقية (uqiyya): A measure of weight equal to 40 dirhams; five awaq equal 200 dirhams.
كسور (kusur): Fractions or increments; in this context, amounts between the nisab and the next full nisab increment (e.g., between 200 and 240 dirhams).
وزن سبعة (wazn sab'ah): The standard weight for dirhams: ten dirhams weigh seven mithqals (each mithqal approx 4.25g).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the zakat due on 220 dirhams of silver held for one year?
A) 5.5 dirhams (proportional for the excess)
B) 5 dirhams (only on the first 200, excess exempt)
C) 6 dirhams (since 20 dirhams is half of 40)
D) No zakat (since 220 is less than 240)

Key Takeaway
Zakat on silver is due on the nisab of 200 dirhams, but according to the Hanafi mufta bihi, no zakat is due on excess amounts until they reach a full nisab increment of 40 dirhams.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Zakat on Surplus: Dispute Between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Dispute over zakat obligation on fractional surplus after nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on zakat for surplus above 200 dirhams, identify their proofs, and calculate the practical difference.

Core Idea
Zakat on fractional surplus is not due until the surplus reaches a full nisab (40 dirhams) — Imam Abu Hanifa's view to avoid hardship.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about zakat on amounts exceeding the nisab of 200 dirhams. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on the excess unless it reaches 40 dirhams, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that any excess, however small, incurs zakat proportionally. We will explore their proofs and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of disagreement
Determine exactly when zakat becomes obligatory on the surplus over 200 dirhams: does it require a full 40 dirhams or any amount?
Focus on amounts between 200 and 240 dirhams.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Examine the hadith of Ali and the rational argument that zakat is thankfulness for wealth, so any increase is wealth.
The hadith of Ali: 'Whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams, its zakat is to be paid according to its calculation.'
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
Study the hadiths of Mu'adh (do not take from fractions) and Amr ibn Hazm (no sadaqah on less than 40), plus the hardship argument.
The hardship of calculating fractions for the common person is a key rational proof.
4
Understand the resolution of conflict
See how the hadith of Ali is interpreted to mean an increase of at least 40 dirhams, removing the apparent contradiction with Amr ibn Hazm.
The Hanafi tarjih (preference) rests on the strength of the hadiths and the removal of hardship.
5
Calculate the practical difference
Apply both views to a concrete amount (e.g., 201 dirhams) and note the difference in zakat due.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the dispute).

مقصد نعمت مال کا شکر ادا کرنا ہے تو مطلق مال میں زکوۃ واجب ہونی چاہئے، خواہ مال بقدر نصاب ہو یا اس سے کم ہو۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ زکو اغنیاء پرواجب ہوتی ہے نہ کہ فقراء پر چنانچہ رسول برحق صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد ہے خُذُوا مِنْ أَغْنِيَائِهِم وَتَرُ دُوا إلى فُقَرَائِهِمُ ' پس منی اور فقیر کے درمیان امتیاز کرنے کے لئے مقدار نصاب کو فاصل قرار دیا گیا ہے یعنی مقدار نصاب سے مالک کے لئے فنی حاصل ہو جائے گا اور اس سے کم سے غنی حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ مغنی ثابت کرنے کے لئے ابتداء میں نصاب کو شرط قراردیا گیا ہے۔ اور مازاد علی المائتین میں زیادتی سے غنی کی زیادتی مراد ہے۔ اور منی میں زیادتی قلیل دکثیر دونوں سے حاصل ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ مقدار نصاب پر جو مقدار بھی زائد ہوگی اس میں اس کے حساب سے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ لیکن اب سوال ہوگا کہ سوائم کے اندر نصاب کے بعد مطلقاً زیادتی میں زکوۃ کیوں واجب نہیں کی گئی۔ مثلاً پانچ اونٹوں میں ایک بکری ہے اب اگر اس پر چار اونٹوں کا اضافہ ہو گیا تو اس اضافہ میں کوئی زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے تا وقتیکہ یہ انصافہ مقدار نصاب کو نہ پہنچ جائے اور اونٹ دس ہو جائیں تو ان میں دو بکریاں واجب ہوں گی ۔ جواب: سوائم میں نصاب کے بعد مطلقاً زیادتی میں وجوب نہ ہو نا ٹکڑے کرنے سے بچاؤ کے لئے ہے۔ یعنی اگر پانچ اونوں پر مثلاً چار اونٹ بڑھ گئے تو ان چار اونٹوں کی زکوۃ ایک بکری کے پانچ

۔
دوسری دلیل عمرو بن حزم کی حدیث ہے حدیث یہ ہے لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ الْأَرْبَعِينَ صَدَقَةٌ یعنی چالیس سے کم میں زکو انہیں ہے بلکہ چالیس درہم میں ایک درہم ہے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ یہ حکم دو سو درہم کے بعد کا ہے یعنی دو سو درہم کے بعد چالیس درہم سے کم میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ البتہ چالیس درہم میں زکوۃ ہے کیونکہ دو سو درہم سے پہلے پہلے نہ چالیس درہم میں زکوۃ ہے اور نہ چالیس سے کم میں زکوۃ ہے۔ رہا یہ سوال کی عمرو بن حزم کی حدیث حدیث علی فَإِذَا زَادَ عَلَى الْمَائِتَيْنِ کے معارض ہو گئی ہے کیونکہ حدیث علی میں ہے کہ مطلقا زیادتی پر زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ اور حدیث عمرو بن حزم میں ہے کہ دو سو درہم پر اگر چالیس درہم زائد ہوں تو زیادتی میں زکوۃ واجب ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں حدیثوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حدیث علی میں جہاں یہ احتمال ہے کہ مطلقاً زیادتی مراد ہے۔ وہیں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ دوسو پر زیادتی سے مراد چالیس درہم کی زیادتی ہو پس احتمال ثانی مراد لینے کی صورت میں دونوں روایتوں میں کوئی تعارض باقی نہ رہے گا۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرج تو شرعا دور کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ کسور کے اندر زکوۃ واجب کرنے میں یہ حرج موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ کسور کے حساب پر واقف ہونا مستعد رہے مثلا ایک شخص کی ملک میں دوسوسات در اہم ہیں اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس پر دو سو درہم کے پانچ درہم اور سات درہم کی زکوۃ ایک درہم کے چالیس ٹکڑوں میں سے سات ٹکڑے واجب ہوئے۔ پس زکوۃ نکال کر اس کے پاس ایک درہم کے ۳۳ ٹکرے اور دو سو ایک درہم باقی رہے اگر اس پر دوسرا سال گذر گیا تو دو سو درہم میں پانچ درہم واجب ہوں گے اور ایک درہم میں اس کا چالیسواں حصہ واجب ہو گیا اور ۳۳ ٹکڑوں میں اس کا چالیسواں حصہ واجب ہوگا۔ اب آپ غور کیجئے کہ ۳۳ ٹکڑوں میں سے حساب لگا کر چالیسواں حصہ نکالنا کس قدر دشوار ہے بلکہ ہم جیسوں کے لئے ناممکن ہے پس ان بے پڑھے لکھے لوگوں کا کیا حال ہوگا جو سو سے اوپر گنتی نہیں جانتے ۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے اسی حرج اور دقت کو دور کرنے کے لئے فرمایا ہے کہ کسور میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی نہ بلکہ دوسو پر اگر چالیس درہم زائد ہوں تو ان میں زکوۃ واجب ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ زکوۃ کے نصاب مہر اور صدقۃ الفطر اور سرقہ کے نصاب کے بارے میں دراہم میں وزن سبعہ معتبر ہے۔ وزن سبعہ یہ ہے کہ دس درہم سات مثقال کے وزن کے برابر ہوں اس کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ابتداء میں تین قسم کے دراہم تھے۔ (۱) وزن عشره، (۲) وزن سته ، (۳) وزن خمسہ وزن عشرہ تو یہ ہے کہ دس درہم دس مثقال کے برابر ہوں وزن ستہ یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کچھ مثقال کے برابر ہوں اور وزن خمسہ یہ ہے کہ دس درہم پانچ مثقال کے برابر ہوں۔ ان تینوں اوزان میں وزن عشر ہ سب سے عمدہ ہے اور وزن خمسہ سب سے کمتر ہے لوگوں کا تینوں پر عمل تھا تینوں اور ان کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے تھے جب حضرت عمر خلیفہ مقرر ہوئے تو آپ نے چاہا کہ زکوۃ اور
Book of Zakat. 84. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Three: ... because zakat is obligatory as a thank-offering for the blessing of wealth, and stipulating nisab at the beginning is unanimously for the purpose of richness. And in grazing livestock, the condition after nisab is to avoid fragmentation. And the proof of Abu Hanifa is that in the hadith of Mu'adh, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not take anything from fractions (kusur).' And in the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty.' And also because hardship is removed by Sharia, while making fractions obligatory involves hardship, because one must be acquainted with the calculation of fractions. And regarding dirhams, the weight of seven (wazn sab'ah) is considered. Wazn sab'ah is that ten dirhams equal the weight of seven mithqals. In this manner, estimation was conducted in the bureau of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and this matter became settled. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: If there is an increase over two hundred dirhams, zakat is not obligatory on the increase unless the increase reaches the amount of forty dirhams. Thus, if there are two hundred and forty dirhams, six dirhams are obligatory. Then for every forty, one dirham remains obligatory. This is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: Absolutely, zakat is obligatory on the increase, whether it is little or much. Thus, if two hundred dirhams are increased by one dirham, then besides five dirhams, one-fortieth of one dirham is also obligatory. This is also the saying of Imam Shafi'i. The proof of the Sahibayn is that at the end of the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams, its zakat is to be paid according to its calculation.' The second proof is that zakat is obligatory as a thank-offering for the blessing of wealth, and whatever exceeds two hundred dirhams is all wealth, whether the excess is forty dirhams or less; thus, a thank-offering proportionate to the calculation is obligatory in that excess. And 'washtirat al-nisab...' etc. is the response to an objection raised against the rational proof presented by the Sahibayn, 'wa lian al-zakat...' The substance of the objection is: If zakat is obligatory to give thanks for the blessing of wealth, then why is nisab stipulated at the beginning? Because just as wealth exists to the extent of nisab, similarly wealth exists below nisab. So if the purpose of the obligation of zakat is to give thanks for the blessing of wealth, then zakat should be obligatory on all wealth, whether the wealth is to the extent of nisab or less. The answer is that zakat is obligatory on the rich, not on the poor, as the true Messenger said: 'Take from their rich and give to their poor.' So to distinguish between the rich and the poor, the amount of nisab was made the dividing line; that is, with the amount of nisab, the owner attains richness, and with less than that, richness is not attained. The conclusion is that to establish richness, nisab is stipulated at the beginning. And in 'ma zad ala al-mi'atayn', the intended increase is the increase of richness. And richness is attained by both a little and a large increase. Therefore, we said that whatever amount exceeds nisab, zakat is obligatory on it according to its calculation. But now a question arises: In grazing livestock, after nisab, why is zakat not made obligatory absolutely on the increase? For example, for five camels, one goat is due. Now if four camels are added to them, no zakat is obligatory on this increase until this addition reaches the amount of nisab, and the camels become ten; then two goats will be obligatory. Answer: In grazing livestock, the reason for not making zakat obligatory absolutely on the increase after nisab is to avoid fragmentation. That is, if four camels are added to five camels, the zakat of those four camels would be four-fifths of one goat, and in that case, even if it is in terms of value, cutting the goat would become necessary. Therefore, to avoid this harm, in grazing livestock, zakat is not made obligatory absolutely on the increase after nisab; rather, if the increase is to the extent of nisab, then zakat is obligatory, e.g., if five camels are added to five, then two goats become obligatory. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that when the Messenger of Allah sent Mu'adh as governor of Yemen, he said: 'Do not take anything from fractions; rather, take one full dirham for forty, and since less than forty is a fraction, do not take half, third, etc. from less than forty.' The second proof is the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty,' meaning there is no zakat on less than forty; rather, on forty dirhams, one dirham is due. It should be noted that this ruling is after two hundred dirhams; i.e., after two hundred dirhams, there is no zakat on less than forty dirhams. However, on forty dirhams, zakat is due, because before two hundred dirhams, neither forty dirhams nor less than forty have zakat. As for the question that the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm conflicts with the hadith of Ali 'fa idha zad ala al-mi'atayn', because the hadith of Ali says that zakat is obligatory on any increase absolutely, and the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm says that on two hundred dirhams, if forty dirhams are added, zakat is obligatory, otherwise not. The answer is that there is no conflict between these two hadiths, because the hadith of Ali, while it might imply absolute increase, also has the possibility that the increase meant is specifically an increase of forty dirhams. So, if the second possibility is taken, no conflict remains between the two narrations. The rational proof is that hardship is removed by Sharia, while making zakat obligatory on fractions involves hardship, because one must be acquainted with the calculation of fractions. For example, a person owns two hundred and seven dirhams. According to the Sahibayn, on two hundred dirhams, five dirhams are due, and on the seven dirhams, seven-fortieths of one dirham are due. After paying zakat, he would have thirty-three parts of one dirham and two hundred and one dirhams remaining. If another year passes, on two hundred dirhams, five dirhams become due, on one dirham, its fortieth part becomes due, and on the thirty-three parts, their fortieth part becomes due. Consider how difficult it is to calculate the fortieth part from thirty-three parts—impossible for the likes of us. Then what about the illiterate who cannot count beyond a hundred? Imam Abu Hanifa, to remove this hardship and difficulty, ruled that zakat is not obligatory on fractions; rather, on two hundred, if forty dirhams are added, zakat is obligatory on them. The author of Hidayah says: Regarding the nisab of zakat, mahr, sadaqat al-fitr, and theft, the weight of seven (wazn sab'ah) is considered for dirhams. Wazn sab'ah is that ten dirhams equal the weight of seven mithqals. Its investigation is that initially there were three types of dirham weights: (1) wazn ashara, (2) wazn sitta, (3) wazn khamsa. Wazn ashara: ten dirhams equal ten mithqals; wazn sitta: ten dirhams equal six mithqals; wazn khamsa: ten dirhams equal five mithqals. Among these three weights, wazn ashara is the best and wazn khamsa is the lowest. People practiced with all three and traded with them. When Umar became caliph, he wanted that zakat and...
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and an expansion of the ruling on zakat for surplus (zawa'id) after the nisab of 200 dirhams. The text first presents the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: no zakat on any increase unless it reaches a full nisab of 40 dirhams. So at 240 dirhams, zakat is 6 dirhams; at 241, still 6 dirhams because the extra 1 dirham is less than 40. This is based on hadiths commanding not to take zakat from fractions (kusur) and that there is no sadaqah on less than 40. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that zakat is due on any increase, however small, proportionally. Their proof is the hadith of Ali that any increase over 200 is subject to zakat according to its amount, and the rational argument that zakat is thankfulness for wealth, so any increase is wealth. The text then responds to an objection: if zakat is thankfulness, why is nisab required? The answer: zakat is on the rich, and nisab is the threshold for richness (ghina), established by the hadith 'Take from their rich.' The text then distinguishes grazing livestock (sawa'im) where zakat on fractional increases is waived to avoid fragmentation (tukre tukre) of the animal. Then it elaborates Imam Abu Hanifa's proofs: the hadith of Mu'adh and the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm, and a rational proof based on hardship (haraj) in calculating fractions. It resolves the apparent conflict between the hadith of Ali and the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm by interpreting Ali's hadith to refer to an increase of at least 40 dirhams. Finally, it introduces the standard of wazn sab'ah for dirhams used in zakat nisab, mahr, sadaqat al-fitr, and theft, explaining that Umar standardized this weight, which means 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals, and traces the earlier three weight standards. The passage clearly establishes the Hanafi position with its proofs and answers the opponents.

Key Terms
كسور (kusur): Fractions or incomplete units of the nisab, e.g., amounts less than the full nisab increment.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth liable for zakat, which for silver is 200 dirhams (or equivalent).
سوائم (sawa'im): Grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep, goats) that are kept for milk, breeding, or meat and graze on open land most of the year.
وزن سبعہ (wazn sab'ah): The standard weight of dirhams where 10 dirhams equal 7 mithqals (approx. 2.97 grams per dirham).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 5 dirhams
B) 5.5 dirhams
C) 5 dirhams + 20/40 dirham
D) 6 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that zakat on surplus is not due until the surplus reaches a full nisab of 40 dirhams, based on hadith and to prevent hardship.
