Zakat on Fractional Amounts (Kusr): The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for fractional excess over nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on zakat for fractional amounts and apply the madhhab's tarjih method to resolve intra-school ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Within the Hanafi school, the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa disagree on zakat for fractional excess, but the mufta bihi follows the Imam's view based on explicit hadith and the principle of removing hardship.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), on whether zakat is due on fractional amounts of wealth that exceed the nisab of 200 dirhams but are less than an additional complete nisab (40 dirhams). The disagreement has practical implications for calculating zakat on savings that fall between these thresholds. By studying the proofs and the Hanafi school's method of resolving differences, you will learn not only the ruling but also how the school prioritises explicit textual evidence and the removal of hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and the Two Positions
State the point of dispute: whether zakat is wajib on fractional excess (kusr) less than 40 dirhams above 200 dirhams. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is not wajib; the Sahibayn hold it is.
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams; zakat on that is 5 dirhams (2.5%). The dispute concerns additional amounts, e.g., 30 dirhams extra.
2
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's Dalil
Read the two hadith cited: the Prophet's instruction to Mu'adh (RA) 'Do not take anything from fractions' and the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty dirhams'. Understand how these explicitly exempt fractions from zakat.
Also note the rational argument of hardship (haraj) in calculating fractions.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's Dalil
Identify the opposing proof: the hadith of Ali (RA) 'When it exceeds two hundred, calculate accordingly'. The Sahibayn interpret this to mean any increase, however small, incurs zakat proportionally.
This hadith is less specific than Abu Hanifa's proofs.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response and Resolution
Understand the author's resolution: the hadith of Ali is ambiguous; it may mean the increase must reach a full nisab (40 dirhams). Hence no contradiction. The explicit hadith and hardship principle favour Abu Hanifa's view.
This is a classic case of tarjih (preference) within the school.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
Calculate the practical difference: e.g., on 230 dirhams, Abu Hanifa: 5 dirhams; Sahibayn: 5.75 dirhams. Identify that the mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) is Imam Abu Hanifa's position.
The school's tarjih authority (e.g., Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) supports this.

پہلے پہلے نہ چالیس درہم میں زکوۃ ہے اور نہ چالیس سے کم میں زکوۃ ہے۔ رہا یہ سوال کی عمرو بن حزم کی حدیث حدیث علی فَإِذَا زَادَ عَلَى الْمَائِتَيْنِ کے معارض ہو گئی ہے کیونکہ حدیث علی میں ہے کہ مطلقا زیادتی پر زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ اور حدیث عمرو بن حزم میں ہے کہ دو سو درہم پر اگر چالیس درہم زائد ہوں تو زیادتی میں زکوۃ واجب ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں حدیثوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حدیث علی میں جہاں یہ احتمال ہے کہ مطلقاً زیادتی مراد ہے۔ وہیں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ دوسو پر زیادتی سے مراد چالیس درہم کی زیادتی ہو پس احتمال ثانی مراد لینے کی صورت میں دونوں روایتوں میں کوئی تعارض باقی نہ رہے گا۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حرج تو شرعا دور کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ کسور کے اندر زکوۃ واجب کرنے میں یہ حرج موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ کسور کے حساب پر واقف ہونا مستعد رہے مثلا ایک شخص کی ملک میں دوسوسات در اہم ہیں لگا کر چالیسواں حصہ نکالنا کس قدر دشوار ہے بلکہ ہم جیسوں کے لئے ناممکن ہے پس ان بے پڑھے لکھے لوگوں کا کیا حال ہوگا جو سو سے اوپر گنتی نہیں جانتے ۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے اسی حرج اور دقت کو دور کرنے کے لئے فرمایا ہے کہ کسور میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی نہ بلکہ دوسو پر اگر چالیس درہم زائد ہوں تو ان میں زکوۃ واجب ہے۔
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he sent Mu'adh as governor of Yemen said: 'Do not take anything from fractions (kusr).' That is, do not take anything in fractions, but at forty (dirhams) take one dirham fully, and what is less than forty is a fraction, so do not take half, one-third, etc. The second proof is the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty (dirhams).' That is, there is no zakat on less than forty, but on forty dirhams there is one dirham. Note that this ruling is after two hundred dirhams. That is, after two hundred dirhams, there is no zakat on less than forty dirhams. However, on forty dirhams there is zakat, because before two hundred dirhams, there is no zakat on forty dirhams nor on less than forty. As for the question that the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm conflicts with the hadith of Ali: 'And when it increases beyond two hundred (dirhams),' because the hadith of Ali states that zakat is due on any increase absolutely, while the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm states that on two hundred dirhams, if forty dirhams are added, then zakat is due on the increase, otherwise not. The answer is that there is no contradiction between these two hadith. Because in the hadith of Ali, there is a possibility that absolute increase is meant, but there is also a possibility that the increase beyond two hundred means an increase of forty dirhams. If the second possibility is taken as the intended meaning, then there is no contradiction remaining between the two narrations. The rational proof is that hardship (haraj) has been removed by Shari'ah, while imposing zakat on fractions involves hardship. Because being aware of the calculation of fractions is troublesome. For example, if a person owns 207 dirhams, according to the Sahibayn, on the two hundred dirhams five dirhams are due, and on the seven dirhams, seven parts of forty parts of a dirham are due. After paying zakat, he has 33 pieces of one dirham and 201 dirhams remaining. If the second year passes, on the two hundred dirhams five dirhams are due, on the one dirham its fortieth part is due, and on the 33 pieces their fortieth part is due. Consider how difficult it is to calculate the fortieth part of 33 pieces, indeed impossible for someone like us. What then of the illiterate who cannot count beyond one hundred? Imam Abu Hanifa, to remove this hardship and difficulty, ruled that zakat is not due on fractions, but only when forty dirhams are added to two hundred, then zakat is due on that addition.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding whether zakat is due on fractional amounts (kusr) that are less than a full nisab (40 dirhams) above the initial nisab of 200 dirhams. The author, Ashraf Ul Hadaya, first presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proofs. The first is the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal (RA) in which the Prophet (SAW) instructed not to take zakat on fractions. The second is the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm that there is no sadaqah on less than 40 dirhams. Then the text addresses a potential objection: that the hadith of Ali (RA) 'When it increases beyond two hundred, calculate accordingly' seems to command zakat on any excess, contradicting the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm. The author resolves this by noting that the hadith of Ali is ambiguous; it may mean that the excess must reach a complete nisab (i.e., 40 dirhams) to incur zakat. Thus there is no real contradiction. Finally, a rational argument (dalil 'aqli) is given: imposing zakat on fractions would cause extreme hardship (haraj) in calculation, especially for the common people. Since the Shari'ah removes hardship, zakat is not imposed on fractions. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that zakat is only due on fractional excess when it reaches a full nisab of 40 dirhams. This is the relied-upon position in the school.

Key Terms
كسور (kusr): Fractional amounts of dirhams or other wealth that do not make up a full nisab (40 dirhams) above the base nisab of 200 dirhams.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that must be possessed for zakat to become obligatory. For silver, it is 200 dirhams (according to the weight standard discussed later).

Key Takeaway
Zakat on fractional amounts (kusr) above the nisab is not wajib according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, because explicit hadith and the principle of removing hardship require the fractional excess to reach a complete nisab (40 dirhams) before additional zakat becomes due.

Standard Dirham Weight for Zakat Nisab (Wazan Sab'ah)
Determination of standard dirham weight for zakat and other nisabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi standard dirham weight (10 dirhams = 7 mithqals) and explain how it was derived through the consensus of the Companions.

Core Idea
The nisab for zakat is measured by the weight of sab'ah: ten dirhams equal seven mithqals, established by consensus.

The correct weight of the dirham is essential for determining the nisab threshold for zakat, mahr, sadaqat al-fitr, and theft penalties. This lesson traces the historical derivation of the standard weight ('wazan sab'ah') from three pre-existing weights under the authority of Caliph Umar and the Companions' consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scope
Note that the weight standard applies to the nisab of zakat, mahr, sadaqat al-fitr, and sariqa (theft). Understand that this is a definitional ruling defining the measure of wealth.
The weight is not arbitrary; it has a historical and legal basis.
2
Understand the historical derivation
Recognize that there were three pre-existing dirham weights: wazan 'asharah (10 dirhams = 10 mithqals), wazan sittah (10 dirhams = 6 mithqals), and wazan khamsah (10 dirhams = 5 mithqals). Caliph Umar sought a moderate weight.
The accountants averaged the three: (10+6+5)/3 = 7 mithqals per 10 dirhams.
3
Confirm the legal authority
The resulting weight (wazan sab'ah) was adopted by Caliph Umar and gained consensus (ijma') of the Companions. This ijma' makes it authoritative in the Hanafi school.
Ijma' is a primary source of law; thus the weight is binding.
4
Apply to nisab calculation
The zakat nisab for silver is 200 dirhams of this standard weight. This equates to 200 dirhams × (7 mithqals/10 dirhams) = 140 mithqals. Using the approximation of 1 mithqal = 4.25 grams, the nisab is about 595 grams of silver.
This weight is used consistently across all relevant chapters.

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ زکوۃ کے نصاب مہر اور صدقۃ الفطر اور سرقہ کے نصاب کے بارے میں دراہم میں وزن سبعہ معتبر ہے۔ وزن سبعہ یہ ہے کہ دس درہم سات مثقال کے وزن کے برابر ہوں اس کی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ابتداء میں تین قسم کے دراہم تھے۔ (۱) وزن عشره، (۲) وزن سته ، (۳) وزن خمسہ وزن عشرہ تو یہ ہے کہ دس درہم دس مثقال کے برابر ہوں وزن ستہ یہ ہے کہ دس درہم کچھ مثقال کے برابر ہوں اور وزن خمسہ یہ ہے کہ دس درہم پانچ مثقال کے برابر ہوں۔ ان تینوں اوزان میں وزن عشر ہ سب سے عمدہ ہے اور وزن خمسہ سب سے کمتر ہے لوگوں کا تینوں پر عمل تھا تینوں اور ان کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے تھے جب حضرت عمر خلیفہ مقرر ہوئے تو آپ نے چاہا کہ زکوۃ اور خراج عمد دوزن عشرہ کے ساتھ وصول کریں اور لوگوں نے اس میں تخفیف چاہی تو خلیفہ المسلمین سید نا عمر فاروق نے اپنے زمانے کے حساب داں، ان کو جمع فرمایا تا کہ وہ ان اوزان ثلاثہ کو سامنے رکھ کر درمیانی وزن متعین کریں جس میں دونوں کی رعایت ملحوظ ہو۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے تینوں اور ان کے مثاقبیل کو اکٹھا کیا تو وہ اکیس ہوئے ۔ اور وزن چونکہ تین ہیں اس لئے اکیس مثاقیل کو جب تین پر تقسیم کیا گیا تو ایک حصہ میں سات مثقال آئے یعنی درمیانی وزن یہ نکلا کہ دس درہم سات مثقال کے برابر ہوں ۔ اسی کو وزن سبعہ کہا جاتا ہے اسی پر صحابہ کا اجماع ہوا۔ اس پر حضرت عمر کے دفتر میں عمل ہوتا رہا اور اسی وزن پر یہ امر مستعقر ہو گیا۔
The author of al-Hidayah says: For the nisab of zakat, mahr (dowry), sadaqat al-fitr, and the nisab of theft, the weight of 'sab'ah' (seven) is considered for dirhams. The weight of sab'ah is that ten dirhams equal the weight of seven mithqals. Its investigation is that initially there were three types of dirhams: (1) weight ten (wazan 'asharah): ten dirhams equal ten mithqals; (2) weight six (wazan sittah): ten dirhams equal six mithqals; (3) weight five (wazan khamsah): ten dirhams equal five mithqals. Among these three weights, weight ten is the best and weight five is the worst. People used to deal with all three. When Umar (RA) became caliph, he wished to collect zakat and kharaj according to the weight ten, but the people asked for leniency. So the Commander of the Faithful, our master Umar al-Faruq, gathered the accountants of his time so that they, keeping the three weights in view, could determine a middle weight that would take into consideration both sides. Accordingly, they collected the three weights and their mithqals; they totaled twenty-one. Since there were three weights, when twenty-one mithqals were divided by three, one portion came to seven mithqals. That is, the middle weight turned out to be that ten dirhams equal seven mithqals. This is called wazan sab'ah. There was consensus (ijma') of the Companions upon it. It was practised in Umar's office and this weight became established.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage explains the standard weight of the dirham used in determining the nisab for zakat, mahr, sadaqat al-fitr, and the minimum for theft (sariqa). The author of al-Hidayah states that the weight of sab'ah (seven) is the authoritative measure: ten dirhams should weigh seven mithqals (a mithqal is a unit of weight, approximately 4.25 grams). Historically, there were three different dirham weights in circulation. When Caliph Umar wanted to standardize the currency to the best weight (weight ten), people found it too heavy. He then convened accountants who took the three weights (10, 6, and 5 mithqals per 10 dirhams) and took their average: (10+6+5)/3 = 7 mithqals. This became the standard, and the Companions agreed on it. Thus, the nisab of 200 dirhams is calculated based on this weight. This is a definition_ruling because it defines the measure of the nisab. The authority is ijma' (consensus).

Key Terms
وزن سبعہ (wazan sab'ah): The standard dirham weight: 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals. This is the Hanafi standard for nisab calculations.
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight. Historically, one mithqal is approximately 4.25 grams. Here it is used to define the dirham weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How was the weight of sab'ah (7 mithqals per 10 dirhams) determined?
A) It was the weight used during the Prophet's time.
B) It was the average of three existing weights by Caliph Umar's accountants.
C) It was chosen arbitrarily by the Umayyad dynasty.
D) It was based on a hadith from the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi standard dirham weight is wazan sab'ah (10 dirhams = 7 mithqals), established by the consensus of the Companions under Caliph Umar's authority.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Zakat on Mixed Coins: The Criterion of Dominance
Determination of zakat on coins based on dominant component

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of ghalabah (dominance) to determine the zakat ruling on mixed coins and identify the condition of trade intention and its exception.

Core Idea
Dominance (ghalabah) of silver or alloy dictates zakat treatment: over half is the decisive threshold.

In a world of minted coins, silver is rarely pure. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: whichever component exceeds half the coin's weight determines its zakat classification. This passage from al-Hidayah, explained by Ashraf ul Hadaya, sets out the criterion, the need for trade intention when alloy dominates, and the exception when pure silver can be extracted. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the principle of ghalabah and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognise that the passage addresses zakat on coins containing both precious metal and alloy. The question is: which zakat regime applies?
2
State the criterion: ghalabah
The author declares that the ruling follows the dominant component. 'Ghalabah' means exceeding half (more than 50%). This is the dividing line between a silver coin and a trade good.
The reasoning: coins inevitably contain trace alloy, so a little is ignored; only significant alloy shifts the ruling.
3
Apply the two scenarios
If silver (or gold) is dominant → treated as silver → zakat on the silver content at 2.5% if nisab reached. If alloy (ghash) is dominant → treated as a trade good (urud) → zakat only if market value reaches nisab AND intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah) is present.
Trade intention is necessary because it becomes a commodity, not a currency.
4
Note the exception for extractable silver
Even if alloy is dominant, if pure silver can be extracted from the coin that itself reaches a nisab, then the coin's silver content is treated as pure silver. In that case, no trade intention is required; zakat is due on the silver alone.
This exception protects the substance (ayn al-fiddah) regardless of mixture.
5
Summarise the fiqh hierarchy
For zakat on coins: first determine dominance by weight (over half). Then apply the corresponding regime. Ensure that for trade goods, intention and value are checked.
This framework applies to gold coins analogously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ڈھلے ہوئے سکوں میں سونا چاندی یا کھوٹ جس کا غلبہ ہے اس کے حساب سے زکوۃ کا حکم جاری ہوگا وَإِذَا كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الْوَرْقِ الْفِصَّهُ فَهُوَ فِى حُكْمِ الْفِضَّةِ وَإِذَا كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَيْهَا الْعَشُ فَهُوَ فِى حُكم الْعُرُوضِ يُعْتَبَرُ انْ تَبْلُغَ قِيْمَتُهُ نِصَابًا لأنَّ الدَّرَاهِمَ لَا تَخُلُو عَنْ قَلِيلِ غَشْ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَنْطَبِعُ إِلَّا بِهِ وَ تَخُلُو عَنِ الْكَثِيرِ فَجَعَلْنَا الْغَلَبَةَ فَاصِلَةٌ وَهُوَ أَنْ تَزِيدَ عَلَى النِّصْفِ اِعْتِبَارًا لِلْحَقِيقَةِ وَسَتَذْكُرُ فِي الصَّبْرِفِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ فِي غَالِبِ الْعَشُ لَابُدَّ مِنْ نِيةِ التِّجَارَةِ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ الْعُرُوضِ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ تَخَلَّصُ مِنْهَا فَضَةً تَبْلُعُ بِصَابًا لِأُنهُ لَا يُعتب فِي عَيْنِ الْفِضَّةِ الْقِيِّمَةُ وَلَاتَّيَةُ التِّجَارَةِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ ترجمہ اور اگر ڈھلے ہوئے سکہ میں چاندی غالب ہو تو وہ سکہ چاندی کے حکم میں ہے اور اگر اس پر چوٹ غالب ہو تو وہ سامان کے حکم میں ہے اعتبار اس کا ہو گا کہ اس کی قیمت نصاب کو پہنچ جائے کیونکہ درہم تھوڑے سے کھوٹ سے خالی نہیں ہوتا اس لئے کہ وہ بغیر کھوٹ کے ڈھلتا نہیں ہے۔ اور درہم زیادہ کھوٹ سے خالی ہوتا ہے پس ہم نے غلبہ کو حد فاضل قرار دیا۔ اور غلبہ یہ ہے کہ آدھے سے زائد ہو حقیقت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور ہم کتاب الصرف میں انشاء اللہ ذکر کریں گے۔ لیکن کھوٹ غالب ہونے کی صورت میں تجارت کی نیت ضروری ہے۔ جیسا کہ تمام اسباب میں ہے۔ مگر جب کے اس سے چاندی بقدر نصاب نکل سکتی ہو کیونکہ عین چاندی میں نہ قیمت معتبر ہے اور نہ نیت تجارت ۔ واللہ اعلم تشریح ورق واؤ کا فتہ اور راء کا کمرہ ڈھلا ہوا سکہ جیسے دراہم وغیر و منش غین کا کرہ اور شین کی تشدید معنی کدورت میل کچیل کھوٹے یہاں فش سے مراد چاندی اور سونے کے علاوہ دوسری دھاتیں ہیں جنکو چاندی میں ملا کر مکہ ڈھالا جاتا ہے اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ چاندی یا سونے کا سکہ بغیر کوٹ کی آمیزش کے نہیں ڈھالا جاتا ہے اب صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے ہے کہ ڈھلے ہوئے سکہ میں اگر چاندی غالب ہو اور کھوٹ یعنی دوسری دھات مغلوب ہو تو وہ سکہ چاندی کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ اور اس میں چاندی کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کھوٹ غالب اور چاندی مغلوب ہے تو وہ سامان کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اس کی قیمت کا اندازہ کر کے دیکھا جائے گا کہ اس کی قیمت مقدار نصاب کو پہنچتی ہے یا نہیں اگر مقدار نصاب کو پہنچ جاتی ہے تو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہو گی ۔ ورنہ نہیں ، صاحب ہدایہ نے مسئلہ کو مدلل کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ در اہم وغیرہ ڈھلے ہوئے سکوں میں تھوڑے سے کھوٹ کا ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اس کے بغیر سکوں کا ڈھالنا ممکن نہیں ب۔ البتہ کھوٹ کی کثیر مقدار کا ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے پس ہم نے قلیل اور کثیر کے درمیان غلبہ کو حد فاضل قرار دیا ہے اور نا پیر سے کہ آدھے سے زائد ہو اور یہی غلبہ کی حقیقت بھی ہے لہذا اگر چاندی آدھے سے زائد ہو اور کھوٹ آدھے سے کم ہو تو وہ سکہ
In minted coins, whichever of gold, silver, or alloy is dominant, the ruling of zakat will be accordingly: 'And if the dominant on the waraq (silver coin) is silver, then it is in the ruling of silver; and if the dominant on it is alloy (ghash), then it is in the ruling of trade goods, and it is considered whether its value reaches a nisab. Because dirhams are not free of a little alloy, since they cannot be minted without it, but they are free of a lot of alloy. So we made dominance (ghalabah) the criterion, and it is that it exceeds half, considering the reality (al-haqiqah). And we will mention in the book of Sarf, inshaAllah. But in the case of dominant alloy, the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah) is necessary, as in all trade goods, except when silver can be extracted from it that reaches a nisab, because in the case of pure silver, neither value nor trade intention is considered. And Allah knows best.' Translation: If in a minted coin silver is dominant, then that coin is in the ruling of silver. And if alloy is dominant, then it is in the ruling of goods. Its consideration is that its value reaches a nisab. Because dirhams are not free of a little alloy, since they cannot be minted without it. And dirhams are free of a lot of alloy. So we made dominance the limit, and dominance is that it exceeds half, considering reality. And we will mention in the book of Sarf, inshaAllah. But in the case of dominant alloy, the intention of trade is necessary, as in all goods. Except when silver can be extracted from it that reaches a nisab, because in pure silver neither value nor trade intention is considered. And Allah knows best. Explanation: 'Waraq': with fatha on waw and sukun on ra, meaning minted coins like dirhams. 'Ghash': with fatha on ghayn and shadda on shin, meaning impurity, dirt, alloy. Here 'fissah' means metals other than silver and gold that are mixed into silver to mint coins. It is a known fact that silver or gold coins cannot be minted without mixing alloy. Now the case: In a minted coin, if silver is dominant and alloy (other metal) is subordinate, that coin is in the ruling of silver, and silver zakat is wajib. And if alloy is dominant and silver is subordinate, it is in the ruling of goods. Thus its value will be assessed to see if it reaches the nisab amount. If it reaches a nisab, zakat is wajib; otherwise not. The author of al-Hidayah, while providing the proof, says that in minted coins such as dirhams, having a little alloy is necessary because without it coins cannot be minted. However, having a large quantity of alloy is not necessary. So we made dominance the limit between little and much, and it is that it exceeds half, and this is the reality of dominance. Therefore, if silver is more than half and alloy is less than half, that coin...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on zakat for mixed coins (maghshushah). Minted coins inevitably contain some alloy, but the ruling depends on what is dominant (ghalib). The Arabic matn (from al-Hidayah) states: if silver (or gold) is dominant, the coin is treated as silver or gold, and zakat is due on the silver content once it reaches the nisab. If the alloy (ghash) is dominant, the coin is treated as a trade good (urud), and its market value must be assessed: if the value reaches the trade nisab, zakat is due, and crucially, the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijarah) is necessary because it is now a trade commodity. An exception arises when pure silver can be extracted from the coin that itself reaches a nisab; in that case, the silver content is treated as pure silver and zakat is due on it without requiring trade intention. The Urdu commentary by Ashraf Ul Hadaya clarifies the definitions: 'waraq' means minted coins, 'ghash' means alloy. It confirms the criterion of dominance (exceeding half) as the dividing line. This ruling demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing reality (haqiqah) and custom (urf) in legal analysis.

Key Terms
غلبہ (ghalabah): Dominance; the condition where one component exceeds half of the coin's weight. This determines whether the coin is treated as silver/gold or as a trade good for zakat purposes.
ورق (waraq): Minted silver coins, dirhams.
غش (ghash): Alloy; non-precious metals mixed into the coin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has a coin that is 60% silver and 40% copper. How is zakat treated?
A) The coin is treated as silver; zakat is due on the full weight of the coin at 2.5%.
B) The coin is treated as a trade good; zakat is due if its value reaches the nisab and trade intention exists.
C) No zakat is due because it is mixed.
D) Zakat is due only on the silver content, not the coin itself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi criterion of ghalabah (dominance by weight over half) determines whether a mixed coin is zakatable as silver or as a trade good, with intention of trade required for alloy-dominant coins unless pure silver can be extracted.

Zakat — Almsgiving

The Standard Weight of the Dirham (Wazn al-Sab'ah)
Establishes dirham weight by consensus of Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard weight ratio of the dirham (Wazn al-Sab'ah) and explain why it is binding on the basis of Ijma of the Sahaba.

Core Idea
The dirham weight is fixed by Ijma of the Sahaba at 10 dirhams = 7 mithqaals.

This passage recounts the historical determination of the dirham weight under Caliph Umar (ra). The resolution of differing weights through a consultative process led to a standard that was unanimously accepted by the Companions. This consensus (Ijma) makes the weight binding for all future generations, particularly for zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Historical Context
Understand the problem: people sought reduction in weight for kharaj collection. Caliph Umar gathered accountants to find a middle standard.
2
Method of Averaging
Three known weights were combined with their mithqaal equivalents, totaling 21 mithqaals. Dividing by 3 yields 7 mithqaals per set, meaning 10 dirhams = 7 mithqaals.
This averaging ensured fairness.
3
Name and Ijma
This ratio is called Wazn al-Sab'ah. The text states that the Sahaba made Ijma on it, making it authoritative.
Ijma is a primary source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Implementation and Stability
Umar's office implemented this weight, and it became established (mustaqir). This gives it practical and legal permanence.
5
Application to Zakat
Based on this fixed weight, the nisaab of silver is 200 dirhams of this standard. Any deviation would affect zakat obligations.
Other schools may have different standards, but Hanafis follow this Ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خراج عمد دوزن عشرہ کے ساتھ وصول کریں اور لوگوں نے اس میں تخفیف چاہی تو خلیفہ المسلمین سیدنا عمر فاروق نے اپنے زمانے کے حساب داں، ان کو جمع فرمایا تا کہ وہ ان اوزان ثلاثہ کو سامنے رکھ کر درمیانی وزن متعین کریں جس میں دونوں کی رعایت ملحوظ ہو۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے تینوں اور ان کے مثاقبیل کو اکٹھا کیا تو وہ اکیس ہوئے ۔ اور وزن چونکہ تین ہیں اس لئے اکیس مثاقیل کو جب تین پر تقسیم کیا گیا تو ایک حصہ میں سات مثقال آئے یعنی درمیانی وزن یہ نکلا کہ دس درہم سات مثقال کے برابر ہوں ۔ اسی کو وزن سبعہ کہا جاتا ہے اسی پر صحابہ کا اجماع ہوا۔ اس پر حضرت عمر کے دفتر میں عمل ہوتا رہا اور اسی وزن پر یہ امر مستقر ہو گیا۔
Collect kharaj with the weight of ten, and when people sought reduction, the Caliph of the Muslims, our master Umar al-Faruq, gathered the accountants of his time so that they could determine a middle weight considering the three weights. So they combined the three and their equivalents, and they became twenty-one. Since the weights are three, when twenty-one mithqaals were divided by three, each share came to seven mithqaals, meaning the middle weight was that ten dirhams equal seven mithqaals. This is called Wazn al-Sab'ah, and the Sahaba made Ijma on it. It was implemented in the office of Umar and this weight became established.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage establishes the standard dirham weight for zakat and other transactions. It recounts how Caliph Umar (ra) resolved a dispute over weights by averaging three known standards. The resulting weight, Wazn al-Sab'ah (the seven weight), where ten dirhams equal seven mithqaals, was unanimously agreed upon by the Sahaba. This Ijma makes the weight binding in the Hanafi school. The ruling is that the nisaab of silver (200 dirhams) and other measures must be based on this weight.

Key Terms
وزن سبعہ (wazn al-sab'ah): The standard weight where 10 dirhams equal 7 mithqaals, established by consensus of the Sahaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the standard dirham weight (Wazn al-Sab'ah) according to the Hanafi school?
A) The custom of the people of Madina
B) The Ijma of the Sahaba
C) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone
D) The measurement from the time of the Prophet (saw)

Key Takeaway
The dirham weight for zakat is fixed by Ijma of the Sahaba as 10 dirhams = 7 mithqaals, known as Wazn al-Sab'ah.

Zakat on Mixed-Alloy Coins: The Rule of Ghalebah
Ruling with proof on classifying mixed coins for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of ghalebah to classify mixed-alloy coins for zakat and identify the conditions for zakat in each scenario (silver-predominant, alloy-predominant, and extractable silver).

Core Idea
The predominant metal (>50%) in a coin determines its zakat status: silver-predominant = silver; alloy-predominant = merchandise.

In Hanafi law, struck coins (waraq) are rarely pure silver; they contain alloy (ghash) for striking. The key question is: when does a coin retain the ruling of silver, and when does it become merchandise? This lesson examines the criterion of ghalebah (predominance) laid down in al-Hidayah. We will see how the threshold of >50% separates the two categories and learn the exceptions when trade intention or extractable silver applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that coins are classified based on whether the silver or the alloy (base metal) is predominant. The text presents two main cases: silver-ghalib (silver >50%) and alloy-ghalib (alloy >50%).
This is the foundational split; the ruling follows the majority component.
2
Understand the ghalebah threshold
Ghalebah means exceeding half (>50%). The text explicitly defines it: 'it is that it exceeds half, considering the reality.' This is the dividing line between little and much alloy, since a small amount of alloy is inevitable in coinage.
The Hanafi school uses a simple majority; other schools may differ.
3
Apply the ruling to each scenario
If silver is ghalib, the entire coin takes the ruling of silver: zakat is wajib on the total weight if it reaches nisaab (200 dirhams), with no need for trade intention. If alloy is ghalib, the coin is treated as merchandise: zakat is wajib only if its market value reaches nisaab AND the owner intends trade (niyyah al-tijarah).
This distinction is critical because silver-predominant coins bypass the trade intention requirement.
4
Recognize the extraction exception
Even if alloy is ghalib, if pure silver can be extracted from the coins and that extracted silver itself reaches the nisaab (200 dirhams), then zakat on that silver is wajib as silver—no need for trade intention or value assessment. The extracted silver is treated as pure silver ('ayn al-fiddah).
This exception protects the zakat on actual silver content when it is separable.
5
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning (dalil) is the established fact that coins cannot be struck without some alloy. Therefore, a small amount is excusable; but when alloy becomes predominant, the substance changes in reality, so the ruling shifts. Ghalebah (>50%) is the pragmatic borderline set by the Hanafi fuqaha.
This is an example of ta'lil using custom and necessity to define a legal criterion.

نیت تجارت ضروری ہے اگر سکوں میں چاندی تو مغلوب ہے لیکن اس کو اگر جدا کر کے الگ کر لیا جائے تو وہ مقدار نصاب یعنی دو سو درہم کی مقدار کو پہنچ جاتی ہے تو اس چاندی میں چاندی کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی نہ اس میں قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور نہ نیت تجارت کا۔ کیونکہ مین چاندی میں ان دونوں کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا۔ واللہ اعلم
In struck coins, the ruling of zakat will be based on what is predominant: gold, silver, or alloy. And if silver is predominant over the coins, it is in the ruling of silver; and if alloy is predominant over it, it is in the ruling of merchandise, so it is considered that its value reaches nisaab. Because dirhams are not free from a little alloy, since they cannot be struck without it, but they are free from large amounts of alloy. So we made predominance (ghalebah) the separator, and it is that it exceeds half, considering the essence. And you will mention it in the book of Sarf, if Allah wills. But in the case where alloy is predominant, there must be the intention of trade, as in other merchandise, except if pure silver can be extracted from it that reaches nisaab, because in pure silver neither value nor intention of trade is considered. And Allah knows best. Translation: And if in a struck coin silver is predominant, then that coin is in the ruling of silver; and if alloy is predominant over it, then it is in the ruling of merchandise; its consideration will be that its value reaches nisaab. Because dirhams are not free from a little alloy, for they cannot be struck without it. And dirhams are free from a lot of alloy. So we made predominance the dividing line. And predominance is that it exceeds half, considering the reality. And we will mention in the book of Sarf, if Allah wills. But in the case of predominant alloy, the intention of trade is necessary, as in all merchandise. Except when silver can be extracted from it that reaches nisaab, because in pure silver neither value nor intention of trade is considered. And Allah knows best. Commentary: Waraq (with fatha on waw and sukun on ra) means struck coin like dirhams etc. Ghash (with fatha on ghain and shadda on shin) means impurity, dirt, alloy. Here, fissah refers to metals other than silver and gold that are mixed with silver when striking coins. And it is established that silver or gold coins cannot be struck without mixing alloy. Now the issue: If in a struck coin silver is predominant and alloy (other metal) is subordinate, then that coin is in the ruling of silver, and zakat of silver is wajib on it. And if alloy is predominant and silver is subordinate, then it is in the ruling of merchandise. So its value will be estimated to see if it reaches the nisaab; if it does, zakat is wajib; otherwise not. The author of Hidayah said, providing proof, that in dirhams and other struck coins, a little alloy is necessary because without it, striking coins is not possible. However, a large amount of alloy is not necessary. So we made predominance as the dividing line between little and much, and it is that it exceeds half. And that is the reality of ghalebah. So if silver is more than half and alloy is less than half, then that entire coin is considered silver, and zakat of silver is wajib on it. And if the opposite, i.e., alloy is more than half and silver is less than half, then that coin is considered metal other than silver, and its ruling is like other merchandise. The author of Hidayah said that in the case of predominant alloy, the intention of trade is necessary for zakat to be wajib, because in that case it is in the ruling of merchandise. And it is established that in other than silver and gold, intention of trade is necessary for zakat. If the silver in the coins is subordinate, but if it is separated and taken out, it reaches the nisaab (i.e., 200 dirhams), then zakat of silver is wajib on that silver; neither value nor intention of trade is considered. Because in pure silver, these two are not considered. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical issue: when coins are made from a mixture of silver and other metals, how is zakat determined? The ruling: look at the predominant component. If silver (or gold) is more than half (>50%), the entire coin is treated as silver (or gold) and zakat is due on its weight if it reaches nisaab. If the alloy (other metal) is predominant, then the coin is treated as merchandise, meaning zakat is only due if its market value reaches nisaab AND the owner intends trade (niyyah al-tijarah). There is an exception: if the silver content, when extracted, would itself reach the nisaab of silver (200 dirhams), then that silver is subject to zakat as silver—no need for trade intention or value assessment. The reasoning is that a small amount of alloy is unavoidable in coinage, so the dividing line is ghalebah (predominance). This ruling is based on ta'lil (legal reasoning) and is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الغالب (al-ghalib): The component that exceeds half (more than 50%) in a mixture.
الورق (al-waraq): Struck silver coins (dirhams).
العش (al-'ash): Alloy, the non-silver metal mixed in coins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a coin has 40% silver and 60% alloy?
A) It is treated as silver for zakat.
B) It is treated as merchandise requiring trade intention.
C) Zakat is not due at all.
D) It is treated as gold.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: the predominant metal (>50%) in a coin determines its zakat classification—silver-predominant is treated as silver (zakat on weight, no trade intention), while alloy-predominant is merchandise (zakat on value, trade intention required), unless the extractable silver itself reaches nisaab.

Zakat on Gold: Nisaab and Calculation
States ruling and proof for zakat on gold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the zakat due on gold based on the Hanafi nisaab and rate, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Gold zakat is obligatory at 20 mithqaals; the rate is 2.5% (half mithqaal per 20 mithqaals).

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the zakat ruling for gold. It specifies the minimum threshold (nisaab) and the amount due, providing a hadith as evidence. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct zakat calculation on gold assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisaab
The nisaab for gold is 20 mithqaals. Less than that, no zakat is wajib.
The mithqaal is a weight unit; 7 mithqaals = 10 dirhams.
2
Note the zakat amount
On 20 mithqaals, half a mithqaal is due, which is 1/40 (2.5%).
3
Understand the proof
The hadith from the Prophet (SAW) 'He used to take from every 20 dinars half a dinar' is the primary evidence. Despite being ahad, its meaning is clear (qati) and establishes obligation (wujub).
Dinars are gold coins; a dinar equals one mithqaal by weight.
4
Apply the rate to excess
For gold above the nisaab, the same 2.5% rate applies. For every 4 mithqaals, 2 qirats are due (since 1 mithqaal = 20 qirats, 1/40 of 4 mithqaals = 0.1 mithqaal = 2 qirats).
The text states: 'For every four mithqaals, two qirats.'
5
Calculate a sample
Take 24 mithqaals: zakat is half a mithqaal for the first 20, plus 2 qirats for the extra 4. Total = 0.5 mithqaal + 0.1 mithqaal = 0.6 mithqaal (12 qirats).
Alternatively, 2.5% of 24 = 0.6 mithqaal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلُّ فِي الذَّهَبِ
ترجمہ فصل سونے کی زکوۃ میں ہے
سونے کی زکوۃ سونے کا نصاب و مقدار زکوة
لَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا مِنْ ذَهَبِ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ عِشْرِينَ مَتَقَالًا فَفِيهَا نِصْفُ مِثْقَالَ لِمَا رَوِّينَا وَالْمِثْقَالُ مَا يَكُونْ كُلّ سَبْعَةٍ مِنْهَا وَزُنٌ عَشَرَةَ دَرَاهِم وَهُوَ الْمَعْرُوفَ
ترجمہ میں مثقال سونے سے کم میں زکو نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر میں مشتقال ہوں تو ان میں آدھا مثقال ہے۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ اور مثقال یہ ہے کہ ہر سات مثقال دس درھم کے برابر ہوں۔ اور یہی معروف ہے۔
تشریح ۔ اس فصل میں سونے کی زکوۃ کا بیان ہے سونے کا نصاب میں مشتقال میں اور اس سے کم میں زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ اور میں مثقال میں آدھا مثقال واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل وہ روایت ہے جو فصل فی الفضة کے اول میں گذر چکی ہے من وَمِنْ كُلِّ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ نِصْفُ مُتَقَالِ ابن ماجہ میں یہ روایت ابن عمر اور حضرت عائشہ سے ان الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے اُنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وَسَلَّم كَانَ يَأخُذُ مِنْ كُلَّ عِشْرِينَ دِينَارًا نِصْفُ دِينَارٍ وَمِنَ الْأَرْبَعِينَ دِينَارًا (شرح نقایہ ) مثقال سے مراد وہ مثقال ہے جن کے ساتھ مثقال کا وزن دس درہم کے برابر ہولوگوں میں یہی وزن متعارف ہے۔
ہیں مثقال سے زائد میں زکوۃ
ثُمَّ فِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعَةِ مَنَا قِبل قِيرَاطَانِ لِأَنَّ الوَاجِبَ رُبُعُ الْعُشْرِ وَ ذَلِكَ فِيْمَا قُلْنَا ذُكُلُّ مَتَقَالِ عِشْرُونَ قِيْراطًا ترجمہ پھر ہر چار مثقال میں دو قیراط ہیں کیونکہ واجب تو چالیسواں حصہ ہے اور یہ اس میں ہے جو ہم نے کہا کیونکہ ہر مثقال نہیں
قیراط کا ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ میں مثقال پر اگر چار مثقال کا اضافہ ہو گیا ہو تو نصف مثقال کے ساتھ دو قیراط اور واجب ہوں
Section on gold. Translation: Section on zakat of gold. The nisaab and amount of zakat of gold. There is no charity on less than twenty mithqaals of gold; when it becomes twenty mithqaals, then half a mithqaal is due, due to what we have narrated. And the mithqaal is that every seven of them weigh ten dirhams, and that is well-known. Translation: There is no zakat on less than twenty mithqaals of gold. So if there are twenty mithqaals, then half a mithqaal is due, due to the hadith we have narrated. And the mithqaal is that every seven mithqaals weigh ten dirhams, and this is well-known. Commentary: In this section, zakat of gold is discussed. The nisaab of gold is twenty mithqaals; less than that, zakat is not wajib. On twenty mithqaals, half a mithqaal is wajib. The proof is the narration that passed in the section on silver: 'And from every twenty mithqaals of gold, half a mithqaal.' In Ibn Majah, it is narrated from Ibn Umar and Aisha with these words: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to take from every twenty dinars half a dinar, and from forty dinars...' (Sharh Niqayah). The mithqaal referred to is that seven mithqaals weigh ten dirhams, and this is the common weight among people. Then for more than mithqaals: Then for every four mithqaals, two qirats are due, because the wajib is one-fortieth, and that is as we said since every mithqaal is twenty qirats. Translation: Then for every four mithqaals, two qirats are due, because the wajib is one-fortieth, and that is in what we said, since every mithqaal is twenty qirats. Commentary: The author of Quduri said that if twenty mithqaals are increased by four mithqaals, then along with half a mithqaal, two qirats are also wajib.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on zakat for gold. The nisaab (minimum threshold) is 20 mithqaals. The zakat due on that amount is half a mithqaal (which is 1/40 of the total, i.e., 2.5%). The evidence is a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated in Ibn Majah. For gold exceeding the nisaab, the rate remains 2.5%: for every additional 4 mithqaals, 2 qirats are due (since 1 mithqaal = 20 qirats, and 1/40 of 4 mithqaals is 2 qirats). The mithqaal is defined as a weight where 7 mithqaals equal 10 dirhams, consistent with the dirham weight established earlier. This is the standard Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
المثقال (al-mithqaal): A unit of weight for gold; in this text, 7 mithqaals = 10 dirhams.
القيراط (al-qirat): A subunit of the mithqaal; 1 mithqaal = 20 qirats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the zakat due on 24 mithqaals of gold?
A) Half a mithqaal
B) Half a mithqaal plus 2 qirats
C) One mithqaal
D) 2.5% of the value

Key Takeaway
Gold zakat is due at 2.5% on the nisaab of 20 mithqaals and on any excess at the same rate, as established by the hadith of the Prophet (SAW).

Zakat on Gold: Nisab, Amount, and the Fractional Surplus Dispute
Commentary on gold zakat nisab and the intra-Hanafi dispute on fractional surplus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab of gold, calculate the zakat due on a given amount, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on fractional surplus along with the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold: 20 mithqals due half a mithqal; fractions below 4 mithqals disputed – Abu Hanifa exempts, Sahibayn require proportional zakat.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi ruling on zakat for gold, including the definition of weight units and the calculation method. The commentary presents a foundational framework: no zakat below 20 mithqals, half a mithqal on exactly 20, and two qirats per every additional 4 mithqals. It then introduces the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute over fractional surplus (mas'alat al-kusur): does zakat apply to amounts less than 4 mithqals above the nisab?

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab and base zakat
From the passage: 'There is no charity on less than twenty mithqals of gold. When there are twenty mithqals, half a mithqal is due.' Note the nisab and the fraction (1/40).
2
Understand the weight units: mithqal, qirat, dinar
The text defines a mithqal as a weight where 7 mithqals weigh 10 dirhams. One mithqal = 1 dinar = 20 qirats. The Sharia valuation: 1 dinar = 10 dirhams.
3
Calculate zakat on surpluses above the nisab
For every additional 4 mithqals, two qirats are due (since 2/20 = 1/10 of a mithqal per 4 mithqals = 1/40). This matches the general one-fortieth rule.
4
State the intra-Hanafi dispute on fractions
The text explicitly notes ikhtilaf: 'According to Abu Hanifa, there is no charity on less than four mithqals, but according to them (Sahibayn), it is due proportionally.' This is the issue of fractions.
5
Analyze the proofs and determine the mufta bihi
Abu Hanifa analogizes to silver (no zakat on fractions below 40 dirhams). The Sahibayn argue from the general principle of zakat on all surplus. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Sahibayn's view, as it is more precautionary and aligns with later Hanafi authority.

Source Text

فَصْلُّ فِي الذَّهَبِ
لَيْسَ فِيْمَا دُونَ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا مِنْ ذَهَبِ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ عِشْرِينَ مَتَقَالًا فَفِيهَا نِصْفُ مِثْقَالَ لِمَا رَوِّينَا وَالْمِثْقَالُ مَا يَكُونْ كُلّ سَبْعَةٍ مِنْهَا وَزُنٌ عَشَرَةَ دَرَاهِم وَهُوَ الْمَعْرُوفَ

Section on gold. There is no charity on less than twenty mithqals of gold. When there are twenty mithqals, half a mithqal is due on them, due to what we have narrated. The mithqal is such that every seven of them weigh ten dirhams, and that is well known. Then, on every four mithqals, two qirats are due, because what is obligatory is one-fortieth, and that is as we said: every mithqal is twenty qirats. And according to Abu Hanifa, there is no charity on less than four mithqals, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is due proportionally; this is the issue of fractions. And every dinar in the Sharia is ten dirhams, so four mithqals in this are like forty dirhams.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah discusses the zakat obligation on gold. It begins by stating the authoritative ruling: no zakat is due on gold less than twenty mithqals. When one possesses exactly twenty mithqals, half a mithqal is due. The proof is the hadith narrated earlier in the chapter on silver (from Ibn Majah: the Prophet would take half a dinar from every twenty dinars). The mithqal is defined as a unit where seven mithqals weigh ten dirhams, which is the well-known standard. Next, it addresses the surplus above the nisab. For every additional four mithqals, two qirats are due, because zakat is one-fortieth, and each mithqal equals twenty qirats. Then the key intra-Hanafi dispute appears: according to Abu Hanifa, no zakat is due on less than a full four mithqals above the nisab (i.e., fractions are exempt). According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), zakat is due on any fraction proportionally (e.g., one mithqal above twenty yields half a mithqal plus a quarter qirat). This is the 'issue of fractions' (mas'alat al-kusur) also seen in the silver section. Finally, the note clarifies the Sharia equivalence: one dinar (one mithqal of gold) is valued at ten dirhams of silver, so four mithqals equal forty dirhams (the nisab of silver), reinforcing the analogy.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight for gold; the text defines it as a measure where seven mithqals weigh ten dirhams. One mithqal equals one dinar.
قيراط (qirat): A subdivision of the mithqal; one mithqal equals 20 qirats. Two qirats are due on every four mithqals (i.e., 1/40 of 4 mithqals).
دينار (dinar): A gold coin equivalent to one mithqal. The Sharia equates one dinar to ten dirhams in value (not weight).
مسألة الكسور (mas'alat al-kusur): The issue of fractions: whether zakat is obligatory on amounts less than a full unit (e.g., less than 4 mithqals above the nisab).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the definition of a mithqal in terms of its weight in dirhams?
A) One mithqal equals ten dirhams
B) Seven mithqals weigh ten dirhams
C) One mithqal weighs seven dirhams
D) Ten mithqals weigh seven dirhams

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold is due at 1/40 of the nisab (20 mithqals) and on any additional full 4 mithqal increments, but the relied-upon position requires proportional zakat on all surplus, including fractional amounts.

Zakat on Fractional Gold: Mas'alah al-Kusur
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for fractional gold below nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for fractional gold (mas'alah al-kusur) and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Zakat on fractional gold above the nisab is wajib for the Sahibayn but not for Abu Hanifa — the issue of fractions (mas'alah al-kusur).

This lesson explores an internal Hanafi disagreement about whether zakat is due on fractional amounts of gold that are less than four mithqals when added to a complete nisab. The dispute, known as mas'alah al-kusur, mirrors a similar disagreement in silver zakat. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how the Hanafi school applies the nisab condition to additions.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on zakat on fractions below 4 mithqals.
Abu Hanifa: no zakat; Sahibayn: proportional zakat.
2
Apply to an example
Consider a nisab of 4 mithqals plus an additional 1 mithqal. Calculate zakat due under each position.
Abu Hanifa: zakat on 4 mithqals only (0.1 mithqal); Sahibayn: zakat on 5 mithqals (0.125 mithqal).
3
Connect to silver analogy
The same dispute applies to silver: Abu Hanifa says no zakat on additions less than 40 dirhams; Sahibayn say proportional. The nisab for gold in this context is 4 mithqals because 1 dinar = 10 dirhams.
4 mithqals = 40 dirhams value.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which position is relied upon for fatwa and why.
The Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi due to ease and practice.

And there is no sadaqah in what is less than four mithqals according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (Sahibayn) it is obligatory in proportion to that, and this is the issue of fractions. And every dinar is ten dirhams in the Shariah, so four mithqals in this are like forty dirhams. Translation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no zakat in less than four mithqals. According to the Sahibayn, it is obligatory in proportion, and this is the same issue of fractions. And every dinar in the Shariah is ten dirhams, so four mithqals are like forty dirhams. Explanation: If there is an addition of less than four mithqals to the nisab, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no zakat is due on that addition. According to the Sahibayn, zakat is due in proportion. For example, if one mithqal is added, half a mithqal and half a qirat are due as zakat. Because the fortieth part of a mithqal is half a qirat. The author of Hidayah says: This is the same issue of fractions that passed in the previous chapter on silver, i.e., according to the Sahibayn, zakat is due on fractions, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not due. The proofs of both sides have been stated. The author adds: In the Shariah, one dinar equals ten dirhams, and mithqal and dinar are the same, so four mithqals equal forty dirhams. Just as in silver, according to Abu Hanifa, there is no zakat on additions less than forty dirhams, similarly, on additions of less than four mithqals above the nisab, zakat is not due. Here a question may arise: In the previous chapter, it was said that seven mithqals equal ten dirhams in weight, and here it is said that one dinar equals ten dirhams. The answer is that the previous chapter dealt with weight, i.e., the weight of ten dirhams equals seven mithqals, while here it is about value, i.e., the Shariah fixed the value of one dinar (one mithqal of gold) at ten dirhams of silver. For example, in the diyah for accidental killing, if payment is made in dinars, one thousand dinars are given; if in dirhams, ten thousand dirhams. But note that this estimation was according to the market of that time, and since prices fluctuate, in every time the value is fixed according to the market of that time.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the obligation of zakat on fractional amounts of gold that are less than the nisab of four mithqals. The ruling is part of the broader issue known as mas'alah al-kusur (the issue of fractions). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on any amount less than four mithqals, even if it is added to an existing nisab. Thus, if one possesses four mithqals plus an additional fractional amount, the zakat is only on the full four mithqals, not on the fraction. The Sahibayn, on the other hand, hold that zakat is due on the fraction in proportion to its amount. For example, if an extra mithqal is added, the zakat on that mithqal is half a mithqal plus half a qirat (since the rate is 2.5%, i.e., 1/40). The author of Al-Hidayah clarifies that this is the same dispute that occurred in the chapter on silver regarding fractions below forty dirhams. The text then reconciles an apparent contradiction: earlier it was stated that seven mithqals equal ten dirhams in weight, but here it says one dinar (a mithqal of gold) equals ten dirhams in value. The explanation is that the earlier statement referred to physical weight equivalence (i.e., ten dirhams of silver weigh seven mithqals), while the latter refers to the Shariah-established value equivalence for purposes like diyah and zakat assessment. Importantly, this value equivalence is not fixed for all times but is based on market rates, so in each era zakat valuation should be according to the prevailing market price.

Key Terms
مسئلہ کسور (mas'alah al-kusur): The issue of fractions: whether zakat is due on amounts less than the nisab when added to a complete nisab.
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight for gold; approximately 4.25 grams. The nisab for gold is 20 mithqals, but here the context is the silver-equivalent nisab of 4 mithqals.
قیراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1/20 of a mithqal. Also used in measuring zakat amounts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only on 4 mithqals

C) Only on the 2 qirats
D) No zakat at all

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school on zakat for fractions is that of the Sahibayn: proportional zakat is wajib on fractions above the nisab.

Zakat on Gold and Silver Jewelry and Vessels
Inter-madhhab dispute on zakat for gold and silver in usable forms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat for gold and silver jewelry, explain the opposing Shafi'i view, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the concept of 'mal namī'.

Core Idea
Zakat is wajib on all gold and silver because their inherent growth potential makes them like trade goods, regardless of use.

Gold and silver jewelry is a common asset, but scholars disagree on whether zakat applies. This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya pits the Hanafi school against the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali positions. The key is understanding what makes wealth 'growing' (mal namī) and why that matters for zakat.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the matn: zakat is obligatory on all gold and silver – bullion, jewelry, and vessels.
2
Identify the opposing view
What do Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali hold? They exempt women's jewelry and men's silver rings used for permissible purposes.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i analogy: jewelry is like ordinary clothes (thiyāb al-badhalah) – used for permissible needs and not intended for trade.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that gold and silver inherently have growth potential (khilqatan), unlike clothes. This inherent nature is the effective cause for zakat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi women must pay zakat on their gold jewelry; Shafi'i women do not. Men's silver rings: same difference.

Source Text

قَالَ وَفِي تبرِ الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ وَحُلَيْهِمَا وَانِيهِمَا الزَّكوةُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعُى لا تَجِبُ فِى حُليّ النِّسَاءِ وَخَاتَمِ الْفِضَّةِ للرجال لأنَّهُ مَبْتَدِلٌ فِي مُبَاحٍ فَشَابَهَ ثِيَابُ الْبَذَلَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ السَّبَبَ مَالٌ نام و دَلِيلُ اليَمَاءِ مَوْجُودٌ وَهُوَ الْإِعْدَادُ لِلتِّجَارَةِ خِلْقَةً وَالدَّلِيلُ هُوَ الْمُعْتَبَرُ بِخَلافِ القِيَابِ

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب مال نامی ہے۔ اور نمود و طرح کا ہوتا ہے ایک خلتی جیسے سونے اور چاندی میں ہوتا ہے دوم فعلی یعنی بذریعہ تجارت یہاں نمو کی دلیل موجود ہے یعنی پیدائشی اور خلقی طور پر اس کا تجارت کے لئے مہیا ہونا۔ اور دلیل ہی معتبر ہے ۔ پس جب دلیل نمو موجود ہے تو کسی کے باطل کرنے سے یہ خلقی نماء باطل نہیں ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف شیاب بذلہ کہ ان میں نہ خلقہ نما پایا جاتا ہے اور نہ فعلاً پایا جاتا ہے خلقہ تو اس لئے نہیں پایا جاتا کہ کپڑے پیدائشی طور پر تجارت کے لئے مہیا نہیں ہیں۔ اور فعلا اس لئے ں کہ شیاب بذلہ ( روز مرہ کے استعمال کے کپڑوں ) میں بندے کی طرف سے تجارت کی نیت نہیں ہوتی پس جب کسی طرح بھی نمو موجود نہیں ہے تو شیاب بذلہ میں زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ آیت بھی ہے " وَالَّذِيْنَ يَكْبِرُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ وَلَا يُنفِقُونَها فِى سبيل الله فَبَشِّرُهُمْ بِعَذَاب اليم " . التوبة (۳۳) اور جو لوگ گاڑھ کر رکھتے ہیں سونا اور چاندی اور اس کو خرچ نہیں کرتے اللہ کی راہ میں سوان کو خوشخبری سنادے عذاب دردناک کی۔ اس آیت کے عموم سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ سونا اور چاندی ڈھلا ہوا ہو یا بغیر ڈھلا ہوا اور ڈھلا ہوا بھی سکہ کی شکل میں ہو یا زیور وغیرہ کی شکل میں بہر صورت اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ عدم انفاق فی سبیل اللہ کی صورت میں عذاب الیم کی وعید آئی ہے اور وعید ترک واجب پر آتی ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ مطلقا سونے اور چاندی میں انفاق فی سبیل اللہ یعنی زکوۃ واجب ہے نیر امام ابوداؤ داور امام نسائی نے عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبِ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عن جدہ سے ایک حدیث روایت کی ہے جس کے الفاظ یہ ہیں إِنَّ امْرَأَةٌ أتَتِ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَمَعَهَا بِنتُ لَهَا وَ فِي
He said: And in bullion of gold and silver, and their jewelry and their vessels, zakat is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not obligatory on women's jewelry and a man's silver ring, because it is used for permissible purposes, so it resembles ordinary clothes. Our evidence is that the cause is wealth that grows, and the indication of growth exists, and that is its natural readiness for trade, and the evidence is what is considered, contrary to ordinary clothes. Commentary: 'Tibr' is unminted silver, raw silver, and gold jewelry that women use for adornment. According to us, zakat is obligatory on unminted gold and silver, their jewelry and vessels. Imam Shafi'i said that zakat is not obligatory on women's jewelry and men's silver ring. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. Imam Shafi'i's evidence is that the use of silver and gold jewelry is permissible for women, and the use of a silver ring is permissible for men, and a thing whose use is permissible and commonly used is not subject to zakat, like everyday clothes and work clothes, in which there is no zakat. Our evidence is that the cause of zakat is growing wealth. Growth is of two types: inherent, as in gold and silver, and actual, through trade. Here the evidence of growth exists, i.e., its natural readiness for trade, and the evidence is what is considered. So when the evidence of growth exists, it is not invalidated by anyone. In contrast, ordinary clothes have neither inherent nor actual growth: not inherent because clothes are not naturally ready for trade, and not actual because the owner does not intend trade. Thus, when no growth exists, zakat is not obligatory. Our evidence is also the verse: 'And those who hoard gold and silver and spend them not in the way of Allah – give them tidings of a painful punishment' (al-Tawbah 9:34). The generality of this verse shows that gold and silver, whether minted or unminted, whether in the form of coins or jewelry, are subject to zakat. Because the threat of painful punishment is for not spending in the way of Allah, and a threat comes for abandoning an obligation. So it is understood that spending in the way of Allah, i.e., zakat, is obligatory on gold and silver in absolute terms. Also, Imam Abu Dawud and Imam Nasa'i narrated from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather a hadith: 'A woman came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, with her daughter, and in...'
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school (along with Maliki and Hanbali) regarding the obligation of zakat on gold and silver jewelry, vessels, and bullion. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that zakat is obligatory on all forms of gold and silver – whether in bullion (tibr), jewelry (huly), or vessels (awani). The Shafi'i position exempts women's jewelry and men's silver rings because these are used for permissible purposes and are thus similar to everyday clothes, which are not zakatable. The Hanafi response provides two lines of evidence: (1) Rational: the cause (sabab) for zakat is 'mal namī' (growing wealth). Gold and silver inherently possess the potential for growth (khilqatan) because they are naturally ready for trade and can be used as capital. This inherent growth potential is sufficient for zakat to be obligatory, regardless of whether the owner actually intends trade. In contrast, clothes (thiyāb al-badhalah) have no such growth potential — they are not naturally trade goods, and the owner does not intend them for trade. (2) Scriptural: the Qur'anic verse 9:34 threatens punishment for those who hoard gold and silver and do not spend in Allah's way (i.e., pay zakat). The verse is general (āmm) and includes all forms of gold and silver. Additionally, the hadith narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i (though cut off here) supports the obligation of zakat on jewelry. The lesson emphasizes that the Hanafi school gives weight to the inherent growth potential of gold and silver as the effective cause, while the Shafi'i school considers actual usage and intention.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Uncoined, raw gold or silver (bullion).
حلی (huly): Jewelry, ornaments made of gold or silver.
مال نامی (mal namī): Wealth that naturally grows or has the potential to increase, such as gold, silver, trade goods.
ثیاب البذلة (thiyāb al-badhalah): Ordinary everyday clothes, work clothes that are not trade goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi school's primary evidence for obligating zakat on gold jewelry?
A) The jewelry is intended for trade
B) Gold and silver inherently have growth potential
C) The owner uses it for savings
D) The hadith of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Gold and silver are zakatable in all forms because their inherent readiness for trade (khilqatan) fulfills the sabab of mal namī, regardless of actual use.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Zakat on Gold and Silver Jewelry: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on zakat of jewelry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for jewelry and utensils, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the key proofs (Quran and hadith) used by each school.

Core Idea
Gold and silver jewelry is subject to zakat because the capacity for growth (nama') is inherent in the metal itself.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: Is zakat obligatory on gold and silver when fashioned into jewelry or utensils for personal use? The Hanafi school holds that zakat is always due, while the Shafi'i school exempts women's jewelry and men's silver rings. Understanding the proofs each school uses—from Quranic verses to hadiths and legal reasoning—deepens your grasp of zakat obligations and the role of 'illah (effective cause) in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi text (al-Hidayah) asserts: zakat is obligatory on all forms of gold and silver, including raw metal (tibr), jewelry, and utensils.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the items are for adornment or use.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize Imam al-Shafi'i's position: women's jewelry and men's silver rings are exempt because they are used for permissible purposes, akin to everyday clothing.
The Shafi'i school analogizes jewelry to clothing, which has no zakat.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i reasoning: jewelry is mubah (permissible) use, similar to clothing; since clothing is not subject to zakat, jewelry should not be either.
This is an argument by analogy (qiyas).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi counter-argument: the cause (sabab) for zakat is mal nam—wealth inherently capable of growth. Gold and silver have this capacity by their very nature (khilqatan), which is not negated by use.
The Hanafi cite Quran 9:34 and three hadiths as dalil naqli.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Assess the practical consequence: a woman owning gold jewelry must pay zakat annually according to the Hanafi school, but is exempt under the Shafi'i school.
This difference directly impacts millions of Muslims who own gold jewelry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَفِي تبرِ الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ وَحُلَيْهِمَا وَانِيهِمَا الزَّكوةُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعُى لا تَجِبُ فِى حُليّ النِّسَاءِ وَخَاتَمِ الْفِضَّةِ للرجال لأنَّهُ مَبْتَدِلٌ فِي مُبَاحٍ فَشَابَهَ ثِيَابُ الْبَذَلَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ السَّبَبَ مَالٌ نام و دَلِيلُ اليَمَاءِ مَوْجُودٌ وَهُوَ الْإِعْدَادُ لِلتِّجَارَةِ خِلْقَةً وَالدَّلِيلُ هُوَ الْمُعْتَبَرُ بِخَلافِ القِيَابِ وَاحْتَجُّوا بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى {وَالَّذِيْنَ يَكْبِرُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ وَلَا يُنفِقُونَها فِى سبيل الله فَبَشِّرْهُمْ بِعَذَاب اليم} (التوبة: 33) وعمومه يشمل الحلي وغيره. وَعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عن جدَّه أَنَّ امْرَأَةً أَتَتِ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَمَعَهَا بِنتُ لَهَا وَفِي يَدِابْنَتِهَا مَسْكَتَان غَلِيظَتَانِ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ فَقَالَ لَهَا أَتُعْطِينَ زَكَوةَ هَذَا قَالَتْ لَا قَالَ أَيَسُرُّكَ أَنْ يُسَوِّرَكَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِمَا يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ سَوَارَيْنِ مِنْ نَارٍ قَالَ فَخَلَعَتُهَا فَالْقَتْهُمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَقَالَتْ هُمَا لِلَّهِ وَلِرَسُولِهِ. وَعَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ قَالَتْ كُنْ أَلْبَسُ أَوْضَاخًا مِنْ ذَهَبٍ فَقُلْتُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ اَكَنزٌ هُوَ فَقَالَ مَا يَبْلُغُ أَنْ تُؤْدَى زَكَوتُهُ فَلَيْسَ بِكَنْزٍ. وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ دَخَلْتُ عَلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَرَأَى فِي يَدِى فَتَحَاتٍ مِنْ وَرِقٍ فَقَالَ مَاهَذَا قُلْتُ صَنَعْتُهُنَّ أَتَزَيَّنُ لَكَ بِهِنَّ قَالَ أَفَتُؤَدِّينَ زَكَوتَهُنَّ قُلْتُ لَا فَقَالَ حَسْبُكَ مِنَ النَّارِ
He said: In uncoined gold and silver (tibr), their jewelry, and their utensils, zakat is due. Al-Shafi'i said: Zakat is not obligatory on women's jewelry and a man's silver ring because it is used for permissible purposes, resembling ordinary clothing. And our (Hanafi) proof is that the cause (sabab) is growth-capable wealth (mal nam), and the evidence of growth exists—namely, it is inherently prepared for trade (khilqatan). And the evidence is considered, contrary to clothing. They also argued with Allah's saying: 'And those who hoard gold and silver and spend them not in the way of Allah—give them tidings of a painful punishment' (9:33), and its generality includes jewelry and other items. And from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: A woman came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) with her daughter, and the daughter had two thick bracelets of gold. He asked: 'Do you give zakat on this?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'Would it please you that Allah will give you two bracelets of fire on the Day of Judgment?' She then removed them and threw them to the Prophet, saying: 'They are for Allah and His Messenger.' And from Umm Salama: She said: 'I used to wear gold anklets. I asked: O Messenger of Allah, is this a treasure (kanz)?' He said: 'Whatever reaches the zakat threshold and you pay its zakat is not a treasure.' And from Aisha: She said: 'I entered upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and he saw silver rings on my hands. He asked: What is this? I said: I made them to adorn myself for you. He asked: Do you pay zakat on them? I said: No. He said: Sufficient for you is the fire of Hell.'
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on zakat for gold and silver, particularly when fashioned into jewelry (huliy) or utensils (aniyah), followed by a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The text is part of a sharh (commentary) on al-Hidayah, expanding the matn. The Hanafi position: zakat is obligatory on all forms of gold and silver, whether raw (tibr), minted coins, jewelry, or utensils, provided they reach the nisab. The Shafi'i position exempts women's jewelry and men's silver rings because such items are mubah (permissible) and akin to everyday clothing (thiyab al-badhalah), which have no zakat. The Hanafi response: the cause for zakat is mal nam—wealth capable of growth. Growth is indicated either inherently (khilqatan), as in gold and silver which are naturally suitable for trade, or actually (fi'lan) through trade. In jewelry, the inherent growth potential (i'dad lil-tijara khilqatan) remains, so zakat is due. The Quranic verse (9:33) is cited as a general proof: the threat of painful punishment applies to all who hoard gold and silver, including jewelry, unless they pay zakat. Three hadiths are then presented: (1) The story of a woman with her daughter's gold bracelets—the Prophet (saw) asked about zakat, and when she said no, he warned of fire bracelets. (2) Umm Salama's hadith about gold anklets—the Prophet clarified that if zakat is paid, it is not a hidden treasure (kanz). (3) Aisha's hadith about silver rings—the Prophet again asked about zakat and warned of hellfire when she said no. These hadiths strongly support the Hanafi position that jewelry is subject to zakat. The authority_weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as the matn is from al-Hidayah, which relies on the six core books of Imam Muhammad. The mufta bihi (operative position) is the Hanafi view: zakat is obligatory on all gold and silver jewelry and utensils, regardless of use.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Uncoined gold or silver, raw metal not yet minted into coins or shaped into objects.
حلية (huliy): Jewelry; ornaments made of gold or silver worn for adornment.
مال نام (mal naam): Wealth that has the capacity to grow, either inherently (like gold/silver) or through trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary reason zakat is obligatory on gold and silver jewelry?
A) Because it is used for adornment which is a form of wealth display.
B) Because gold and silver are inherently growth-capable wealth (mal nam), and the capacity for growth exists even when fashioned into jewelry.
C) Because the Prophet (saw) specifically commanded zakat on all gold and silver items.
D) Because jewelry is considered a trade good.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is obligatory on all gold and silver jewelry and utensils because growth capacity is inherent, and the hadiths of the Prophet (peace be upon him) confirm this obligation.

Zakat on Trade Goods: Ruling, Proof, and Condition
Ruling with proof and condition for zakat on trade goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for trade goods, explain the proof from the hadith and the qiyas analogy, and identify the condition of trade intention.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods is obligatory when their value meets nisab, proven by a hadith and analogy to gold/silver.

Many Muslims own merchandise for business. Does this inventory attract zakat? The Hanafi school, based on a direct hadith and legal reasoning, rules that all trade goods are subject to zakat if they reach the nisab and the owner had trade intent. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the key condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the ruling: zakat is wajib on all trade goods (‘urud al-tijara) of any kind. Note that the obligation applies regardless of the type of merchandise.
The text says 'kaanatin ma kaanat' – of any kind.
2
Examine the proof from the Sunnah
Cite the hadith that commands evaluating trade goods and paying 2.5% (5 dirhams per 200). Recognize that this is an ahad hadith, but it is sufficient for establishing a wajib ruling in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is cited as: 'yugawwimuha fa yu’adda min kulli mi’atay dirhamin khamsata darahima'.
3
Understand the qiyas analogy
The text explains that trade goods are prepared for growth (i’dad lil-istinma’) by human intent, analogous to gold and silver which are prepared by Shari’ah. This qiyas justifies applying the same zakat rules to trade goods.
The analogy is between 'al-mu’add bi i’dad al-’abd' and 'al-mu’add bi i’dad al-shar’'.
4
Note the condition of trade intention
Intention of trade (niyyat al-tijara) at the time of acquisition is a necessary condition for the goods to be considered trade goods. Without it, the goods are personal property and not subject to zakat.
The text says 'wa yushtartu niyyat al-tijara li yathbuta al-i’dad'.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab agreement
All four schools agree on the obligation of zakat on trade goods with nisab and hawl. Minor differences exist on valuation methods and timing of intention, but the core obligation is unanimously accepted.
The disagreement is over details like valuation at cost vs. market price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي الْعُرُوضِ الزكوةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِى عُرُوضِ التِّجَارَةِ كَائِنَةٌ مَا كَانَتْ إِذَا بَلَغَتْ قِيْمَتُهَا نِصَابًا مِنَ الْوَرَقِ أَوِ الذَّهَبِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ فِيهَا يُقَوَّمُهَا فَيُؤَدَّى مِنْ كُلَّ مِائَتَى دِرْهَمٍ خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَلِأَنَّهَا مُعَدَّةٌ لِلِاسْتِنُمَاءِ بِاعْدَادِ الْعَبْدِ فَأَشْبَهَتِ الْمَعَدَّ بِاعْدَادِ الشَّرْعِ وَيُشْتَرَطُ نِيَّةُ التِّجَارَةِ لِيَثْبُتَ الْإِعْدَادُ
Chapter on trade goods (al-'urud). Zakat is obligatory on trade goods of any kind when their value reaches a nisab of silver or gold, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'He evaluates them and pays five dirhams for every two hundred dirhams.' And because they are prepared for growth by the preparation of the slave (i.e., human intent), so they resemble what is prepared by the preparation of the law (i.e., gold and silver). And the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijara) is a condition to establish the preparation.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the ruling on zakat for 'urud al-tijara—merchandise or trade goods. The text is a complete legal unit: it states the ruling, gives the proof, and mentions a condition. The ruling: zakat is wajib on all types of trade goods (clothes, furniture, animals, etc.) provided their total market value reaches the nisab threshold of silver (200 dirhams) or gold (20 mithqal). The proof is a hadith (mawquf or marfu' depending on narration) that instructs a trader to evaluate his merchandise at the end of the year and pay zakat at the rate of 5 dirhams per 200 (i.e., 2.5%). The rationale: trade goods are prepared for growth (i'dad lil-istinma') by the trader's intent, making them analogous (qiyas) to gold and silver, which are prepared for growth by Islamic law (shar'). The condition: intention of trade (niyyat al-tijara) at the time of acquisition is necessary to establish that the goods are held for trade. If one buys goods for personal use but later resells, the majority (including Hanafi) require intention from the start. This is part of Zahir al-Riwayah. The mufta bihi: zakat is due on trade goods if the annual value meets nisab and the owner had trade intent.

Key Terms
عروض التجارة (urud al-tijara): Merchandise or trade goods—any movable property intended for sale and profit.
نصاب (nisab): Minimum threshold of wealth (e.g., 200 dirhams silver or 20 mithqal gold) above which zakat becomes obligatory.
نية التجارة (niyyat al-tijara): Intent when acquiring property to use it for trade and profit, not personal use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary condition for trade goods ('urud al-tijara) to be subject to zakat according to this passage?
A) The goods must be non-perishable.
B) The owner must have the intention of trade (niyyat al-tijara) at the time of acquiring the goods.
C) The goods must have been purchased with gold or silver.
D) The goods must be agricultural produce.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on trade goods is wajib on the market value at end of hawl, provided trade intention was present at acquisition.
