Zakat Is Wajib on Gold and Silver Jewelry: The Prophetic Proofs
Presents hadith proofs that zakat is due on gold and silver jewelry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for jewelry and explain the evidence from the three hadiths presented.

Core Idea
Jewelry made of gold or silver reaching nisab is subject to zakat, as proven by explicit hadith.

Many assume that jewelry worn for adornment is exempt from zakat. However, the Hanafi school holds it wajib, relying on clear prophetic instructions. This lesson examines the three hadiths that form the basis of this ruling and shows how they establish the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The core question: Is zakat obligatory on gold and silver jewelry used for personal adornment? Recognize that this is a point of ikhtilaf between schools.
The Hanafi position is that zakat is wajib, not fard, due to the zanni nature of the evidence.
2
Analyze the First Hadith (Woman with Bangles)
The Prophet asks a woman if she pays zakat on her daughter's gold bangles. When she says no, he warns of fire bracelets. She then gives them away. This implies zakat is due; otherwise the warning is unjustified.
The woman's action of removing the bangles indicates she understood the obligation.
3
Analyze the Second Hadith (Umm Salamah)
Umm Salamah asks if her gold anklets are kanz (treasure). The Prophet replies that jewelry reaching nisab and whose zakat is paid is not kanz. This implies that zakat must be paid to avoid the punishment of kanz.
Here 'kanz' refers to wealth on which zakat is not paid, threatened with punishment.
4
Analyze the Third Hadith (Aisha)
The Prophet sees silver rings on Aisha and asks if she pays zakat. When she says no, he says 'Sufficient for you is the fire of Hell.' This direct threat strongly indicates obligation.
The phrases 'sufficient for you is the fire' is a severe warning, indicating wajib status.
5
Draw the Conclusion
All three hadiths together make a strong case that zakat is wajib on gold and silver jewelry, regardless of whether it is for use or saved. The Hanafi school relies on these proofs and holds this ruling as mufta bihi.
Contrast with the Shafi'i view that exempts jewelry intended for personal use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب التركوة اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم يَدِابْنَتِهَا مَسْكَتَان غَلِيظَتَانِ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ فَقَالَ لَهَا اَ تُعْطِين زَكَوةَ هَذَا قَالَتْ لَا قَالَ اَيَسُرُّكَ أَنْ يُسَوِّرَكَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِمَا يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ سَوَارَيْنِ مِنْ نَارٍ قَالَ فَخَلَعَتُهَا فَالْقَتْهُمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَقَالَتْ هُمَا لِلَّهِ وَلِرَسُولِهِ. (فتح التقدير. شرح نقایه البس یعنی ایک عورت اپنی صاحبزادی کو لے کر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں حاضر ہوئی اور اس کی صاحبزادی کے ہاتھ میں سونے کے دو موٹے کڑے تھے رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تو اس کی زکوۃ دیتی ہے اس نے کہا کہ نہیں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تجھے یہ اچھا معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے قیامت کے دن ان کے عوض تجھے آگ کے دو کنگن پہنائے ۔ پس اس نے کڑوں کو نکال کر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی خدمت میں ڈال دیا۔ اور کہا کہ یہ دونوں اللہ اور اس کے رسول کے لئے ہیں۔ اس روایت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ زیور میں بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے۔ حضرت ام سلمہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا کی حدیث سے بھی اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے عَنْ اُمّ سَلَمَةَ قَالَت کن أوْ ضَاخَامِنُ ذَهَبٍ فَقُلْتُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ اَكَنرٌ هُوَ فَقَالَ مَايُبْلَعُ أنْ تُؤْذِى زَكَوتَهُ فَرَكَى فَلَيْسَ بِكَنْزِام سلمہ کہتی ہیں کہ میں سونے کی پسلیاں پہنتی تھی میں نے کہا کہ اے اللہ کے رسول کیا یہ بھی کنز ہے فرمایا کہ جو نصاب زکوۃ کو پہنچ جائے اور تو اس کی زکوۃ دیدے تو وہ کنز نہیں ہے حضرت ام سلمہ نے کنز سے اس کنز کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے جس پر عذاب الیم کی وعید آئی ہے یہ حدیث بھی زیور میں وجوب زکوۃ پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ حدیث عائشہؓ بھی اس کی مؤید ہے عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ دَخَلْتُ عَلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَرَأَى فِي يَدِى فَتَحَامَتْ مِنْ وَرِقٍ فَقَالَ مَاهَذَا قُلْتُ صَنَعْتُهُنَّ اَتَزَيَّنُ لَكَ بِهِنَّ قَالَ أَفَتُو دَيْنِ زَكَوتَهُنَّ قُلْتُ لَا فَقَالَ حَسْبُكَ مِنَ النَّارِ حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا کہ میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت اقدس میں حاضر ہوئی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دیکھا کہ میرے ہاتھ میں چاندی کے چھلے ہیں پھر فرمایا یہ کیا ہے میں نے کہا کہ میں نے ان کو اس لئے بنایا ہے تا کہ ان کے ساتھ آپ کے لئے آراستہ ہو جاؤں آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ان کی زکوۃ بھی دیتی ہو میں نے کہا کہ نہیں فرمایا کہ تجھ کو جہنم کی آگ کافی ہے اس روایت سے بھی زیور میں زکوۃ کا واجب ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ جمیل احمد غفرلہ
Book of Zakat. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidaya, Volume Three. 'A woman brought her daughter to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the daughter had two thick bangles of gold. He said to her, 'Do you pay zakat on this?' She said, 'No.' He said, 'Would it please you for Allah to encircle you with two bracelets of fire on the Day of Judgment?' He said, 'So she removed them and threw them to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said, 'They are for Allah and His Messenger.'' (Fath al-Taqdeer, Sharh Nuqayah) Meaning: A woman came with her daughter to the service of the Prophet, and her daughter had two thick gold bangles. The Prophet said, 'Do you pay zakat on this?' She said, 'No.' The Prophet said, 'Would it please you that Allah will give you two fire bangles in exchange on the Day of Judgment?' So she removed the bangles and threw them to the Prophet, saying, 'These are for Allah and His Messenger.' From this narration it is known that zakat is wajib on jewelry. The hadith of Umm Salamah also supports this: From Umm Salamah, she said, 'I wore anklets of gold.' She said, 'O Messenger of Allah, is it treasure?' He said, 'Whatever reaches the nisab of zakat and you pay its zakat, then it is not treasure.' She explained that treasure refers to that which the severe punishment is threatened upon. This hadith also indicates the obligation of zakat on jewelry. The hadith of Aisha also supports it: From Aisha, she said, 'I entered upon the Prophet and he saw on my hands rings of silver. He said, 'What is this?' I said, 'I made them to adorn myself for you.' He said, 'Do you pay zakat on them?' I said, 'No.' He said, 'Sufficient for you is the fire of Hell.' This narration also proves that zakat is wajib on jewelry. Jamil Ahmad Ghafara llah.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that zakat is wajib on jewelry. The author presents three hadiths: (1) The hadith of the woman with gold bangles, where the Prophet explicitly asks about zakat and the woman gives them away upon realizing the consequence. (2) The hadith of Umm Salamah, where the Prophet clarifies that jewelry reaching nisab and whose zakat is paid is not kanz (hoarded treasure). (3) The hadith of Aisha, where the Prophet tells her that if she does not pay zakat on her silver rings, she will face hellfire. These proofs establish that gold and silver jewelry, even for personal use, is subject to zakat. The Hanafi school holds this as wajib, based on these ahadith.

Key Terms
زكوة (zakāh): Obligatory charity on wealth, specifically gold and silver jewelry in this context.
كنز (kanz): Hoarded treasure on which zakat is not paid, subject to punishment.
نصاب (niṣāb): Minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is still considered kanz.
B) It is not kanz.
C) It must be given away.
D) No zakat is due on it.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold and silver jewelry is wajib in the Hanafi school, based on explicit hadith that do not exempt personal use.

Zakat on Trade Goods: The Valuation Currency Dispute
Defines zakat on trade goods and presents ikhtilaf on valuation currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on zakat for trade goods and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding valuation currency.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods is wajib when value reaches nisab; the currency of valuation is disputed among the Hanafi masters.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the obligation of zakat on trade goods and then presents the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute on how to value those goods for zakat. We will first understand the conditions for obligation, then analyse the three different positions on valuation currency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (zakat on trade goods) and its hukm level (wajib).
The ruling is clear: zakat is wajib on all trade goods when conditions are met.
2
Locate the proofs for obligation
Identify the dalil cited: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding valuation and payment, and the qiyas to gold and silver as growth-seeking wealth.
The hadith is primary; qiyas supports it.
3
Understand the condition of intention
Note that niyyah (intention of trade) at the time of purchase is a condition for the goods to be considered trade goods.
If intention is made later, it must be accompanied by a trade act.
4
Analyze the valuation dispute
The core issue: once nisab is confirmed, with which currency (silver or gold) should the value be estimated? There are three positions from the Hanafi imams.
Each imam has a specific criterion: most beneficial (Abu Hanifa), purchase currency (Abu Yusuf), or prevalent currency (Muhammad).
5
Compare the positions
List the views of Abu Hanifa (two narrations: choice or most beneficial for poor), Abu Yusuf (by purchase currency if currency, else prevalent), and Muhammad (always prevalent).
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in zakat amount depending on which currency is used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي الْعُرُوضِ ترجمه ی فصل سامان ( کی زکوۃ کے بیان میں ) ہے ساز و سامان میں زکوة ... نصاب زکوة و مقدار زکوة الزكوةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِى عُرُوضِ التِّجَارَةِ كَائِنَةٌ مَا كَانَتْ إِذَا بَلَغَتْ قِيْمَتُهَا نِصَابًا مِنَ الْوَرَقِ أَوِ الذَّهَبِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ فِيهَا يُقَوَمُهَا فَيُؤدَى مِنْ كُلَّ مِانَتَى دِرْهَم خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَلَانَّهَا مَعَدَّةِ لِلاسْتِنُمَاء بِاعْدَادِ الْعَبْدِ فَاشْبَة المَعَدُّ بِاعْدَادِ الشَّرع وَيُشْتَرَطُ نِيَّةُ التَّجَارَةِ لِيَثْبُتَ الْإِعْدَادُ ترجمہ تجارت کے سامان میں زکوۃ واجب ہے سامان کوئی بھی ہو بشر طیکہ اس کی قیمت چاندی یا سونے کے نصاب کو پہنچ جائے ۔ کیونکہ تجارت کے سامان کے بارے میں رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سامان کی قیمت لگالے پھر ہر دو سو درہم سے پانچ درہم ادا کرے۔ اور اس لئے کہ سامان تجارت بھی بندے کے مہیا کرنے سے نمو طلب کرنے کے لئے مہیا کیا گیا ہے پس اس کے مشابہ ہو گیا جو شریعت کے مہیا کرنے سے مہیا ہوا ہے اور تجارت کی نیت شرط ہے تاکہ نامی ہونا ثابت ہو۔ تشریح عروض عرض کی جمع ہے معنی ہیں چاندی اور سونے کے علاوہ سامان دنیا کے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ تجارت کا سامان خواہ کسی بھی قسم کا ہو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہے بشرطیکہ اس کی قیمت چاندی یا سونے کے نصاب کو پہنچ جاتی ہو ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سامان تجارت کی قیمت لگا کر ہر دو سو درہم میں سے پانچ درہم زکوۃ ادا کرے۔ اور سمرہ بن جندب سے مروی ہے اِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَا مُرُنَا أَنْ نَخْرُجَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنَ الَّذِى يَعَدُّ لِلبيع یعنی رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم حکم فرماتے کہ ہم لوگ اس چیز کی زکوۃ نکالیں جو بیج کے واسطے مہیا ہو ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ سامان کے اندر بندے کے تجارت کی نیت کرنے سے وہ سامان بھی مال نامی ہو گیا ہے اور چونکہ مال نامی میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے سامان تجارت میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی جیسے چاندی اور سونے میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ من جانب شرع مال نامی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں نمو ثابت کرنے کے لئے سامان خریدتے وقت تجارت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے چنانچہ اگر خریدتے وقت تجارت کی نیت نہیں کی گئی ہے بلکہ مالک ہونے کے بعد نیت کی ہے تو نیت کے ساتھ فعل تجارت کا مقترن ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے کہ محض نیست کافی نہیں ہوتی بلکہ نیت کے ساتھ فعل کا متصل ہونا بھی ضروری ہے۔ سامان میں انفع للفقراء سے قیمت لگائی جائے گی ثُمَّ قَالَ يُقَوَمُهَا بِمَا هُوَ أَنْفَعُ لِلْمَسَاكِينِ اِحْتِيَاطًا لِحَقِّ الْفُقَرَاءِ قَالَ وَهذَا رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ فِي الْأَصْلِ خَيَّرَهُ لأنَّ الثَّمَنَيْنِ فِى تَقْدِيرِ قِيمِ الْأشْيَاءِ بِهِمَا سَوَاءٌ وَ تَفْسِيرُ الْأَنْفَع أَنْ يُقَوَمُهَا بِمَا يَبْلُغُ نِصَابًا وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوْسَفَ أَنَّهُ يُقَوَمُهَا بمَا اشْتَرى إِنْ كَانَ الثَّمَنُ مِنَ التَّقَوُدِ لأنَّهُ أبْلَعُ فِى مَعْرِفَةِ الْمَالِيَّةِ وَإِن اشْتَرَاهَا بِغَيْرِ التَّقَوُدِ قَوْمَهَا بِالتَّقْدِ الْغَالِبِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ يُقَرِّمُهَا بِالنَّقْدِ الغَالِبِ عَلَى كُلّ حَالِ كَمَا فِي الْمَغْضُوبِ وَالْمَسْتَهَلَكِ ترجمہ پھر امام قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ سامان کی قیمت ایسے نقد سے لگائے جو مساکین کے لئے زیادہ نافع ہو۔ (یہ حکم ) فقراء کے حق کی وجہ سے احتیاط پر مبنی ہے مصنف نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت ہے اور مبسوط میں (امام صاحب نے ) مالک کو اختیار دیا ہے کیونکہ اشیاء کی قیمتوں کا اندازہ کرنے میں دونوں نقد برابر ہیں۔ اور انفع کی تفسیر یہ ہے کہ ایسے نقد کے ساتھ قیمت لگائے جس کے ساتھ اندازہ کرنے میں نصاب پورا ہو جاتا ہو ۔ اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ اس سامان کی قیمت ایسے نقد کے ساتھ لگائے جس کے عوض خریدا تھا بشر طیکہ ثمن نقود میں سے دیا ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ مالیت پہچاننے میں زیادہ ابلغ ہے اور اگر سامان کو نقود کے سواء کسی اور چیز کے عوض خریدا ہو تو ایسے نقد سے اندازہ کرے جس کا چلن سب سے زیادہ ہو۔ اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ ہر حال میں زیادہ چلن والے نقد کیساتھ قیمت کا اندازہ کرے جیسے مغصوب اور مستبلک میں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح گذشتہ مسئلہ میں کہا گیا ہے کہ سامان تجارت میں زکوۃ واجب کرنے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس کی قیمت چاندی کے نصاب کو پہنچ جائے یا سونے کے نصاب کو لیکن اب سوال یہ ہے کہ قیمت کا اندازہ چاندی یعنی در اہم کے ساتھ کرے یا سونے یعنی دنا نیر کے ساتھ، تو اس بارے میں چار قول ہیں۔ پہلا قول جو امام ابو حنیفہ سے امالی میں ایک روایت بھی ہے یہ ہے کہ سامان کی قیمت کا اندازہ ان
Section on Trade Goods. Translation: This section is about zakat on goods. Zakat is obligatory on trade goods, whatever they may be, when their value reaches a nisab of silver or gold, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'He values them and then pays from every two hundred dirhams five dirhams.' And because trade goods are prepared by the servant for seeking growth, so they resemble what is prepared by the Sharia. And the intention of trade is required to establish growth. Explanation: 'Urud' is the plural of 'ard', meaning goods of the world other than silver and gold. The issue: Zakat is wajib on all types of trade goods when their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. The proof: The Prophet said to value the goods and pay five dirhams per two hundred dirhams. Also from Samurah ibn Jundub: 'The Prophet used to command us to give charity from what is prepared for sale.' Another proof: When a person intends trade, the goods become growth-seeking wealth, and zakat is due on growth-seeking wealth like silver and gold which are growth-seeking by Sharia. The author of Hidaya says: Intention of trade at the time of purchase is a condition to establish growth. If not intended at purchase but later, the act of trade must accompany the intention, because mere intention is not sufficient. The valuation should be with what is more beneficial for the poor. Then he said: He values them with what is most beneficial for the needy, out of caution for the right of the poor. He said: This is a narration from Abu Hanifa. In the original work, he gave the owner a choice because both currencies are equal in estimating values. The interpretation of 'most beneficial' is that he values them with what reaches the nisab. From Abu Yusuf: He values them with the currency with which he purchased, if the price was from currencies, because that is more revealing of value. If he purchased with other than currency, he values with the prevalent currency. From Muhammad: He values them with the prevailing currency in all cases, as in the case of usurped or destroyed goods. Commentary: It was said in the previous issue that for zakat on trade goods, it is necessary that its value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. Now the question is whether to value with silver (dirhams) or gold (dinar). There are four opinions. The first opinion, which is a narration from Abu Hanifa in the Amali, is that the value of the goods is estimated with... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage covers the chapter on trade goods (urud al-tijarah) and its zakat ruling. The author first states the ruling: zakat is wajib on all trade goods when their total market value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. The proofs include a hadith that the Prophet ordered valuation and payment of 2.5% (5 dirhams per 200 dirhams), and the hadith of Samurah ordering zakat on goods prepared for sale. Analogy (qiyas) is also used: trade goods become 'growing wealth' (mal nami) by human effort, similar to silver and gold which are growing by Sharia. A condition is that the intention of trade must be present at the time of purchase; if not, the intention must be accompanied by a trade act later. Then the passage delves into a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation currency: Abu Hanifa gives two views—one is to value with the currency most beneficial to the poor (to ensure nisab is reached), another narration gives owner choice. Abu Yusuf says value by the currency used to purchase the goods if it was currency; otherwise use the prevalent currency. Imam Muhammad says always use the prevalent currency. The commentary explains that the dispute arises because we need to know if the value reaches nisab in either silver or gold.

Key Terms
عروض التجارة (ʿurūḍ al-tijārah): Goods and merchandise intended for trade, excluding gold and silver coins.
نصاب (niṣāb): Minimum value threshold: 200 dirhams silver or 20 mithqal gold.
نقود (nuqūd): Currencies (gold and silver coins) used as payment.
أنفع للفقراء (anfaʿu lil-fuqarāʾ): What is more beneficial for the poor; a criterion for valuation to ensure zakat is calculated favorably for recipients.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how should trade goods be valued for zakat?
A) By the currency used to purchase the goods.
B) By the currency most beneficial for the poor.
C) By the prevalent currency in all cases.
D) By the owner's choice of gold or silver.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has multiple valid positions on valuation currency for zakat on trade goods; the prevalent currency view is often relied upon in practice.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
6 min
Valuation of Trade Goods for Zakat: Four Hanafi Opinions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat valuation currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi opinions on valuing trade goods for zakat and explain the basis and practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods is valued by either the most beneficial for poor, owner's choice, purchase currency, or prevalent currency.

When a trader's inventory reaches the nisab threshold, zakat becomes obligatory. But which currency should be used to measure that value—dirhams (silver) or dinars (gold)? The Hanafi school offers four valid answers, each rooted in a different legal reasoning. This lesson walks you through the ikhtilaf and its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation and condition
Start by recognizing that zakat on trade goods is wajib when the value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. The intention to trade at purchase (or combined with a trading act) is a condition.
The nisab is 200 dirhams or 20 dinars.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf
The key dispute: when valuing trade goods, should we use dirhams or dinars? The answer affects both nisab and zakat amount.
3
State the four opinions
List the four positions: (1) most beneficial for the poor (narration from Abu Hanifah), (2) owner's choice (Al-Asl), (3) purchase currency (Abu Yusuf), (4) prevalent currency (Muhammad).
Opinions 1 and 2 are attributed to Abu Hanifah; 3 and 4 are from the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the basis of each
Examine the reasoning behind each opinion: precaution for the poor (1), equality of currencies (2), accuracy of known price (3), and qiyas on huquq al-ibad (4).
Muhammad's qiyas uses the prevalent currency as a standard, analogous to usurpation cases.
5
Identify the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: depending on the method, the trader may pay more or less zakat, or even avoid it if valuation in one currency fails to reach nisab.
Example: If goods are worth 250 dirhams but only 18 dinars, opinion 1 and 4 (if dirhams are prevalent) would trigger zakat; opinion 3 might use dinars if purchased with dinars, avoiding zakat.

پھر ہر دو سو درہم سے پانچ درہم ادا کرے۔ اور اس لئے کہ سامان تجارت بھی بندے کے مہیا کرنے سے نمو طلب کرنے کے لئے مہیا کیا گیا ہے پس اس کے مشابہ ہو گیا جو شریعت کے مہیا کرنے سے مہیا ہوا ہے اور تجارت کی نیت شرط ہے تاکہ نامی ہونا ثابت ہو۔ تشریح عروض عرض کی جمع ہے معنی ہیں چاندی اور سونے کے علاوہ سامان دنیا کے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ تجارت کا سامان خواہ کسی بھی قسم کا ہو اس میں زکوۃ واجب ہے بشرطیکہ اس کی قیمت چاندی یا سونے کے نصاب کو پہنچ جاتی ہو ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سامان تجارت کی قیمت لگا کر ہر دو سو درہم میں سے پانچ درہم زکوۃ ادا کرے۔ اور سمرہ بن جندب سے مروی ہے اِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَا مُرُنَا أَنْ نَخْرُجَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنَ الَّذِى يَعَدُّ لِلبيع یعنی رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم حکم فرماتے کہ ہم لوگ اس چیز کی زکوۃ نکالیں جو بیج کے واسطے مہیا ہو ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ سامان کے اندر بندے کے تجارت کی نیت کرنے سے وہ سامان بھی مال نامی ہو گیا ہے اور چونکہ مال نامی میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے سامان تجارت میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی جیسے چاندی اور سونے میں زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے کیونکہ یہ من جانب شرع مال نامی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں نمو ثابت کرنے کے لئے سامان خریدتے وقت تجارت کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے چنانچہ اگر خریدتے وقت تجارت کی نیت نہیں کی گئی ہے بلکہ مالک ہونے کے بعد نیت کی ہے تو نیت کے ساتھ فعل تجارت کا مقترن ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے کہ محض نیست کافی نہیں ہوتی بلکہ نیت کے ساتھ فعل کا متصل ہونا بھی ضروری ہے۔ سامان میں انفع للفقراء سے قیمت لگائی جائے گی

اندازہ ان دونوں نقدوں میں سے اس کے ساتھ کرے جس میں فقراء اور مساکین کا نفع ہو۔ مثلاً تجارت کا ایک سامان ہے جو دوسو درہم کا تو ہو جاتا ہے مگر ہیں مثقال کا نہیں ہوتا تو اس کو دراہم کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے اور اگر چاندی گراں ہو اور سونا ارزاں ہو اور وہ سامان ہیں مثقال سونے کی مالیت کو تو پہنچ جاتا ہے مگر دو سو درہم چاندی کی مالیت کو نہیں پہنچتا تو اس کی قیمت کا اندازہ مثاقبیل کے ساتھ کرے نہ کہ دراہم کے ساتھے اس قول کی بنیاد فقراء اور مساکین کے حق کی وجہ سے احتیاط پر ہے۔ یعنی احتیاطاً فقراء کی رعایت کے پیش نظر ایسا کیا جائے گا۔ دوسرا قول جو مبسوط میں مذکور ہے یہ ہے کہ مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے درہم کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے چاہے دینار کے ساتھ اس قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیمت اس لئے لگائی جاتی ہے تا کہ مالیت کی مقدار معلوم ہو سکے اور اس مقصد میں در اہم ودنا نیر دونوں برابر ہیں ۔ لہذا ایک کو دوسرے پر ترجیح نہ ہوگی۔ تیسر اقول امام ابو یوسف کا ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں وہ یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس سامان کو نقدین میں سے جس کے عوض خریدا ہے اس کے ساتھ اس کی قیمت کا اندازہ کرے۔ اگر دراہم کے عوض خریدا تھا تو دراہم کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے اور اگر دنا نیر کے عوض خریدا تھا تو دنا نیر کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے۔ اور اگر در اہم ودنا نیر کے علاوہ کے عوض خریدا تھا تو دراہم ودنا نیر میں سے جس کا رواج اور چلن زیادہ ہو اس کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے۔ اس قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نقدین میں سے جس کے عوض اس سامان کو خریدا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ مالیت کی معرفت زیادہ ہوگی کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ اس نقد کے ساتھ اس کی قیمت ظاہر ہو چکی ہے اس لئے دوسری مرتبہ اندازہ لگانے میں کوئی دقت نہ ہو گی۔ چوتھا قول امام محمد کا ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہر حال میں غالب نقد بلد کے ساتھ قیمت کا اندازہ لگایا جائے گا یعنی نقدین میں سے جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو اسی کے ساتھ قیمت کا اندازہ کرے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے حق میں قیمت کا اندازہ کرنے کو بندہ کے حق میں قیمت کا اندازہ کرنے پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ اور بندوں کے حق میں غالب نقد بلد کے ساتھ اندازہ کیا جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً اگر کسی نے کوئی چیز نصب کی اور وہ غاصب کے پاس سے ضائع ہو گئی اور وہ چیز ذات القیم میں سے ہو تو غاصب پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی ۔ اور قیمت کا انداز و نقدین میں سے اس کے ساتھ کیا جائے گا جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے کسی کا کوئی سامان ہلاک کر دیا اور وہ ذوات القیم میں سے ہو تو ہلاک کرنے والے پر قیمت کا عمان واجب ہوگا۔ اور قیمت کا اندازہ اس کیساتھ کیا جائے گا جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو پس جس طرح حقوق العباد میں قیمتوں کا اندازہ نقد غالب کے ساتھ کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح حقوق اللہ یعنی زکوۃ وغیر ہ ادا کرنے کے لئے بھی قیمتوں کا اندازہ نقد غالب کے ساتھ کیا جائے گا۔
Then for every two hundred dirhams, he pays five dirhams. And because trade goods are also prepared by the servant for seeking growth, so it became similar to what is prepared by the Shari'ah. And the intention of trade is a condition so that growth is established. Explanation: 'Uruḍ is the plural of 'arḍ, meaning goods of the world besides silver and gold. The issue is that trade goods, of whatever kind, zakat is obligatory in them on condition that their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Value the trade goods and pay for every two hundred dirhams five dirhams of zakat.' And it is narrated from Samurah ibn Jundub: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us to give charity from what is prepared for sale.' The second proof is that by the servant's intention of trade, the goods become growing wealth, and since zakat is obligatory on growing wealth, zakat becomes obligatory on trade goods just as it is obligatory on silver and gold because they are growing wealth by Shari'ah. The author of Al-Hidayah says: To establish growth, the intention of trade at the time of purchase is a condition. So if the intention of trade was not made at purchase but after ownership, then the act of trade must be conjoined with the intention. Because mere intention is not sufficient, but connection of the act with intention is also necessary. The goods will be valued by that which is most beneficial for the poor.

Then he said: He values them with what is most beneficial for the poor as a precaution for the right of the poor. He said: This is a narration from Abu Hanifah. And in Al-Asl, he gave him a choice because both currencies are equal in estimating the value of things. And the interpretation of 'most beneficial' is that he values them with that which reaches the nisab. And from Abu Yusuf that he values them with what he bought with, if the price was from currency, because it is more effective in recognizing the monetary value. And if he bought them with other than currency, he values them with the prevalent currency. And from Muhammad that he values them with the prevalent currency in all conditions, as in the case of usurped and destroyed goods. Translation: Then Imam Quduri said: He values the goods with that currency which is more beneficial for the poor. (This ruling) is based on precaution for the right of the poor. The author said: This is a narration from Abu Hanifah, and in Al-Mabsut, the owner is given a choice because both currencies are equal in estimating the value of things. And the interpretation of 'most beneficial' is that he values them with that currency by which the nisab is completed. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he values them with the currency with which he bought, provided the price was from currency, because it is more effective in recognizing the monetary value. And if he bought them with other than currency, he values them with the prevalent currency. And from Muhammad that he values them with the prevalent currency in all conditions, as in the case of usurped and destroyed goods. Explanation: In the previous issue, it was said that for zakat to be obligatory on trade goods, it is necessary that their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. But now the question is whether to estimate the value with silver (dirhams) or gold (dinars). In this regard, there are four opinions. The first opinion, which is also a narration from Abu Hanifah in Al-Amali, is that he values the goods with that one of the two currencies which brings benefit to the poor and needy. For example, a trade good that amounts to two hundred dirhams but not twenty dinars, then he values it with dirhams. And if silver is expensive and gold is cheap, and that good reaches the value of twenty dinars but not two hundred silver dirhams, then he values it with dinars, not dirhams. This opinion is based on precaution for the right of the poor. The second opinion mentioned in Al-Mabsut is that the owner has a choice: he may estimate with dirhams or with dinars. The proof of this opinion is that valuation is done to determine the amount of monetary value, and in this purpose both dirhams and dinars are equal, so there is no preference for one over the other. The third opinion is from Abu Yusuf, and Imam Shafi'i also held it: he says that he estimates the value with the same currency with which he bought the good. If he bought it with dirhams, he estimates with dirhams; if with dinars, with dinars. And if he bought it with something other than dirhams and dinars, then he estimates with the more prevalent currency among dirhams and dinars. The proof of this opinion is that the knowledge of monetary value is greater with the currency with which the good was bought, because its price was once revealed in that currency, so there will be no difficulty in estimating a second time. The fourth opinion is from Muhammad: he says that in all cases, valuation should be done with the prevalent currency of the land, i.e., the currency with greater circulation. His proof is that valuation in the right of Allah is analogized to valuation in the right of servants. And in the rights of servants, valuation is done with the prevalent currency of the land. For example, if someone usurps something and it perishes with the usurper, and the thing is of the category of valuable property (dhāt al-qīm), then the price is obligatory on the usurper, and the valuation is done with the more prevalent of the two currencies. Similarly, if someone destroys someone else's goods and they are of valuable property, the destroyer is liable for the price, and the valuation is done with the prevalent currency. So just as in the rights of servants, valuations are made with the prevalent currency, likewise for fulfilling the rights of Allah, i.e., zakat etc., valuations should also be made with the prevalent currency.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about how to value trade goods for zakat. It begins by establishing the obligation: zakat is due on trade goods if their value reaches the nisab of silver or gold. The proof is from a hadith commanding valuation and payment. The condition of trade intention at purchase is emphasized. Then the main ikhtilaf is presented: when valuing the goods, which currency (dirhams or dinars) should be used? Four opinions are given. (1) A narration from Abu Hanifah in Al-Amali: use the currency most beneficial for the poor— i.e., whichever makes the nisab easier to reach. This is precaution for the rights of the poor. (2) In Al-Asl/Mabsut, Abu Hanifah gives the owner a choice, since both currencies are equivalent for measuring value. (3) Abu Yusuf (and Shafi'i) says: use the purchase currency if it was cash; otherwise use the prevalent currency. (4) Muhammad says: always use the prevalent currency, by analogy (qiyas) with the rights of servants (e.g., usurpation and destruction), where prevalent currency is used. The passage does not explicitly state which is mufta bihi, but Muhammad's view is supported by a clear qiyas.

Key Terms
عروض (ʿurūḍ): Plural of ʿarḍ, meaning all goods of the world except silver and gold; trade goods.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat.
نقد (naqd): Currency, specifically dirhams (silver) and dinars (gold) used as money.
غالب (ghālib): Prevalent, dominant; the currency that is most commonly used in the locality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Abu Hanifah in Al-Amali, how should trade goods be valued for zakat?
A) With the currency in which the goods were purchased
B) With the prevalent currency of the land
C) With the currency that is most beneficial for the poor
D) With the owner's choice of either dirhams or dinars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers four valid methods for valuing trade goods in zakat, each with a distinct legal basis, and the choice of method can affect the amount due.

Nisab Must Be Complete at Both Ends of the Zakat Year
States ruling with rational proof on nisab requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nisab fluctuations during the zakat year and distinguish between total and partial loss of nisab.

Core Idea
Only the start and end of the year matter for nisab; mid-year drops do not void zakat.

Many zakat payers worry when their wealth dips during the year, thinking they may lose the obligation. The Hanafi school provides ease: as long as the nisab is present at the beginning and end of the lunar year, the obligation stands. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the critical exception of total loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and state the core ruling: if nisab is complete at the start and end of the year, mid-year deficiency does not cancel zakat.
Note the key terms: ṭarafā al-ḥawl (two ends of the year).
2
Understand the reasoning (dalīl)
The passage gives a rational proof: it is difficult (shāqq) to require continuous nisab. The cause (sabab) is established at the beginning (inʿiqād) and obligation is at the end (wujūb); the middle is a state of continuation (ḥālat al-baqāʾ).
This is an example of istiḥsān based on hardship.
3
Identify the exception
The passage contrasts the situation where all nisab perishes during the year—then the obligation is void. Only total loss cancels; partial loss does not.
Hence the ruling is not absolute; there is a clear boundary.
4
Compare with other schools
Other madhāhib (e.g., Shāfiʿī) require nisab to be present throughout the year. The Hanafi position eases the duty, but note the cross-madhhab difference.
This has practical implications for fatwa and for Muslims of different schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سال کے اطراف ( ابتداء و انتہاء) میں نصاب کامل ہو تو سال کے درمیان میں نقصان کا اعتبار نہیں وَإِذَا كَانَ النَّصَابُ كَامِلا فِى طَرَقَى الْحُولِ فَتُقْصَانُهُ فِيمَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ لَا يُسْقِطُ الزَّكوة لِأَنَّهُ يَشُقُ إعتبارا لكمال فِي إِثْنَائِهِ أَمَّا لَا بُدَّ مِنْهُ فِى ابْتِدَائِهِ لِلْإِنْعِقَادِ وَ تَحَقَّقِ الْعِنَاءِ وَ فِى انْتِهَائِهِ لِلْوُجُوبِ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ فِيْمَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ حَالَةَ الْبَقَاءِ بِخِلَافِ مَا لَوَهَلَكَ الكُلُّ حَيْثُ يَبْطُلُ حُكْمَ الْحَولِ وَلَا تَحِبُّ الزَّكَوةَ لِإِنْعِدَامِ النِّصَابِ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ الأولى لأنَّ بَعْضَ النِّصَابِ بَاقٍ فَبَقِيَ الْإِنْعِقَادُ ترجمہ اور جب نصاب سال کے دو طرف میں پورا ہو تو اس کے مابین نصاب کا کم ہو جانا ز کوۃ کو ساقط نہیں کرتا کیونکہ درمیان سال میں پورے نصاب کا اعتبار کرنے میں مشقت ہے۔ ہاں ابتدائے سال میں اس کا پورا رہنا ضروری ہے تا کہ سبب منعقد ہو جائے اور غنی
If the nisab is complete at the two ends of the year, then its deficiency in between does not drop the zakat, because it is difficult to consider completion during the year. However, it is necessary at the beginning for the contract to be established and for the verification of wealth, and at the end for obligation. Not so in between because it is a state of continuation. Unlike if all of it perishes, where the ruling of the year becomes void and zakat is not obligatory due to total absence of nisab. Not so in the first issue because part of the nisab remains, so the contract remains. Translation: When the nisab is complete at the two ends of the year, its decrease in between does not drop the zakat, because considering completion in the middle of the year involves hardship. Yes, its completeness at the beginning is necessary for the cause to be contracted and for wealth, and at the end for obligation. Not so in between because it is a state of continuation...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage states a key Zakat ruling: the nisab must be present at the beginning and end of the lunar year (hawl), but fluctuations in between do not affect the obligation. The reasoning is practical: checking the nisab daily would be excessively burdensome. At the start, the nisab is needed to begin the year count and confirm the person is wealthy (ghani). At the end, it is needed to make zakat incumbent. If the entire nisab is lost during the year, then zakat is cancelled. But if only part is lost, the original contract remains because some nisab still exists. This is based on the Hanafi principle of easing the duty of zakat.

Key Terms
طرفا الحول (ṭarafā al-ḥawl): The two ends of the lunar year: the beginning and the end.
انعقاد (inʿiqād): The formation/establishment of the cause (sabab) of zakat, i.e., the start of the year count.
العناء (al-ʿināʾ): Wealth or richness; verification that the person is wealthy enough to be liable for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what happens to the zakat obligation if the nisab decreases during the middle of the year but is complete at the beginning and end?
A) Zakat is cancelled because the nisab must be present throughout the entire year
B) Zakat is still obligatory because the ends of the year determine obligation
C) Zakat becomes optional at the owner's discretion
D) Zakat is reduced proportionally based on the deficiency

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires nisab only at the start and end of the zakat year, easing the obligation while preserving it.

Four Hanafi Views on Valuing Trade Goods for Zakat Nisab
States four scholarly opinions on currency valuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi opinions on which currency to use for valuing trade goods for zakat nisab and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Zakat valuation of trade goods can use the currency most beneficial to the poor, the owner's choice, the purchase currency, or the dominant local currency — each with a proof.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents four scholarly opinions within the Hanafi school regarding the assessment of trade goods ('urud al-tijara) for zakat nisab. This is a classic example of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, where each view is supported by a different legal reasoning (ta'lil). Understanding these opinions and their proofs helps a student appreciate the richness and analytical depth of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four opinions
Read the passage and list the four opinions: (1) use the currency more beneficial to the poor, (2) owner's choice, (3) Abu Yusuf: use the currency of purchase, (4) Imam Muhammad: use the dominant currency of the locality.
2
Extract the evidence (dalil) for each
For each opinion, find the reasoning given: (1) precaution for the poor, (2) equality of both currencies for valuation, (3) greater knowledge of value with purchase currency, (4) analogy to huquq al-'ibad where dominant currency is used.
3
Compare the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Consider a scenario where the dominant currency differs from the purchase currency. Each opinion yields a different valuation, affecting whether the nisab is met and how much zakat is due.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preferred view)
Note that the passage concludes with Imam Muhammad's view and the qiyas to civil rights, suggesting this is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Source Text

ساتھ اندازہ کرے چاہے دینار کے ساتھ اس قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیمت اس لئے لگائی جاتی ہے تا کہ مالیت کی مقدار معلوم ہو سکے اور اس مقصد میں در اہم ودنا نیر دونوں برابر ہیں ۔ لہذا ایک کو دوسرے پر ترجیح نہ ہوگی۔ تیسر اقول امام ابو یوسف کا ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں وہ یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس سامان کو نقدین میں سے جس کے عوض خریدا ہے اس کے ساتھ اس کی قیمت کا اندازہ کرے۔ اگر دراہم کے عوض خریدا تھا تو دراہم کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے اور اگر دنا نیر کے عوض خریدا تھا تو دنا نیر کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے۔ اور اگر در اہم ودنا نیر کے علاوہ کے عوض خریدا تھا تو دراہم ودنا نیر میں سے جس کا رواج اور چلن زیادہ ہو اس کے ساتھ اندازہ کرے۔ اس قول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نقدین میں سے جس کے عوض اس سامان کو خریدا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ مالیت کی معرفت زیادہ ہوگی کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ اس نقد کے ساتھ اس کی قیمت ظاہر ہو چکی ہے اس لئے دوسری مرتبہ اندازہ لگانے میں کوئی دقت نہ ہو گی۔ چوتھا قول امام محمد کا ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہر حال میں غالب نقد بلد کے ساتھ قیمت کا اندازہ لگایا جائے گا یعنی نقدین میں سے جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو اسی کے ساتھ قیمت مثلاً اگر کسی نے کوئی چیز نصب کی اور وہ غاصب کے پاس سے ضائع ہو گئی اور وہ چیز ذات القیم میں سے ہو تو غاصب پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی ۔ اور قیمت کا انداز و نقدین میں سے اس کے ساتھ کیا جائے گا جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے کسی کا کوئی سامان ہلاک کر دیا اور وہ ذوات القیم میں سے ہو تو ہلاک کرنے والے پر قیمت کا عمان واجب ہوگا۔ اور قیمت کا اندازہ اس کیساتھ کیا جائے گا جس کا چلن زیادہ ہو پس جس طرح حقوق العباد میں قیمتوں کا اندازہ نقد غالب کے ساتھ کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح حقوق اللہ یعنی زکوۃ وغیر ہ ادا کرنے کے لئے بھی قیمتوں کا اندازہ نقد غالب کے ساتھ کیا جائے گا۔
Regarding zakat, he should use that currency which brings benefit to the poor and needy. For example, a trade good worth two hundred dirhams but not twenty mithqal of gold, then assess it with dirhams. If silver is expensive and gold is cheap, and the good reaches twenty mithqal of gold but not two hundred dirhams of silver, then assess its value with mithqal, not with dirhams. The basis of this statement is precaution for the right of the poor and needy. That is, out of precaution with consideration for the poor, this will be done. The second statement mentioned in al-Mabsut is that the owner has the choice: if he wants, he may assess with dirhams, or with dinars. The evidence for this statement is that valuation is done to know the amount of value, and for this purpose dirhams and dinars are equal. Therefore, one will not be preferred over the other. The third statement is that of Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam al-Shafi'i also holds it: he says that this good should be assessed with the currency with which it was purchased. If it was purchased with dirhams, then assess with dirhams; if with dinars, then assess with dinars. And if it was purchased with something other than dirhams and dinars, then assess with the currency among dirhams and dinars that is more commonly used. The evidence for this statement is that knowledge of the value is greater with the currency with which the good was purchased, because once its value has been determined with that currency, there will be no difficulty in assessing it a second time. The fourth statement is that of Imam Muhammad: he says that in every case the valuation should be made with the dominant currency of the locality, i.e., among the two currencies, the one that is more commonly used. His evidence is that valuation for the right of Allah is analogized to valuation for the right of people. And in the rights of people, valuation is made with the dominant currency of the locality. For example, if someone usurps an object and it is lost in the possession of the usurper, and the object is among those that have value (dhat al-qima), then the usurper is liable for its value. And the valuation will be made with the currency among the two that is more commonly used. Similarly, if someone destroys another's good and it is among those that have value, the destroyer is liable for the value. And the valuation will be made with the currency that is more commonly used. Just as in the rights of people, valuations are made with the dominant currency, similarly for the rights of Allah, i.e., zakat etc., valuations will be made with the dominant currency.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents four scholarly opinions within the Hanafi school on how to assess the value of trade goods ('urud al-tijara) for the purpose of completing the zakat nisab when the goods are not themselves gold or silver. The opinions are: (1) The first view, attributed to the earlier scholars, is that the assessment should be made with whichever currency brings greater benefit to the poor recipients of zakat. This is based on precaution (ihtiyat) for their right. (2) The second view, narrated in al-Mabsut, gives the owner full choice between gold and silver. The reasoning is that both are equally valid for determining value. (3) Imam Abu Yusuf (and also Imam al-Shafi'i) holds that the assessment should be with the currency used to purchase the goods, as that provides more accurate knowledge. (4) Imam Muhammad holds that the dominant currency of the locality should be used, drawing an analogy (qiyas) to the rights of people (huquq al-'ibad) where the dominant currency is used for valuation. The passage explains each view briefly, then concludes that just as in civil matters (damages, usurpation) the dominant currency is used, similarly in the right of Allah (zakat) the dominant currency should be used. This suggests that Imam Muhammad's view is preferred or at least strongly considered.

Key Terms
نقد غالب (naqd ghalib): The dominant currency in circulation in a given locality
ذوات القیم (dhawat al-qim): Goods that have a market value but are not measured by weight or measure for currency (as opposed to ribawi items)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad (as presented in this passage), with which currency should the value of trade goods be assessed for zakat nisab?
A) The currency that benefits the poor
B) The currency with which the goods were purchased
C) The dominant currency of the locality
D) The owner's preference

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers multiple valid methods for zakat valuation, with the dominant local currency view (Imam Muhammad) being strongly supported by analogy to civil rights.

Nisab Continuity for Zakat: Beginning and End Only
Explains the ruling when nisab is complete at both ends but deficient in between

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for nisab continuity and explain why a mid-year deficiency does not cancel zakat, while distinguishing total loss from partial decrease.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, zakat requires nisab only at the start and end of the year; mid-year dips do not break the obligation.

Zakat obligation hinges on the nisab threshold, but what happens if your wealth dips below nisab mid-year? The Hanafi school, as articulated by al-Quduri and expanded in this passage, takes a pragmatic view: only the beginning and end of the lunar year matter. This lesson unpacks the rationale, the intra-Hanafi challenge from Imam Zufar, and the critical distinction between partial decrease and total loss.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from al-Quduri: complete nisab at beginning and end of the year is the condition; deficiency in between does not cancel zakat.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam Zufar requires nisab throughout the entire year, and Imam Shafi'i requires it for non-trade goods but exempts trade goods due to hardship.
Imam Zufar is the main intra-Hanafi opponent.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand that the opponent argues that 'nisab hawi' (nisab that completes a year) implies persistence throughout the year.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: requiring continuity is too difficult (mashaqqa); the beginning establishes the cause (sabab), the end triggers obligation (wujub), and the middle is a state of continuation (halat al-baqa).
Total loss (halaka al-kull) is different – it voids the cause.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if nisab drops mid-year, Hanafi still obliges zakat at year-end; Imams Zufar and Shafi'i (for non-trade) would not.
This affects real-world zakat calculations.

ہے اس لئے حوالان حول کی شرط نہیں پائی گئی ہے حالانکہ زکوۃ کا سبب منعقد ہونے کے بعد جولان حول شرط تھا اور مسئلہ اولی میں ایسا نہیں ہے یعنی جس صورت میں فقط نصاب میں کمی آئی ہے پورا نصاب ہلاک نہیں ہوا تو اس صورت میں چونکہ کچھ نہ کچھ نصاب باقی ہے اس لئے انعقاد سبب بھی باقی ہے اور جب انعقاد سبب باقی ہے تو زکوۃ بھی واجب ہے۔
When the nisab is complete at both ends of the year (beginning and end), then its deficiency in between does not cancel zakat, because it is difficult to consider completeness in the middle. As for the beginning, it is necessary for the inception and verification of wealth; and at the end for obligation; and not so in between because it is a state of continuation. Contrary to when everything perishes, where the ruling of the year becomes void and zakat is not due due to total absence of nisab. And not so in the first case because some nisab remains, so the inception remains. Translation: And when the nisab is complete at both ends of the year, then its decrease in between does not cancel zakat, because it is difficult to consider complete nisab during the year. Yes, at the beginning of the year its completeness is necessary so that the cause is established and wealth is realized. And at the end of the year (the nisab remaining complete) is necessary for obligation. And in between it is not so because it is a state of continuation. Contrary to when all wealth perishes, then the ruling of the year is void and zakat is not due because the nisab is completely absent. And in the first case it is not so because some nisab remains, so the inception remains. Explanation: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that for zakat to be obligatory, the condition is that complete nisab exists at the beginning and end of the year. A decrease in nisab during the year does not cancel zakat. That is, at the beginning of the year full nisab is present, and at the end also nisab is complete, but in between it decreased somewhat. In this case zakat remains obligatory, it is not cancelled. And Imam Zufar said that it is condition that complete nisab exists from beginning to end of the entire year; if at any time nisab decreases, zakat is not due. For grazing animals and for cash (gold and silver), Imam Shafi'i also holds this view. However, for other than these, he considers only the end of the year, i.e., complete nisab at the end of the year is a condition, not for the rest. Imam Zufar's evidence is that the cause of zakat obligation is nisab hawi (the nisab that completes a year), and this is dependent on nisab remaining throughout the year. So it is established that nisab remaining the whole year is a condition. The reason for Imam Shafi'i's statement is also this, but he excluded trade goods from this condition due to hardship, because trade goods fluctuate daily. So every day sitting and calculating its value and seeing whether nisab is complete is very difficult, even impossible. Therefore for trade goods he considers only the end of the year. Our evidence is that to consider nisab remaining complete during the year involves hardship, because wealth fluctuates. So the condition of nisab remaining complete in the middle is not set. As for the beginning and end, complete nisab at the beginning is so that the cause of zakat is established and wealth is realized; at the end so that obligation is realized. And in the middle, since neither matter applies, the condition of complete nisab is not set. In contrast to when all wealth perishes, then zakat is not due because at some point nisab is completely absent, so the condition of completion of the year is not found. And in the first case it is not so, i.e., when only a decrease occurs but not total loss, then because some nisab remains, the inception of the cause remains, so zakat is due.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage deals with the condition of nisab continuity throughout the zakat year. The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that only the beginning and end of the year matter: if nisab is complete at both points, any deficiency in between does not cancel zakat. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i (for non-trade goods) require nisab to be present the entire year. The Hanafi evidence is that requiring continuous nisab is difficult (mashaqqa) since wealth fluctuates. The beginning completeness is needed to initiate the cause (in'iqad sabab), and the end completeness is needed for obligation (wujub). The middle period is a state of continuity (halat al-baqa), so deficiency does not invalidate. However, if the entire nisab is lost (halaka al-kull), the cause is void and zakat is not due because no nisab remains at all. The distinction between partial decrease and total loss is key: partial decrease leaves the cause intact; total loss destroys it.

Key Terms
حولان حول (hawalan hawul): The completion of a full lunar year over the nisab
انعقاد سبب (in'iqad sabab): The establishment of the cause (sabab) of zakat at the start of the year

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Complete nisab at the beginning of the year
B) Complete nisab at the end of the year
C) Complete nisab throughout the entire year
D) Existence of some nisab at the time of obligation

Key Takeaway
For zakat in the Hanafi school, nisab is required only at the start and end of the lunar year; a mid-year dip does not cancel the obligation unless the entire nisab is lost.

Combining Trade Goods with Cash for Zakat Nisab
Ruling on combining trade goods with cash for nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that values of trade goods ('urud) are added to gold and silver to complete the nisab for zakat and explain the rationale based on trade intention.

Core Idea
Trade goods and cash are combined for zakat nisab because the obligation arises from the intent to trade.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi zakat law: when calculating the nisab threshold, the market values of trade goods ('urud) are combined with gold and silver currency. The short passage from the matn states this rule and provides the underlying rationale. Understanding this rule ensures that traders correctly assess their zakat liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'The value of goods is added to gold and silver so that the nisab is completed.' This is the explicit ruling.
2
Understand the condition
The ruling applies when one has both trade goods and gold/silver. The goods must be trade goods ('urud tijarah), not personal property.
3
Grasp the rationale (illa)
The reason given is 'because the obligation in all is based on trade' (bi i'tibar al-tijara). The unifying factor is the intention of trade, regardless of the physical nature or preparation of the assets.
This rationale allows combination even if some goods are for growth and others for custody.
4
Note the implication
The ruling implies that trade goods and cash are not treated separately for nisab. They are aggregated to determine if zakat is due.
This is distinct from other schools that may not combine across categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ تُصَمُّ قِيِّمَةُ الْعُرُوضِ إِلَى الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ حَتَّى يُتِمَّ النِّصَابُ لِأَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ فِي الْكُلِّ بِاعْتِبَارِ التِّجَارَةِ وَانِ افْتَرَقَتْ جِهَةُ الإِعْدَادِ ترجمہ اور سامان کی قیمت کو سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملایا جائے تا کہ نصاب پورا ہو کیونکہ ان سب میں وجوب زکوۃ تجارت کے اعتبار سے ہے اگر چہ نمو اور 10 کی، اوجدا ہے۔
He said: And the value of goods ('urud) is added to gold and silver so that the nisab is completed, because the obligation in all is based on trade, even if the aspect of preparation (growth or custody) differs. Translation: And the value of goods is combined with gold and silver so that the nisab becomes complete, because the obligation of zakat in all these is based on trade, even if growth and [...] are separate.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This short passage from the matn states a rule: when calculating zakat on trade goods, the values of different 'urud (commodities) are added together with gold and silver currency to reach the nisab threshold. The reason is that the obligation of zakat on all these items is due to their being for trade (bi i'tibar al-tijara), regardless of the different ways they are prepared for trade (some may be for growth, others for custody). This means that if a trader has a mix of cash and goods, their values are combined. The Urdu translation adds that this applies even if the goods are of different types (e.g., some for profit, some for storage). The passage emphasizes that the unifying factor is the intention of trade, not the nature of the goods themselves.

Key Terms
عروض ('urud): Trade goods and commodities other than gold and silver
ضم قيمة (damm qimah): Adding the monetary values of various assets together to form a single nisab

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the values of trade goods added to gold and silver for completing the zakat nisab?
A) Because all wealth must be combined
B) Because the obligation of zakat on all is based on trade
C) Because gold and silver are the standard
D) Because goods are less valuable

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi zakat, the values of trade goods and gold/silver are combined to reach nisab because the obligation of zakat on all is due to trade intention.

Condition of Nisab at Beginning and End of the Year for Zakat
Explaining Hanafi ruling on nisab condition at beginning and end of the year, with ikhtilaf of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the nisab condition for zakat and distinguish it from the views of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, justifying the reliance on istihsan.

Core Idea
For zakat, the Hanafi school requires nisab only at the beginning and end of the lunar year, not throughout.

Zakat is obligatory when wealth reaches the nisab threshold and a lunar year passes. But what if nisab fluctuates mid-year? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa and his two students, holds that nisab must be present at the start and end of the year; a temporary decrease does not break the obligation. This lesson examines the evidence and the opposing views of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State that nisab must be present at the beginning and end of the haul year; mid-year decrease does not cancel zakat obligation.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Examine the opposing position of Imam Zufar
Imam Zufar requires nisab throughout the entire year. Understand his evidence: the cause of obligation is nisab upon which a full year passes, so the nisab must exist for the entire duration.
He applies strict analogy (qiyas).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using istihsan
The Hanafi school argues that requiring continuous nisab monitoring creates hardship (haraj). Therefore, they adopt istihsan, considering only the beginning and end.
This is a clear example of preferring ease over strict analogy.
4
Compare with Imam al-Shafi'i's view
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with Imam Zufar for livestock and gold/silver, but exempts trade goods due to their fluctuating nature. Note how hardship justifies a relaxation.
The Shafi'i school uses a similar reasoning but narrower scope.
5
Distinguish total loss vs partial decrease
If all nisab is destroyed mid-year, the obligation lapses because the haul condition is broken. If only part is lost, the obligation remains because some nisab remains, preserving the cause.
This nuance is captured in the matn's wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكوة متحقق ہو جائے۔ اور انتہا ء سال میں زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے (نصاب کا پورا رہنا ضروری ہے ) اور اس کے مابین میں ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ حالت بقاء ہے برخلاف اس کے جب کل مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو سال کا حکم باطل ہو جائے گا ۔ اور زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ نصاب بالکلیہ معدوم ہو گیا اور پہلے مسئلہ میں ایسا نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کچھ نصاب باقی ہے تو انعقاد باقی رہا۔ تشریح شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے لئے سال کے اول اور آخر میں کامل نصاب کا ہونا شرط ہے درمیان سال میں نصاب کا کم ہو جانا ز کوۃ کو ساقط نہیں کرے گا یعنی سال کے اول میں بھی پورا نصاب موجود ہے اور آخر میں بھی نصاب پورا ہو گیا مگر درمیان میں کچھ کم ہو گیا تھا تو اس صورت میں زکوۃ واجب رہے گی ساقط نہ ہو گی اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ سال کے اول سے لے کر آخر تک پورے سال کامل نصاب کا موجود رہنا شرط ہے اگر کسی بھی حصہ میں نصاب کم ہو گیا تو زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ سائمہ جانوروں اور نقدین یعنی سونے اور چاندی کے اندر زکوۃ واجب ہونے میں امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ البتہ ان کے علاوہ میں فقط آخر سال کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں یعنی سال کے آخر میں کامل نصاب کا ہونا شرط ہے اس کے علاوہ میں شرط نہیں ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب نصاب حولی ہے یعنی وہ نصاب ہے جس پر حولان حول ہو جائے اور یہ فرع ہے پورے سال نصاب حولی کے باقی بنے کی پس ثابت ہوا کہ نصاب کا پورے سال باقی رہنا شرط ہے۔ امام شافعی کے قول کی وجہ بھی یہی ہے مگر انہوں نے مال تجارت کو اس شرط سے حرج کی وجہ سے خارج کر دیا ہے کیونکہ مال تجارت ہر روز گھٹتا بڑھتا رہتا ہے اب ہر روز بیٹھ کر اس کی قیمت لگانا اور یہ دیکھنا کہ پورا نصاب ہے یا نہیں بہت دشوار کام ہے بلکہ ایک گونہ ناممکن ہے اس لئے مال تجارت میں فقط آخر سال کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ درمیان سال میں نصاب پورا رہنے کا اعتبار کرنے میں مشقت ہے کیونکہ سال گھٹتا بڑھتا رہتا ہے اس لئے درمیان سال میں پورا نصاب رہنے کی شرط نہیں لگائی گئی ہے رہا ابتداء اور انتہاء کا معاملہ تو ابتداء اور انتہاء میں کامل نصاب کا ہونا شرط ہے ابتداء میں تو اس لئے تا کہ زکوۃ کا سبب منعقد ہو جائے اور غنی محقق ہو جائے اور انتہاء میں اس لئے تا کہ زکوۃ کا وجوب متحقق ہو جائے اور درمیان سال میں چونکہ دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں اس لئے درمیان سال میں نصاب کامل رہنے کی شرط نہیں لگائی ہے بخلاف مالو ملك الكل الخ سے متن کی عبارت فنقصانہ کی قید کا فائدہ ذرکیا گیا ہے یعنی درمیان سال میں نصاب کا کم ہو جانا ز کوۃ ساتھ نہیں کرتا البتہ اگر پورا نصاب ہلاک ہو گیا تو زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ سال کے ایک حصہ میں نصاب بالکل معدوم ہو گیا ہے اس لئے حوالان حول کی شرط نہیں پائی گئی ہے حالانکہ زکوۃ کا سبب منعقد ہونے کے بعد جولان حول شرط تھا اور مسئلہ اولی میں ایسا نہیں ہے یعنی جس صورت میں فقط نصاب میں کمی آئی ہے پورا نصاب ہلاک نہیں ہوا تو اس صورت میں چونکہ کچھ نہ کچھ نصاب باقی ہے اس لئے انعقاد سبب بھی باقی ہے اور جب انعقاد سبب باقی ہے تو زکوۃ بھی واجب ہے۔
The condition for zakat to be obligatory is that the nisab must remain complete at the end of the year. It is not required in the middle because that is a state of remaining, unlike the case when all wealth is destroyed, then the ruling of the year becomes void and zakat is not obligatory because the nisab is completely eliminated. In the first case, it is not so because some nisab remains, so the obligation remains. Explanation: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: For zakat to be obligatory, it is a condition that complete nisab exists at the beginning and end of the year. A decrease in nisab during the middle does not cancel zakat. That is, if at the beginning there was complete nisab and at the end it is complete, but during the middle it decreased, then zakat remains obligatory and is not cancelled. Imam Zufar said: It is a condition that complete nisab remains throughout the entire year. If at any point it decreases, zakat is not obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i also holds this view for sa'imah animals and gold and silver. However, for other than these, he only considers the end of the year. Imam Zufar's evidence is that the cause of zakat obligation is nisab upon which a year passes, and this is a branch of nisab remaining throughout the year. Therefore, nisab remaining throughout the year is a condition. Imam al-Shafi'i's reason is also this, but he excluded trade goods due to hardship because trade goods fluctuate daily, making it difficult to assess nisab daily. So for trade goods, only the end of the year is considered. Our evidence is that requiring nisab to remain complete throughout the year involves hardship because the year fluctuates. Therefore, the condition of complete nisab during the middle has not been imposed. As for the beginning and end, complete nisab is a condition: at the beginning so that the cause of zakat is established and the person is verified as wealthy; at the end so that the obligation of zakat is actualized. Since neither occurs in the middle, the condition of complete nisab during the middle has not been imposed. The benefit of the restriction 'decrease' in the text of the matn is that a decrease in the middle does not cancel zakat. However, if the entire nisab is destroyed, then zakat is not obligatory because in a part of the year the nisab is completely absent, so the condition of the passing of the year is not fulfilled. In the first case (mere decrease), it is not so, because some nisab remains, so the establishment of the cause remains, and zakat is obligatory.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses the condition of nisab over the course of the zakat year. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that nisab must be present at the beginning and end of the haul year. A mid-year decrease does not nullify the obligation. The author contrasts this with the view of Imam Zufar, who requires nisab throughout the entire year. Imam al-Shafi'i adopts Imam Zufar's view for livestock and gold/silver but exempts trade goods due to hardship. The Hanafi proof is based on istihsan: requiring continuous nisab monitoring would cause undue hardship. Therefore, only the two endpoints matter. Additionally, if the entire nisab is destroyed mid-year, the obligation lapses because the haul condition is broken. However, if only part is lost and later restored, zakat remains due.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth upon which zakat is obligatory.
حولان حول (hawalan al-hawl): The passing of one lunar year over the nisab.
سائمہ (sa'imah): Livestock that graze freely for most of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on nisab during the zakat year for zakat to be wajib?
A) Nisab must be present throughout the entire year.
B) Nisab must be present at the beginning and end of the year only.
C) Nisab must be present only at the end of the year.
D) Nisab must be present at the beginning of the year only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires nisab only at the beginning and end of the zakat year, relying on istihsan to avoid hardship.

Combining Trade Goods with Gold and Silver to Complete Nisab
Ruling with proof via ijma and illa of nama'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that trade goods are combined with gold/silver by value to determine zakat nisab, and explain the basis in ijma and the illa of nama'.

Core Idea
Trade goods and gold/silver share the essence of growth (nama'), so their values combine to complete nisab.

This lesson explains a key Hanafi ruling that trade goods are valued and combined with gold or silver to reach the zakat threshold. While the mode of growth differs—human effort versus divine design—the essential attribute of growth justifies combination. The ruling is established by consensus and is fundamental for merchants and investors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that the value of trade goods is added to gold and silver so that the nisab is completed. This is the core ruling: combination by value.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is ijma (consensus of scholars). The text says 'Yah hukm bil-ijma' (this ruling is by consensus).
Ijma is a qat'i source of law.
3
Trace the illa
The underlying cause (illa) that allows combination is the attribute of growth (nama'), which is present in both trade goods and gold/silver, even though the source of growth differs.
In trade goods, growth comes from human effort; in gold/silver, it is inherent by divine creation.
4
Apply to an example
Work through the examples in the text: if one has 50 dirhams of silver and trade goods worth 150 dirhams, zakat is due on the total 200 dirhams.
Always use current market value for goods.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is mutaffaq alayh (unanimously agreed upon) among all schools of thought.
No significant ikhtilaf exists on this principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سامان کی قیمت سونے اور چاندی کیسا تھ نصاب مکمل کرنے کے لئے ملائی جائے گی قَالَ وَ تُصَمُّ قِيِّمَةُ الْعُرُوضِ إِلَى الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ حَتَّى يُتِمَّ النِّصَابُ لِأَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ فِي الْكُلِّ بِاعْتِبَارِ التِّجَارَةِ وَانِ افْتَرَقَتْ جِهَةُ الإِعْدَادِ ترجمہ اور سامان کی قیمت کو سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملایا جائے تا کہ نصاب پورا ہو کیونکہ ان سب میں وجوب زکوۃ تجارت کے اعتبار سے ہے اگر چہ نمو اور 10 کی، اوجدا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کی ملک میں سامان تجارت بقدر نصاب نہ ہو البتہ اس کے پاس کچھ سونا یا چاندی ہے تو نصاب پورا کرنے کے لئے سامان تجارت کی قیمت کو سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملا دیا جائے گا مثلا کسی کے پاس پچاس درہم ہوں اور ایک سو پچاس درہم کی مالیت کا سامان تجارت ہو تو اس پر دو سو درہم چاندی کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ یا مثلا کسی کے پاس آٹھ مثقال سونا ہے اور بارہ مثقال کی مالیت کا سامان تجارت ہے تو اس پر نہیں مثقال سونے کی زکوۃ واجب ہو جائے گی یہ حکم بالا جماع ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہر چیز کے اندر زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب نصاب نامی کا مالک ہونا ہے اور نماء سامان تجارت میں بھی موجود ہے اور سونے اور چاندی میں بھی اگر چہ نما ء کی جہت مختلف ہے یعنی سامان تجارت میں بندوں کی جانب سے نما متحقق ہوتا ہے کیونکہ بندوں نے اس کو تجارت کے لئے مہیا کیا ہے اور سونے اور چاندی میں نماء من جانب اللہ پایا جاتا ہے کیونکہ خدا نے ان دونوں کو پیدا ہی تجارت کے لئے کیا ہے جب اصل یعنی نما ، دونوں جگہ موجود ہے تو سامان تجارت کی قیمت کو سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملا کر ز کو ۃ واجب کر دی جائے گی۔
The value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver so that the nisab is completed. Because the obligation (of zakat) in all of them is by consideration of trade, even if the mode of growth differs. Translation: And the value of goods is combined with gold and silver so that the nisab is completed, because the obligation of zakat in all is by consideration of trade, even if the mode of growth differs. Explanation: The issue is that if someone does not possess trade goods to the extent of nisab, but has some gold or silver, then the value of the trade goods is added to the gold and silver to complete the nisab. For example, if someone has fifty dirhams and trade goods worth one hundred fifty dirhams, then zakat on two hundred dirhams of silver is due. Or if someone has eight mithqals of gold and trade goods worth twelve mithqals, then zakat on twenty mithqals of gold is due. This ruling is by consensus. The evidence is that the cause of zakat obligation in everything is ownership of productive nisab, and growth is present in trade goods as well as in gold and silver, even though the source of growth differs. In trade goods, growth occurs from the efforts of servants because they prepare them for trade, while in gold and silver, growth comes from Allah because He created them for trade. Since the essence of growth is present in both, the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver and zakat is made obligatory.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage explains how trade goods (urud al-tijarah) are combined with gold or silver to reach the nisab threshold. The text states that the value of the goods is added to the gold or silver. For example, if one has less than nisab in gold but has trade goods whose value completes the nisab, zakat becomes wajib. This is by consensus (ijma). The underlying illa is that both possess the quality of growth (nama'), even though the mechanism differs. Trade goods grow through human effort (kasb), while gold and silver grow inherently (by divine design). Since the essential cause is ownership of growth-capable nisab, they are combined.

Key Terms
عروض (urud): Trade goods or commodities other than gold, silver, and livestock.
قیمت (qimah): Monetary value, used here to combine trade goods with gold/silver.
نماء (nama'): Growth or increase, the attribute that makes wealth subject to zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By weight of the goods.
B) By value of the goods.
C) By quantity of items.
D) They are not combined at all.

Key Takeaway
Trade goods and gold/silver are combined by value to complete nisab because they share the attribute of growth (nama'), as established by consensus.

Combining Gold and Silver for Zakat Nisab: Hanafi Ikhtilaf and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on combining gold and silver for zakat nisab with ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams and with Imam Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on combining gold and silver for zakat nisab, distinguish between the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (value vs weight), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Gold and silver combine for zakat via shared thamaniyyah; Hanafi dispute is over value vs weight.

This passage addresses a key zakat question: can gold and silver be combined to reach the nisab? The Hanafi school says yes, based on their shared attribute of being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah). However, there is a disagreement among the Hanafi imams themselves on how to combine—by value or by weight—and a more fundamental disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who rejects combination entirely. Understanding these layers of ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply zakat rulings in complex cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
Recognize that the passage addresses combining gold and silver to complete the nisab for zakat. The Hanafi school holds that they are combined because of homogeneity (mujanasah) in thamaniyyah.
The term 'thamaniyyah' is central.
2
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa combines by value (qimah); the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) combine by weight (ajza'). There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa agreeing with them.
The practical difference: a person with gold and silver each below nisab may or may not owe zakat depending on which method is used.
3
Identify the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i does not combine gold and silver at all, considering them different species. The Hanafi response rests on the common attribute of being a medium of exchange.
Imam Malik agrees with the Hanafi position.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the Hanafi school (mufta bihi: Abu Hanifa's value-based combination), zakat becomes wajib if the combined value reaches nisab. Under the Shafi'i school, no zakat is due unless each metal alone reaches its respective nisab.
This affects many zakat calculations in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ يُضَمُّ الذَّهَبُ إِلَى الْفِضَّةِ لِلمُجَانِسَةٍ مِنْ حَيْثُ الثَّمَنَيَّةِ وَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ صَارَ سَبًا ثُمَّ تُضَمُّ بِالْقِيِّمَةِ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا بِالْأَجْزَاءِ وَهُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْهُ حَتَّى أَنَّ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ مِائَةُ دِرْهَم وَ خَمْسَةٌ مَثَاقِيل ذَهَبَ وَتَبْلُغُ قِيمَتَهَا مِائَةَ دِرْهَم فَعَلَيْهِ الزَّكوةُ عِنْدَهُ خِلَافًا لَّهُمَا هُمَا يَقُولَانِ الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِيهِمَا الْقَدْرُ دُونَ الْقِيْمَةِ حَتَّى لَا تَحِبُّ الزَّكوة فِي مَصْنُوعِ وَزُنَهُ اقَلَ مِنْ مِائَتَيْنِ وَقِيمَهُ فَوْقَهَا هُوَ يَقُولُ إِنَّ الصَّمَ لِلْمُجَانِسَةِ وَهُوَ يَتَحَقَّقِ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْقِيِّمَةِ دُونَ الصُّورَةِ فَيُضَةٌ بِهَا وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ
And gold is combined with silver due to homogeneity in terms of being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah), and from this aspect it becomes a cause. Then, according to Abu Hanifa, it is combined by value, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) by weight, and this is also a narration from him. So that if someone has one hundred dirhams and five mithqals of gold, and the value of the five mithqals reaches one hundred dirhams, then according to him zakat is obligatory, contrary to them. They say: The consideration in them is the quantity, not the value. Thus, zakat is not obligatory on a manufactured item whose weight is less than two hundred (dirhams) and whose value is above it. He says: The combination is due to homogeneity, and that is realized by value, not by form, so it is combined by it. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage covers two levels of disagreement. First, among the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa holds that when combining gold and silver, the criterion is value (qimah), so if one has gold worth less than nisab and silver worth less than nisab, but their combined value equals nisab, zakat is wajib. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the criterion is weight (ajza'), so only actual weights are combined, not values. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa agreeing with them. The second dispute is with Imam al-Shafi'i, who entirely denies combining gold and silver, considering them different species. The Hanafi-Maliki position is that the common attribute of being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah) unites them for zakat purposes. The practical consequence: under the Hanafi school, a person with partial amounts of both pays zakat if combined value reaches nisab; under the Shafi'i school, no zakat is due unless either metal alone reaches its respective nisab.

Key Terms
ضم (damm): The act of combining different types of wealth to complete the nisab for zakat.
مجانسة (mujanasah): Homogeneity in terms of being a medium of exchange.
ثمينيت (thamaniyyah): The quality of being a medium of exchange or monetary value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, how are gold and silver combined to complete the nisab for zakat?
A) By weight (ajza')
B) By value (qimah)
C) They are not combined
D) By number of coins

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school combines gold and silver for zakat nisab based on shared thamaniyyah, with the mufta bihi position being combination by value.
