Combining Trade Goods with Gold and Silver for Nisab
Ruling and proof for combining trade goods with gold/silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on combining trade goods with gold/silver to complete nisab for zakat and identify the cause (sabab) that justifies this combination.

Core Idea
Trade goods combine with gold/silver for zakat nisab because all share the essential cause of growth (nama).

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a person possesses trade goods insufficient to reach nisab but also owns some gold or silver. Can the two be combined? The Hanafi school answers yes, and the proof rests on identifying the common sabab (cause) of zakat obligation: ownership of a growing nisab. Understanding this principle clarifies why zakat applies across diverse wealth types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the scenario: someone has trade goods below nisab but also has gold or silver. The ruling states that the value of trade goods is added to the gold/silver to complete nisab, making zakat wajib on the total.
The ruling is 'by consensus' within the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the cause (sabab) as stated in the proof
The text states the cause: 'ownership of a growing nisab' (nisab nami). This is the underlying reason for zakat obligation.
Growth (nama) is the essential element.
3
Analyze how the cause applies to both types of wealth
The author argues that growth exists in trade goods (through human trade effort) and in gold/silver (divinely ordained as mediums of exchange). Since the cause is common, combining is valid.
Different sources of growth do not negate the common cause.
4
Note the examples and their numerical illustrations
Two examples are given: silver dirhams + trade goods, and gold mithqals + trade goods. Work through the math to see how the combination works.
The examples show that the value of trade goods is added to the precious metal.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
This is a Hanafi position. The Shafi'i school does not combine these categories. Understand that the difference stems from different definitions of the cause for zakat.
The subsequent lesson may cover the Shafi'i view.

Source Text

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کی ملک میں سامان تجارت بقدر نصاب نہ ہو البتہ اس کے پاس کچھ سونا یا چاندی ہے تو نصاب پورا کرنے کے لئے سامان تجارت کی قیمت کو سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملا دیا جائے گا مثلا کسی کے پاس پچاس درہم ہوں اور ایک سو پچاس درہم کی مالیت کا سامان تجارت ہو تو اس پر دو سو درہم چاندی کی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ یا مثلا کسی کے پاس آٹھ مثقال سونا ہے اور بیس مثقال کی مالیت کا سامان تجارت ہے تو اس پر بیس مثقال سونے کی زکوۃ واجب ہو جائے گی یہ حکم بالا جماع ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہر چیز کے اندر زکوۃ واجب ہونے کا سبب نصاب نامی کا مالک ہونا ہے اور نماء سامان تجارت میں بھی موجود ہے اور سونے اور چاندی میں بھی اگر چہ نما ء کی جہت مختلف ہے یعنی سامان تجارت میں بندوں کی جانب سے نما متحقق ہوتا ہے کیونکہ بندوں نے اس کو تجارت کے لئے مہیا کیا ہے اور سونے اور چاندی میں نماء من جانب اللہ پایا جاتا ہے کیونکہ خدا نے ان دونوں کو پیدا ہی تجارت کے لئے کیا ہے جب اصل یعنی نما ، دونوں جگہ موجود ہے تو سامان تجارت کی قیمت کو سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ ملا کر ز کو ۃ واجب کر دی جائے گی۔
Explanation of the issue: If someone owns trade goods not reaching the nisab, but he has some gold or silver, then to complete the nisab, the value of the trade goods will be added to the gold or silver. For example: someone has fifty dirhams and trade goods worth one hundred fifty dirhams, then zakat of two hundred dirhams of silver is obligatory. Or for example: someone has eight mithqal of gold and trade goods worth twelve mithqal, then zakat of twenty mithqal of gold becomes obligatory. This ruling is by consensus. The proof is that the cause for the obligation of zakat in everything is ownership of a growing nisab, and growth exists in trade goods and also in gold and silver, although the direction of growth differs: in trade goods growth is realized from the servants' side because they prepared it for trade, and in gold and silver growth is found from Allah's side because Allah created them for trade. When the essence, that is growth, exists in both places, then the value of trade goods is combined with gold and silver and zakat is made obligatory.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling combined with its proof (dalil) regarding the combination of trade goods (urud al-tijarah) with gold and silver to complete the nisab for zakat. The author states that if someone does not possess a complete nisab of trade goods but has some gold or silver, the value of the trade goods is added to the gold or silver to complete the nisab. This ruling is based on consensus (ijma) of the Hanafi school. The proof is that the cause (sabab) for the obligation of zakat is ownership of a growing nisab (nisab nami). Growth (nama) is present in both trade goods (through human effort in trade) and in gold and silver (through divine intent as they are inherently medium of exchange). Since the cause is present in both, they can be combined. Note that this is a Hanafi ruling, and the proof relies on the common cause of growth, not on the specific form of wealth. The examples clarify the method: the value of trade goods is added to the gold or silver at the time of zakat calculation.

Key Terms
نصاب نامی (nisāb nāmī): A nisab that has the potential for growth (nama), either through trade or natural increase.
نماء (namā’): Growth or increase; the quality that makes wealth zakatable. In trade goods it comes from human effort, in gold/silver from divine intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Prophet ﷺ explicitly commanded it.
D) Because trade goods are more valuable than gold.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, trade goods combine with gold/silver for nisab because the essential cause of zakat—ownership of a growing nisab—is present in both.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Combining Gold and Silver by Value vs Weight
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining gold and silver for zakat nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining gold and silver, explain each position's proof, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a concrete case.

Core Idea
Gold and silver are combined for zakat, but Abu Hanifa combines by value while Sahibayn combine by weight.

In zakat, gold and silver can be combined to complete the nisab. However, the method of combination is disputed within the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn), their proofs, and the practical consequence of their difference.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed premise
The basis for combining gold and silver is thamaniyyah (being a medium of exchange). This is agreed upon.
The text says 'gold is combined with silver due to the similarity in being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah).'
2
Identify the point of dispute
Abu Hanifa says combination is by value (qiymah), while Sahibayn say it is by weight (ajza'). There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa supporting weight.
The text states: 'according to Abu Hanifa, combination is by value, and according to them (Sahibayn) it is by weight, and this is also a narration from him.'
3
Examine the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa: thamaniyyah is value-based, so combination should be by value. Sahibayn: in zakat on gold and silver, weight is the standard (e.g., manufactured vessels – no zakat if weight < nisab even if value high).
Abu Hanifa responds that the weight standard applies to individual categories, but for combination, value is considered.
4
Apply the dispute to a concrete example
Consider a person with 100 dirhams of silver and 5 mithqal of gold worth 100 dirhams. Abu Hanifa: combined value = 200 dirhams → zakat wajib. Sahibayn: silver weight = 100 dirhams (<200), gold weight = 5 mithqal (<20) → no zakat.
This example is directly from the source text.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school gives preference to Abu Hanifa's view; fatwa is on combination by value.
Later Hanafi masters (e.g., al-Marghinani) prefer Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text

And gold is combined with silver due to the similarity (mujānasah) in terms of being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah), and from this aspect it became a cause. Then, according to Abu Hanifa, combination is by value, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is by weight, and this is also a narration from him. So much so that a person who has one hundred dirhams and five mithqal of gold, and the value of the gold reaches one hundred dirhams, then zakat is obligatory according to him, contrary to them. They say that in them the weight is considered, not the value, so much so that zakat is not obligatory in a manufactured vessel whose weight is less than two hundred dirhams and its value is above that. The Sahibayn say that in gold and silver, weight is considered, not value, so much so that zakat is not obligatory on a manufactured vessel whose weight is less than two hundred dirhams and its value is more than two hundred. Abu Hanifa says that combination is because of similarity (mujānasah), and it is realized by consideration of value, not form; so it will be combined by that value. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the method of combining gold and silver for zakat. The passage begins by quoting the original text from the Hidayah: 'Gold is combined with silver due to the similarity in being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah).' Then it explains the difference: Abu Hanifa says the combination is by value (qiymah), while the Sahibayn say it is by weight (ajza'). There is also a narration that Abu Hanifa himself sometimes favored weight. The practical consequence (thamar) is illustrated: if someone has 100 dirhams of silver and 5 mithqal of gold worth 100 dirhams, then according to Abu Hanifa the total value is 200 dirhams, so zakat is wajib; according to the Sahibayn, the weight of silver is only 100 dirhams (below 200) and gold 5 mithqal (below 20), so no zakat is due. The Sahibayn's proof is that in zakat on gold and silver, weight is the standard (as seen in manufactured vessels: if weight < 200 dirhams, no zakat even if value is high). Abu Hanifa's proof is that the cause of combination is similarity in being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah), which is based on value, not form/weight. Therefore, value is the basis for combining. The Hanafi school generally follows Abu Hanifa's view on this, though later fatwa may consider both.

Key Terms
ضم (ḍamm): Combining two types of wealth for the purpose of completing the nisab for zakat.
ثمنیت (thamaniyyah): The quality of being a medium of exchange (thaman). This is the basis for combining gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) By volume

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school combines gold and silver for zakat nisab, but the method differs: Abu Hanifa uses value, Sahibayn use weight; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Combining Gold and Silver for Zakat: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi/Maliki vs Shafi'i on combining gold and silver for zakat, plus intra-Hanafi dispute on method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on combining gold and silver for zakat, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the intra-Hanafi rules on value vs weight.

Core Idea
Gold and silver share thamaniyyah, uniting them for zakat; Hanafis combine by value, Shafi'is do not combine.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on whether gold and silver can be combined to complete the nisab for zakat. The Hanafi and Maliki schools permit combination based on the common cause of thamaniyyah (medium of exchange), while the Shafi'i school treats them as separate species. The text also explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether combination is by value or by weight. Understanding this dispute clarifies both the operative cause (illah) of zakat on currencies and the method of calculation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the issue: gold and silver separately below nisab but together reach nisab. State that Hanafis (and Malikis) combine them to make zakat wajib.
The key is that neither alone reaches nisab, but combined they do.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i opposition
State the Shafi'i view: no combination because gold and silver are different species (jins). Understand their proof: permissible disparity in exchange (riba would apply if same species).
The analogy with camels and goats is used.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
Identify the Hanafi reply: unity in thamaniyyah trumps difference in essence. The cause (illah) of zakat on gold and silver is thamaniyyah, common to both. Also, the practice of the Companions (maḍat al-sunnah) supports combination.
The narration of Hubayr ibn Abdullah is cited as evidence.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa says combination by value; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say by weight. Understand the proof of each side.
The example of a silver vessel shows weight is considered for nisab (Sahibayn). Abu Hanifa argues combination is due to similarity in thamaniyyah, which is value-based.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the different views to the example: 100 dirhams silver + 5 mithqal gold worth 100 dirhams. Abu Hanifa: zakat wajib (by value). Sahibayn: no zakat (by weight). Also note the agreed cases (bilā ittifāq) when portions are clear.
The 'fruit of difference' (thamarah al-khilaf) is crucial for muftis.

اختلاف کا ہونا تو ظاہر ہے اور علما اختلاف جنس اس لئے ہے کہ سونے اور چاندی میں سے ایک کا دوسرے کے تونل متفاضل پینا جائز ہے حتی کہ ایک سو گرام سونا اگر دوسو گرام چاندی کے عوض فروخت کر دیا گیا تو جائز ہے جانوروں میں ضم نہیں کیا جاتا مثلاً اگر کسی کے پاس اونٹ بھی ہیں اور بکریاں بھی اور نصاب کسی کا پورا نہیں ہے تو چونکہ اونٹ اور بکریوں میں اختلاف جنس ہے اس لئے زکوۃ واجب کرنے کے لئے ان میں سے ایک دوسرے کے ساتھ نہیں ملایا جاتا، پس اسی طرح سونے اور چاندی کو بھی نہیں ملایا جائے گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ سونے اور چاندی میں ذات کے اعتبار سے اگر چہ اتحاد نہیں ہے مگر وصف شمنیت کے اعتبار سے اتحاد ہے۔ اور وصف شمنیت ہی وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب ہے۔ پس جب وجوب زکوۃ کے سبب یعنی وصف ثمنیت میں اتحاد ہے تو گویا دونوں ثمنیت کے اعتبار سے ہم جنس ہیں اور جب دونوں ہم جنس ہیں تو زکوۃ واجب کرنے کے لئے ایک کا دوسرے کے ساتھ ملانا بھی واجب ہوگا ہماری تائید بگیر بن عبداللہ بن الا شبح کی روایت سے بھی ہوتی ہے روایت یہ ہے مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي ضَمِّ الذَّهَبِ إِلَى الْفِضَّةِ وَالْفِضَّةِ إِلَى الذَّهَبِ فِي إِحْرَاجِ الزَّكوة یعنی زکوۃ نکالنے کے سلسلہ میں اصحاب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ طریقہ رہا ہے کہ وہ سونے کو چاندی کے ساتھ اور چاندی کو سونے کے ساتھ ملایا کرتے تھے اب رہی یہ بات کہ یہ ملانا قیمت کے اعتبار سے ہوگا یا اجزاء کے اعتبار سے تو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قیمت کے اعتبار سے ہو گا یہی ایک روایت امام احمد کی ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اجزاء کے اعتبار سے ہوگا یہی ایک روایت امام ابوحنیفہ کی ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام مالک ہیں اور یہی ایک روایت امام احمد کی ہے۔ اختلاف کا ثمرہ اس مثال میں ظاہر ہو گا کہ ایک شخص کے پاس ایک سو درہم چاندی ہے اور پانچ مثقال سونا ہے اور پانچ مثقال سونے کی قیمت ایک سو درہم کو پہنچ جاتی ہے تو اس صورت میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک زکوۃ واجب ہو جائے گی کیونکہ قیمت کے اعتبار سے نصاب پورا ہو گیا ہے اور اجزاء کے اعتبار سے چونکہ نصاب پورا نہیں ہوا اس لئے صاحبین کے نزدیک زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر کسی کے پاس دس مثقال سونا ہو اور ایک سو درہم چاندی ہو، یا ان دونوں میں ایک ایک تہائی ہو اور دوسرا دو تہائی ہو یا ایک ایک چوتھائی اور دوسرا تین چوتھائی ہو تو ان صورتوں میں بالا تفاق ضم کر کے زکوۃ واجب کر دی جائے گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سونے اور چاندی میں وزن معتبر ہے نہ کہ قیمت حتی کہ اگر کسی کے پاس چاندی کا کوئی برتن یا زیور ہواور اس کا وزن دو سو درہم سے کم ہو لیکن اس کی قیمت دو سو درہم سے بھی بڑھ جاتی ہو تو اس میں بالا تفاق زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعتبار وزن کا ہے نہ کہ قیمت کا لہذا وزن کے اعتبار سے اگر نصاب پورا ہو گیا تو زکو د واجب ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ضم کرنا ہم جنس ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے، اور ہم جنس ہونا قیمت کے اعتبار سے متحقق ہوتا ہے نہ کہ صورت کے اعتبار سے لہذاضم قیمت ہی کے اعتبار سے ہوگا نہ کہ صورت کے اعتبار سے اور اجزاء کا اعتبار چونکہ صورت کا اعتبار ہے اس لئے صورت کے اعتبار سے ضم کا نہ ہونا گویا اجزاء کے اعتبار سے ضم کا نہ ہونا ہے، پس ثابت ہو گیا کہضم کے لئے اجزاء کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا بلکہ قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Explanation of the case: If someone has neither a complete nisab of gold nor a complete nisab of silver, but both together amount to one nisab, then in this case according to the Hanafi scholars and Imam Malik, one will be combined with the other and zakat will be made obligatory, provided that both together reach the amount of nisab. Imam Shafi'i said that gold and silver will not be combined with each other. And when they are not combined, then due to neither of them completing the nisab, zakat will not be obligatory. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that gold and silver are two different species, both in reality and in legal consideration, just as camels and goats are two different species. The difference in species is apparent, and the reason for the difference in species is that it is permissible to give one of gold and silver in exchange for the other with disparity, so much so that if one hundred grams of gold is sold for two hundred grams of silver, it is permissible. So if there were unity of species, then sale with disparity would not be permissible. Therefore, since there is a difference in species between gold and silver, one will not be combined with the other, just as in different species of grazing animals combination is not done. For example, if someone has both camels and goats, and neither's nisab is complete, then because of the difference in species between camels and goats, one is not combined with the other for zakat. Similarly, gold and silver will not be combined. Our proof is that although in essence there is no unity between gold and silver, there is unity in the quality of being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah). And the quality of thamaniyyah is the cause for the obligation of zakat. So when there is unity in the cause of zakat obligation, that is, the quality of thamaniyyah, then the two are like one species in terms of thamaniyyah. And when they are one species, then combining one with the other to make zakat wajib is also obligatory. Our support also comes from the tradition of Hubayr ibn Abdullah ibn al-Ashajj: 'The practice of the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) continues in combining gold with silver and silver with gold in the payment of zakat.' That is, in the matter of extracting zakat, the practice of the Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was that they would combine gold with silver and silver with gold. Now, regarding whether this combination is by value or by weight, there is a difference of opinion. Accordingly, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it will be by value, and this is one narration from Imam Ahmad. According to the Sahibayn it will be by weight, and this is one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, and Imam Malik holds this view, and this is also one narration from Imam Ahmad. The fruit of the difference becomes apparent in this example: a person has one hundred dirhams of silver and five mithqal of gold, and the value of the five mithqal reaches one hundred dirhams. In this case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, zakat becomes wajib because by value the nisab is complete; but by weight, since the nisab is not complete, the Sahibayn say zakat is not wajib. And if someone has ten mithqal of gold and one hundred dirhams of silver, or if one is one-third and the other two-thirds, or one is one-fourth and the other three-fourths, then in these cases by agreement (bilā ittifāq) zakat is made wajib by combining. The proof of the Sahibayn is that weight is considered in gold and silver, not value, so much so that if someone has a vessel or ornament of silver whose weight is less than two hundred dirhams but its value exceeds two hundred dirhams, then by consensus (bilā ittifāq) zakat is not obligatory. This shows that weight is considered, not value. Therefore, if by weight the nisab is complete, zakat is wajib; otherwise not. Imam Abu Hanifa says that combination is due to similarity (mujānasah), and similarity is realized by consideration of value, not form. Hence combination will be by value, not by form. And consideration of weight is consideration of form, thus combination by form does not occur. So it is established that for combination, weight is not considered, but value is considered. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents a comprehensive inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of combining gold and silver for zakat. It begins by stating the issue: if someone has incomplete nisab of both gold and silver, but together they reach the nisab, then the Hanafi and Maliki schools combine them to make zakat wajib, while Imam Shafi'i refuses to combine them. The Shafi'i proof is based on the difference in species (jins): gold and silver are different species, just as camels and goats are different. The evidence is that it is permissible to exchange gold for silver with disparity in weight, which would be riba if they were the same species. Since disparity is allowed, they are different species, and therefore cannot be combined for zakat, just as camels and goats are not combined. The Hanafi response (and Maliki) is that although they differ in essence (dhat), they share the quality of being a medium of exchange (thamaniyyah), which is the cause (sabab) for zakat obligation. Since the cause is common, they are considered one species for zakat purposes, and hence combination is valid. The Hanafi proof is further supported by the practice of the Companions (رضي الله عنهم) who combined gold and silver in zakat, as narrated by Hubayr ibn Abdullah. After establishing the permissibility of combination, the text revisits the intra-Hanafi dispute on the method: by value (Abu Hanifa) or by weight (Sahibayn). It also mentions the views of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. The practical consequence (thamar) is illustrated: with 100 dirhams silver and 5 mithqal gold worth 100 dirhams, Abu Hanifa says zakat wajib (by value), Sahibayn say no zakat (by weight). The Sahibayn's proof is based on the principle that weight is the standard for gold and silver zakat, as seen in the case of a silver vessel: if weight<200, no zakat even if value is high. Abu Hanifa's response is that combination is based on similarity in thamaniyyah, which is value-based, not form/weight-based. The passage concludes that value is the correct basis for combination.

Key Terms
ثمنیت (thamaniyyah): The quality of being a medium of exchange. The Hanafis argue this is the cause for zakat and is common to gold and silver.
مضت السنة (maḍat al-sunnah): The established practice (of the Companions). Used as a proof for combining gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa), how are gold and silver combined to reach the nisab for zakat?
A) By weight, because weight is the standard for zakat on metals.
B) By value, because they share the quality of thamaniyyah.
C) By count, because each unit counts separately.
D) They are never combined; each must reach nisab alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school combines gold and silver for zakat by value due to their common thamaniyyah, while the Shafi'i school does not combine them because they are different species.
